Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
Reciting Aloud or Silently in the Last Two Rak'ahs: The Correct Hanafi Position
Intra-Hanafi analysis on jahr/ikhfa' recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why reciting both Fatiha and surah aloud is the correct Hanafi view when making up a missed surah in the last two rak'ahs, and rebut the opposing intra-Hanafi views.

Core Idea
Recite both Fatiha and surah aloud to avoid making the wajib subordinate to the sunnah and to prevent mixing jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah.

This lesson addresses the second dimension of the intra-Hanafi dispute: how to recite when making up a missed surah in the last two rak'ahs. Three riwayat exist, each with a different combination of jahr (audible) and ikhfa' (silent) for Fatiha and the surah. We will analyse the reasoning of each and identify the correct view (al-sahih).

Guided Path
1
State the three riwayat on jahr/ikhfa'
Identify each riwayah: (1) Ibn Sa'id from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: jahr only for the surah, ikhfa' for Fatiha. (2) Hisham from Muhammad: no jahr at all, both silently. (3) The correct view: jahr for both Fatiha and the surah.
The text explicitly labels the third as 'هو الصحيح' (it is correct).
2
Analyse Hisham's reasoning (both silent)
Hisham argues that combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah is blameworthy. Since Fatiha is the original and should be silent in the last two, the surah, being subordinate, should also be silent to avoid mixing attributes.
This view prioritises the attribute of Fatiha (ikhfa') over the attribute of the surah (jahr).
3
Analyse Ibn Sa'id's reasoning (only surah jahr)
Ibn Sa'id distinguishes between ada' (actual performance) of Fatiha and qada' (make-up) of the surah. Ada' follows its place (ikhfa' for Fatiha), while qada' follows how it was missed (jahr for surah). The objection of mixing is answered by noting that qada' is attributed to the first rak'ahs, so no actual combination occurs.
This view results in combining jahr and ikhfa' in the same rak'ah, which Hisham criticised.
4
Understand the tarjih for the correct view (both jahr)
The correct view avoids both previous objections. By reciting both aloud, there is no combination of jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah. Moreover, it prevents making the stronger (wajib surah's jahr) subordinate to the weaker (sunnah Fatiha's ikhfa'), as would occur in Hisham's view. It also avoids the problematic combination of Ibn Sa'id's view by making the weaker (Fatiha's sunnah attribute) subordinate to the stronger (surah's wajib attribute).
The principle is: the weaker follows the stronger, not vice versa.

ويجهر بهما هو الصحيح لان الجمع بين الجهر والمخافتة فى ركعة واحدة شنيع وتغير النفل وهو الفاتحة اولى ترجمہ اور سورت اور فاتحہ دونوں کا جبر کرے۔ یہی صحیح ہے کیونکہ جبر اور اختفاء کا ایک رکعت میں جمع کرنا برا ہے۔ اور نفل کا متغیر کرنا اور وہ فاتحہ ہے اولی ہے۔

o کرے جیسا کہ امام محمد سے ہشام نے روایت کی ہے اور یا دونوں کے ساتھ جہر کرے پہلی صورت میں اقومی کو ادنی کے تابع کرنا لازم کہ کان کا صہ ہے جو کسی طرح مناسب نہیں ہے کیونکہ سورت کا بالجبر پڑھنا واجب تھا اور آخر کی رکعتوں میں فاتحہ کا بالا خفاء پڑھنا سنت سے بلال فهو مخيرا درجہ میں ہے پس فاتحہ جو سنت ہے اس کی صفت یعنی اخفاء کی رعایت کے پیش نظر سورت جو واجب ہے اس کی صفت یعنی جہر کو ختم کے ساتھ ۔ اقوامی کو ادنی کے تابع بنانا ہے اجو کسی طرح بھی مناسب نہیں اس لئے یہ صورت درست نہیں ہے اب دوسری صورت باقی رہی یعنی روند بذات خود شنید بالجبر پڑھنا سو اس میں کوئی قباحت نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں واجب (سورت ) کی صفت ( جبر ) کی وجہ سے نفل ( فاتحہ ) کی عنوان دونوں ۔ (اخفاء) کو بدلنا پڑتا ہے اور یہ اولی ہے اس لئے کہ اس صورت میں ادنی اقوی کے تابع ہوگا۔
Chapter on the Description of Prayer. The difference in wording is mentioned here. It is said that in Jami' al-Saghir, a word is mentioned that indicates obligation of qada' of surah in the last two rak'ahs, because in Jami' al-Saghir it says 'He recites in the last two' and this is like a command. And a command indicates obligation. So from the wording of Jami' al-Saghir it is known that qada' of surah in the last two is obligatory. And the evidence is that which passed in the previous lines. And in al-Mabsut it is mentioned with the word istihbab, because the wording of al-Mabsut is 'That he does not leave the surah in the first two, I prefer that he makes it up.' And it is obvious that the word 'aheb' indicates recommendation. So from al-Mabsut it is shown that if one left the surah in the first two, then making it up in the last two is mustahab, not wajib! And the evidence for istihbab is that the surah was delayed after Fatiha, but it was not connected to the first Fatiha because between the first Fatiha and the surah, a second Fatiha (which is better to recite in the last two) interposed. So it became impossible to observe the surah in every respect. Therefore in al-Mabsut it is said that making up the surah is mustahab, not wajib. And he recites both Fatiha and surah aloud. And it is correct to recite both aloud because combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah is reprehensible, and changing the nafl, which is the Fatiha, is preferable. Translation: He should recite both surah and Fatiha aloud. This is correct because combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah is bad. And changing the nafl, that is the Fatiha, is preferable. Explanation: When he makes up the surah in the last two, he should recite al-Fatiha and the surah both aloud; this is the correct statement. Ibn Sa'id narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf that he should recite only the surah aloud, and Hisham narrated from Imam Muhammad that he should not recite aloud at all, neither with Fatiha nor with surah. The reason for Hisham's narration is that combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah is ugly and bad, and it is preferable to change the surah (i.e., recite it silently instead of aloud) because Fatiha is in its place and is prioritized over the surah. So Fatiha is the original and the surah is its subordinate. In the last two rak'ahs, the right of Fatiha is to be recited with ikhfa', so its subordinate (the surah) should also be recited with ikhfa'. The reason for Ibn Sa'id's narration is that reciting Fatiha in the last two is an ada' (actual performance), while reciting the surah is a qada' (make-up). Ada' is according to its place, and qada' is according to how it was missed. Since the surah was missed with the attribute of jahr, its qada' will be with jahr. And since Fatiha is in its place, its attribute is observed: the attribute of Fatiha in the last two is ikhfa', so Fatiha will be recited with ikhfa'. As for the objection that combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah becomes necessary, the answer is that qada' is attached to its original place; the surah, although recited in the last two, is counted in the first two. Therefore, there is no actual combination of jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah. And the evidence for the correct statement is that combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah is legally blameworthy. Now there are only two possibilities: either to recite both with ikhfa' as Hisham narrated from Imam Muhammad, or to recite both with jahr. In the first case, it would necessitate making the stronger subordinate to the weaker, which is in no way appropriate because reciting the surah with jahr was wajib, and reciting Fatiha in the last two with ikhfa' is sunnah and of a lower grade. So to observe the attribute of Fatiha (which is sunnah) and thus ignore the attribute of the surah (which is wajib) is to make the stronger subordinate to the weaker, which is inappropriate. So this case is incorrect. Now only the second case remains: reciting both with jahr. There is no objection in this because in this case, due to the wajib (surah) having its attribute (jahr), the nafl (Fatiha) has to change its attribute (ikhfa'). This is preferable because the weaker becomes subordinate to the stronger.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding two issues: (1) whether making up the missed surah in the last two rak'ahs is wajib or mustahab, and (2) how to recite Fatiha and the surah aloud or silently in that case. The author first notes the difference between Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut. In Jami' al-Saghir, the word 'qara'a fi al-akhirayn' is interpreted as a command, making qada' wajib. In al-Mabsut, the word 'ahabba' indicates recommendation. The reasoning for istihbab is that the surah is delayed by a second Fatiha, so its connection to the first Fatiha is broken. Then, the dispute over jahr and ikhfa' is presented. Three riwayat exist: (i) from Ibn Sa'id from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: jahr only for surah, ikhfa' for Fatiha; (ii) from Hisham from Muhammad: no jahr at all; (iii) the correct view: jahr for both. The reasoning for each is explained. Hisham's view argues that combining jahr and ikhfa' in one rak'ah is bad, and since Fatiha is the original, its ikhfa' should be followed. Ibn Sa'id's view distinguishes between ada' (Fatiha) and qada' (surah), applying each attribute appropriately. The correct view avoids making the stronger (wajib surah's jahr) subordinate to the weaker (sunnah Fatiha's ikhfa'). The tarjih is that reciting both with jahr is correct.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation that others can hear.
مخافتة (mukhafatah): Silent or low recitation that only the reciter can hear.
أداء (ada'): Actual performance of an act in its proper time and place.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed act after its time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi view, what should the imam recite aloud when making up a missed surah in the last two rak'ahs?
A) Only the surah
B) Only al-Fatiha
C) Both al-Fatiha and the surah
D) Neither; both should be silent

Key Takeaway
Recite both Fatiha and surah aloud in the last two rak'ahs when making up a surah, as this avoids blameworthy combination and respects the hierarchy of wajib over sunnah.

Definition of Jahr and Ikhfa' in Recitation
Defines jahr and mukhafatah with two Hanafi opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi definitions of jahr and mukhafatah and apply them to determine the validity of silent recitation in prayer.

Core Idea
Silent recitation requires correct pronunciation of letters, not necessarily hearing oneself.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of recitation in prayer depends on whether it is jahr (audible) or mukhafatah (silent). This passage presents two definitions from classical scholars that affect how we understand these terms. Knowing the difference helps avoid invalidating prayer due to misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Read the passage and note the two definitions: al-Hindawani's (hearing oneself/others) and al-Karkhi's (minimum pronunciation for mukhafatah).
Focus on the key distinction: external audibility vs. articulation.
2
Understand the evidence for each
Al-Hindawani argues mere tongue movement without sound is not qira'ah; al-Karkhi argues qira'ah is an action of the tongue, not of the ear.
This is a difference in the essential nature of recitation.
3
Recognize the preferred view
The text indicates the wording of the book supports al-Karkhi. Note that this is the relied-upon view for fatwa.
The preferred view defines mukhafatah as correct pronunciation of letters.
4
Apply to a prayer scenario
Imagine a person in silent prayer who moves their lips but does not hear any sound. According to al-Karkhi, the recitation is valid; according to al-Hindawani, it is not.
The practical difference affects the validity of countless prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المخافتة ان يسمع نفسه والجهر ان يسمع غيره وهذا عند الفقيه ابى جعفر الهندواني لان مجرد حراً اللسان لايسمى قراءة بدون الصوت وقال الكرخى ادنى الجهر ان يسمع نفسه وادنى المخافتة تصحير ادنى م الحروف لان القراءة فعل اللسان دون الصماخ وفى لفظ الكتاب اشارة الى هذا و على هذا الاصل كل الا يسمى يتعلق بالنطق كالطلاق والعتاق والاستثناء و غير ذلك مادون الا
Then, mukhafatah (silent recitation) is that he makes himself hear, and jahr (audible recitation) is that he makes others hear. This is according to Fakih Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani, because mere movement of the tongue without sound is not called qira'ah. And al-Karkhi said: The minimum of jahr is that he makes himself hear, and the minimum of mukhafatah is the proper pronunciation of the letters, because qira'ah is an action of the tongue, not of the ear. And in the wording of the book there is an indication to this. And upon this principle, everything that is related to pronunciation (nutq) like talaq, 'itaq, istithna, and other than that, below the ...
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage defines the technical terms jahr (audible recitation) and mukhafatah (silent recitation) as used in the Hanafi school. Two definitions are presented: the first, from Fakih Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani, defines mukhafatah as reciting so that one can hear oneself, and jahr as reciting so that others can hear. His evidence is that mere tongue movement without sound does not constitute qira'ah (recitation) linguistically or customarily. The second, from al-Karkhi, defines the minimum of jahr as hearing oneself, and the minimum of mukhafatah as pronouncing the letters correctly (without necessarily hearing oneself). Al-Karkhi argues that qira'ah is an action of the tongue, not dependent on the ear hearing the sound. The text notes that the wording of the book (likely al-Hidayah) indicates support for al-Karkhi's view. The principle extends to all acts related to pronunciation, such as divorce (talaq), manumission ('itaq), legal exceptions (istithna), etc.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation: defined as making others hear (al-Hindawani) or making oneself hear (al-Karkhi).
مخافتة (mukhafatah): Silent recitation: making oneself hear (al-Hindawani) or proper pronunciation of letters (al-Karkhi).
نطق (nutq): Pronunciation or articulation; acts dependent on the tongue, like talaq and 'itaq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Karkhi's definition, what is the minimum for silent recitation (mukhafatah)?
A) Hearing oneself
B) Making others hear
C) Proper pronunciation of letters
D) Moving the lips without sound

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines silent recitation by correct pronunciation, not necessarily audibility to oneself, following al-Karkhi's view.

Defining Jahr and Ikhfa': The Hindawani-Karkhi Dispute
Defines jahr and ikhfa' and presents an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definitions of jahr and ikhfa' according to Hindawani and Karkhi, and apply these definitions to utterances like divorce and manumission.

Core Idea
The definition of jahr and ikhfa' governs not only prayer but also talaq, itq, and istithna.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah defines two key terms for recitation in prayer: jahr (loud) and ikhfa' (quiet). However, the definitions are contested within the Hanafi school between two influential scholars, al-Hindawani and al-Karkhi. Their disagreement affects not only the validity of prayer recitation but also the effectiveness of other speech acts like divorce and manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Read the passage and extract the definitions of jahr and ikhfa' according to Hindawani and according to Karkhi.
Hindawani defines ikhfa' as hearing oneself, jahr as making others hear. Karkhi defines minimum jahr as hearing oneself, minimum ikhfa' as correct pronunciation.
2
Understand the reasoning
Analyze the basis for each definition: Hindawani requires sound because qira'ah is not called recitation without sound; Karkhi says qira'ah is an act of the tongue, not the ear.
The difference hinges on whether qira'ah requires audible sound or merely articulate tongue movement.
3
Identify the practical differences
The passage extends the dispute to other utterances: divorce, manumission, exception. For example, if a man says 'Anti taliq' without hearing himself, Karkhi says talaq occurs, Hindawani says it does not.
The thamarah al-khilaf is seen in the validity of these acts under different conditions.
4
Note the preferred view
The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah indicates support for Karkhi's view by referencing the text of al-Quduri.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the Karkhi definition.

Source Text

باب صفۃ الصلوة

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جو اشرف البدائية کرے جیسا کہ امام محمد سے ہشام نے روایت کی ہے اور یا دونوں کے ساتھ جہر کرے پہلی صورت میں اقومی کو ادنی کے تابع کرنا لازم کہ کان کا صہ ہے جو کسی طرح مناسب نہیں ہے کیونکہ سورت کا بالجبر پڑھنا واجب تھا اور آخر کی رکعتوں میں فاتحہ کا بالا خفاء پڑھنا سنت سے بلال فهو مخيرا درجہ میں ہے پس فاتحہ جو سنت ہے اس کی صفت یعنی اخفاء کی رعایت کے پیش نظر سورت جو واجب ہے اس کی صفت یعنی جہر کو ختم کے ساتھ ۔ اقوامی کو ادنی کے تابع بنانا ہے اجو کسی طرح بھی مناسب نہیں اس لئے یہ صورت درست نہیں ہے اب دوسری صورت باقی رہی یعنی روند بذات خود شنید بالجبر پڑھنا سو اس میں کوئی قباحت نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں واجب (سورت ) کی صفت ( جبر ) کی وجہ سے نفل ( فاتحہ ) کی عنوان دونوں ۔ (اخفاء) کو بدلنا پڑتا ہے اور یہ اولی ہے اس لئے کہ اس صورت میں ادنی اقوی کے تابع ہوگا۔

اور وجوب آ

ثم المخافتة ان يسمع نفسه والجهر ان يسمع غيره وهذا عند الفقيه ابى جعفر الهندواني لان مجرد حرا اللسان لايسمى قراءة بدون الصوت وقال الكرخى ادنى الجهر ان يسمع نفسه وادنى المخافتة تصحير ادنى م الحروف لان القراءة فعل اللسان دون الصماخ وفى لفظ الكتاب اشارة الى هذا و على هذا الاصل كل الا يسمى يتعلق بالنطق كالطلاق والعتاق والاستثناء و غير ذلك مادون الا

ترجمہ پھر اخفاء کا پڑھنا یہ ہے کہ اپنے آپ کو سنائے اور جبر یہ ہے کہ دوسرے کو سنائے اور یہ فقیہ ابو جعفر ہندوانی کے نزدیک ہے کیا تر جمعہ بغیر آواز کے محض زبان کی حرکت کا نام قرآت نہیں کہلاتا۔ اور امام کرتی نے کہا کہ جب کا متر مرتبہ یہ ہے کہ اپنے آپ کو سنائے اور انھ چھوٹی آیتم کمتر مرتبہ یہ ہے کہ حروف صحیح نکلیں۔ کیونکہ قرآت تو زبان کا فعل ہے نہ کہ کان کا۔ اور لفظ کتاب میں بھی اسی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ اور امام صاحب اصل پر ہر وہ امر ہے جو نطق سے متعلق ہو جیسے طلاق آزاد کر نا استثناء اور ان کے علاوہ۔

پوری ایتا

تشریح اس عبارت میں جبر اور اخفاء کی تعریف کی گئی ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ کے بیان کے مطابق حاصل یہ ہے کہ کلمات کے اجزاء تشریح زبان پر مستعمل ہیں ان کی دو قسمیں ہیں کلام اور قرآت کیونکہ اس سے مخاطب کو نسبت کا فائدہ پہنچانا مقصود ہوگا یا نہیں اگر اول ہے تو یعنی جس ۔ کلام ہوگا ور نہ قرآت ہے پھر ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی دو دو قسمیں ہیں جبر اور مخافت لیکن ان دونوں کے درمیان حد فاضل میر کے ساتھ جا ہمارے علماء کا اختلاف ہے چنا نچہ فقیہ ابو جعفر ہندوائی نے کہا کہ اخفاء (آہستہ پڑھنا) یہ ہے کہ اپنے آپ کو سنادے اور اگر اس سے کہ اس ہے تو اس کو مجھ اور دندنہ کہتے ہیں نہ یہ کہ کلام ہے اور نہ قرآت اور جہر یہ ہے کہ دوسرے کو سنادے یعنی اتنی آواز سے پڑھے کہ قریب کا آنا قرآت کی ا سن لے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ بغیر آواز کے خالی زبان کی حرکت کا نام قرآت نہیں نہ الفہ اور نہ عرفاً۔ ہو جائے گی امام کرتی نے کہا کہ جہر کا متر درجہ یہ ہے کہ اپنے آپ کو سنائے اور اخفاء کا کمتر درجہ یہ ہے کہ حروف صحیح نکلیں کیونکہ قرآت زبان کا فرق تو اس ؛
ہے نہ کان کا۔

ما يجوزبه

باب صفة الصلوة
زم آتا کہ کان کا ، صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ قدوری کی عبارت میں بھی امام کرخی کے قول کی طرف اشارہ موجود ہے کیونکہ اول فصل میں مذکور ہے ل کے فهو مخير ان شاء جهر واسمع نفسه وان شاء خافت صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ یہی اختلاف ہر اس چیز میں ہے جس کا تعلق نطق ر کرنا کے ساتھ ہے جیسے طلاق عتاق اور استثناء وغیرہ مثلاً اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوری سے انت طالق یا غلام سے انت جو کہا اور کہنے والے نے ں کو بذات خود نیں سنا تو امام کرخی کے نزدیک طلاق اور عتاق واقع ہو جائیں گے اور ہندوانی کے نزدیک واقع نہیں ہوں گے۔ اسی طرح اگر نت ان دونوں کے ساتھ جبر کیا اور استثناء کا ایسے طور پر اختفاء کیا کہ خود بھی نہیں سن سکا تو امام کرخی کے نزدیک طلاق اور عتاق واقع نہیں ہوں گے۔ اور استثناء معتبر ہوگا اور ہندوانی کے نزدیک دونوں فی الحال واقع ہو جائیں گے اور استثناء معتبر نہیں ہوگا۔ اسی اختلاف پر ذبیحہ پر تسمیہ
لة
اور وجوب سجدہ تلاوت ہے۔
Then mukhafatah (quiet recitation) is that one hears oneself, and jahr (loud recitation) is that one makes others hear. This is according to al-Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani because mere movement of the tongue is not called recitation without sound. Al-Karkhi said: The minimum of jahr is that one hears oneself, and the minimum of mukhafatah is the correct pronunciation of the letters, because recitation is an act of the tongue, not of the ear. In the wording of the book (al-Quduri) there is an indication of this. And upon this principle, every matter related to utterance, such as divorce, manumission, exception, etc.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the definition of jahr (loud recitation) and ikhfa' (quiet recitation) in prayer. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani and Imam al-Karkhi. According to Hindawani, ikhfa' means reciting in a way that one can hear oneself, while jahr means making others hear. He argues that mere movement of the tongue without sound is not considered qira'ah. Al-Karkhi, on the other hand, defines the minimum of jahr as hearing oneself, and the minimum of ikhfa' as pronouncing the letters correctly, because qira'ah is an act of the tongue, not the ear. The author notes that the text of al-Quduri indicates support for al-Karkhi's view. This dispute has practical implications beyond prayer: it applies to any utterance related to speech, such as divorce (talaq), manumission (itq), and exception (istithna). For example, if a person says to his wife 'Anti taliq' or to his slave 'Anta hurr' and does not hear himself, according to al-Karkhi, the divorce or manumission occurs, but according to Hindawani, it does not. Conversely, if he pronounces them loudly but makes an exception in a whisper that he himself does not hear, al-Karkhi considers the exception valid and the divorce/manumission not effective, while Hindawani considers the divorce/manumission effective and the exception invalid.

Key Terms
الْجَهْر (al-jahr): Loud recitation; according to Hindawani: making others hear; according to Karkhi: hearing oneself.
الْمُخَافَتَة (al-mukhafatah): Quiet recitation; according to Hindawani: hearing oneself; according to Karkhi: correct pronunciation of letters.
الْقِرَاءَة (al-qira'ah): Recitation of Quran; disputed whether it requires sound or mere tongue movement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Karkhi, what is the minimum level of ikhfa' (quiet recitation)?
A) Making others hear
B) Hearing oneself
C) Correct pronunciation of letters
D) Reciting in a whisper without moving the tongue

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two valid definitions of jahr and ikhfa', with the Karkhi view (tongue movement suffices) being the relied-upon position that extends to all speech acts.

Minimum Amount of Recitation Sufficient in Prayer: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on minimum qira'ah in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the minimum qira'ah, identify their respective proofs, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds one verse suffices; the Sahibayn require three short verses or one long verse.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum Quranic recitation required for prayer to be valid. Imam Abu Hanifa, relying on the general command 'Read what is easy of the Quran', deems one verse sufficient. His two eminent disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree, arguing that custom dictates a larger amount. Understanding their proofs sharpens your ability to weigh textual and customary evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
What does Abu Hanifa say? What do the Sahibayn say? Be precise about the quantity (one verse vs. three short verses or one long verse).
2
Identify the proof of Abu Hanifa
Locate the Quranic verse he cites and explain how he derives his ruling from it. Note that he interprets the command as absolute.
The verse is from Surah al-Muzzammil (73:20).
3
Identify the proof of the Sahibayn
What is their reasoning? They rely on customary understanding ('urf) to argue that less than three short verses is not considered recitation. They also use an analogy (qiyas) to reciting less than a verse.
Their analogy: reciting less than a verse is insufficient, so less than three short verses is likewise insufficient.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn
How does Abu Hanifa counter the custom argument? He holds that the text is general and cannot be restricted by custom. The literal command overrides 'urf.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
What practical difference does this dispute make? For example, if someone recites 'ثُمَّ نَظَر', which position validates the prayer? Which view is relied upon for fatwa in the Hanafi school?
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

و ادنى ما يجزىء من القراءة في الصلوة اية عند ابي حنيفة وقالا ثلاث آيات قصار او اية طويلة لانه لايسمى قارنا بدونه فاشبه قراءة مادون الآية وله قوله تعالى فَاقْرَءُ وَامَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآن من غير فصل الا ان مادون الآية خارج والآية ليست في معناه

ترجمہ اور قرآت کی ادنی مقدار جو نماز میں کفایت کر جاتی ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ایک آیت ہے اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ تین چھوٹی آیتیں یا ایک بڑی آیت ہے کیونکہ اس سے کم قراءت کرنے والا نہیں کہلائے گا پس یہ مادون الآمیہ کی قرآت کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور امام صاحب کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَاقْرَءُ وَامَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ بغیر کسی تفصیل کے ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ ایک آیت سے کم خارج ہے اور پوری آیت اس کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔

تشریح نماز کے اندر قرآت حالت حضر میں ہوگی یا سفر میں پس اگر حضر میں ہے تو اس کی تین قسمیں ہیں (۱) مـابـجـوز به الصلوة یعنی جس کے ساتھ جواز صلوۃ متعلق ہوتا ہے اس کے بغیر نماز نہیں ہوگی۔ (۲) جس کے ساتھ حد کراہت سے نکل جاتا ہے۔ (۳) جس کے ساتھ حد استجاب میں داخل ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر سفر میں ہے تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں نمازی عجلت میں ہو گا یا حالت امن اور قرار میں۔ اس عبارت میں م یجوز به ال صلوۃ کی مقدار کو بیان کیا گیا ہے خواہ حضر میں ہو یا سفر میں چنانچہ فرمایا کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک قرآت کی اونی مقدار جس سے نماز جائز ہو جائے گی ایک آیت ہے پس اگر ایت دو کلوں یا زیادہ پر مشتمل ہوتو با تفاق مشائخ نماز جائز ہو جائے گی۔ جیسے باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَقُتِلَ كَيْفَ قَدَّرَ ثُمَّ نَظر ، اور اگر ایک ہی کلمہ ہے جیسے مُدُهَامَّتَان یا ایک حرف ہے جیسے ص، ن فی تو اس میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے۔ بعض کے نزدیک کافی ہو جائے گی اور بعض کے نزدیک کافی نہیں ہوگی۔ صاحبین نے کہا کہ ما بجوز بہ الصلوۃ کی مقدار چھوٹی تین آیتیں ہیں یا بڑی ایک ایت جیسے آیتہ الکرسی اور آیت مداینت صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ چھوٹی تمین آیات یا بڑی ایک آیت سے کم پڑھنے والے کو عرف عام میں قاری قرآن نہیں کہا جاتا، پس اس کی قرآت مادون الآیۃ کی قرآت کے مشابہ نہ ہوگی اور مادون الآیتہ نماز کے لئے کافی نہیں لہذا چھوٹی تین آیات یا بڑی ایک آیت سے کم کی قرآت بھی کافی نہیں ہوگی ۔ صالحین کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ایک آیت اگر چہ حقیقتہ قرآن ہے مگر عرف میں چھوٹی تین آیات یا بڑی ایک آیت پر قرآن کا اطلاق
And the minimum that suffices of recitation in prayer is one verse according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Sahibayn) said: three short verses or one long verse, because one is not called a reciter without it, so it resembles recitation of less than a verse. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' without specification, except that less than a verse is excluded, and a full verse is not in its meaning.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage addresses the minimum amount of Quranic recitation that suffices to validate the prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that one verse is sufficient, regardless of length, because the Quranic command 'Read what is easy of the Quran' is general and includes any verse. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the minimum is three short verses or one long verse (like Ayat al-Kursi), because a person who recites less than that is not called a 'qari' (reciter) in common usage. The commentary elaborates on the categories of recitation: what makes prayer valid, what removes dislikedness, and what is recommended. It also discusses the case of very short verses or single words, where there is disagreement among later scholars. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, i.e., one verse suffices, but it is better to recite a longer passage to avoid disagreement.

Key Terms
الْآيَة (al-ayah): A verse of the Quran. In this passage, it refers to the minimum unit of recitation.
صَاحِبَيْن (al-sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
مَا يَجُوزُ بِهِ الصَّلَاةُ (ma yajuzu bihi al-salah): The minimum amount of recitation that makes the prayer valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum amount of Quranic recitation that suffices for prayer according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) Three short verses
B) One long verse
C) One verse of any length
D) The entire Surah al-Fatihah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon view is that one verse of any length suffices for prayer, but the Sahibayn's opinion (three short verses or one long verse) is also a valid position within the school.

Recitation in Travel Prayer
Ruling on which surahs to recite in travel prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah ruling on surah recitation after Fatihah in travel prayer and identify the recommended surahs based on the traveler's situation (haste vs. settlement).

Core Idea
In travel, recite Fatihah and any surah; choose short surahs if in a hurry, longer if settled.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the sunnah of recitation in travel prayer. While the basic obligation is to recite Surah al-Fatihah, the additional surah after it is sunnah, and the choice of surah is flexible. The Prophet's practice shows that short surahs like al-Mu'awwidhatayn are permissible and recommended when the traveler is in haste. However, if the traveler is in a state of safety and settlement, longer surahs like al-Buruj are preferred, balancing the sunnah of lightening with the ability to recite more.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is recitation of a surah after Fatihah in travel prayer. This is a sunnah act.
2
State the basic ruling
You recite Fatihah and then any surah you wish. There is no fixed surah for travel.
3
Note the two scenarios
If in haste (ajlat al-sayr), recite short surahs like al-Mu'awwidhatayn. If in safety and settlement (aman wa qarar), recite medium-length surahs like al-Buruj.
The reasoning: travel already reduces rak'ats, so lightening recitation is even more appropriate.
4
Memorize the proof
The Prophet recited the Mu'awwidhatayn in Fajr during travel, reported by Abu Dawud and Nasa'i.
This hadith is a confirmation of the permissibility and sunnah.

وفي السفر يقرأ فاتحة الكتاب واى سورة شاء لما روى ان النبي عليه السلام قرأ في صلوة الفجر في سفر بالمعوذتين ولان للسفر اثرا فى اسقاط شطر الصلوة فلأن يؤثر فى تخفيف القراءة اولى وهذا اذا كان راتوں کی در عجلة من السير وان كان فى امنة وقرار يقرأ فى الفجر نحو سورة البروج وانشقت لانه يمكنه مراعاة التشريح یعنی ہر ركعت مع التخفيف

ترجمہ اور سفر میں فاتحہ الکتاب اور جو سورت چاہے پڑھے کیونکہ روایت ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے سفر میں فجر کی نماز میں معوذن نے کہا کہ ان قرآت کی ۔ اور اس لئے کہ سفر کو آدھی نماز ساقط کرنے میں داخل ہے پس تخفیف قرآت میں بدرجہ اولی دخل ہوگا۔ اور یہ حکم اس تنت الجمعة " ساتھ اس کو سنت کی رعایت کرنا ممکن ہے۔ جب کہ روانگی کی جندی ہو اور اگر حالت امن اور حالت قرار میں ہو تو فجر میں سورہ بروج اور سورہ وانشقت کے مانند پڑھے کیونک تخفیف اصل انسی

تشریح اس عبارت میں مصنف نے حالت سفر کی نماز میں قرآت کا ذ کر کیا ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ سفر کی حالت میں قرآت مسنون بیت علیہ وسل سورۂ فاتحہ اور جو سورت چاہے پڑھے اگر چھوٹی سورت پڑھی تب بھی سنت ادا ہو جائے گی کیونکہ روایت ہے کہ حضور پیے نے سفر کی جان کی نماز فجر میں قل اعوذ برب الفلق اور قل اعوذ برب الناس پڑھی ہے یہ حدیث ابوداؤ داور نسائی نے عقبہ بن عامر رضی اور سو آیات تک
And in travel, he recites Surah al-Fatihah and whichever surah he wishes, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited in the Fajr prayer during travel the Mu'awwidhatayn (two surahs of refuge). And because travel has an effect in dropping half of the prayer, so it is more appropriate to affect the lightening of the recitation. This is when he is in haste of travel. And if he is in safety and settlement, he recites in Fajr something like Surah al-Buruj and Surah al-Inshiqaq, because he can observe the tashrih (detail) while maintaining lightness.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on recitation in travel prayer. The sunnah is to recite Surah al-Fatihah followed by any surah. If the traveler is in a hurry (e.g., on a journey), it is recommended to recite short surahs like al-Mu'awwidhatayn (Surah al-Falaq and Surah al-Nas), based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in Fajr prayer during travel. The reasoning is that travel reduces the number of rak'ats (from 4 to 2 for most prayers), so it is even more appropriate to lighten the recitation. If the traveler is in a state of safety and settled (not in a hurry), then longer surahs are recommended, like al-Buruj and al-Inshiqaq, because one can manage with some length while still maintaining some lightness. This shows the Hanafi principle of considering circumstances in salah.

Key Terms
تخفيف (takhfif): Lightening, reduction, especially in recitation (qira'ah) due to travel
عجلة السير (ajlat al-sayr): Haste of travel, when the traveler is in a hurry

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Recite a lengthy surah like al-Buruj
B) Recite a short surah like the Mu'awwidhatayn
C) Recite only Fatihah and no additional surah
D) Recite any surah of medium length

Key Takeaway
In travel prayer, recite Fatihah and any surah; choose short surahs when in a hurry and longer surahs when settled.

Imam Abu Hanifa's Proof for Minimum Recitation in Prayer
Establishes that one complete verse suffices for prayer validity based on an absolute Quranic command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence for the sufficiency of one verse in prayer and evaluate the objection regarding less than a verse.

Core Idea
A single complete verse suffices for prayer validity because the Quranic command is absolute and includes it.

Imam Abu Hanifa defends the position that reciting one complete verse (ayat) in prayer is sufficient for validity. He bases this on the absolute command in Surah al-Muzzammil: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran.' In this lesson, we will examine his proof, the objection concerning less than a verse, and the Hanafi response that distinguishes between a verse and a part of a verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled upon? What is the hukm? The act is recitation in prayer; the ruling is that reciting one complete verse makes the prayer valid.
2
Locate the dalil
Imam Abu Hanifa cites Quran 73:20: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran.' Identify this as the primary evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this verse prove the ruling? The phrase is absolute (muthlaq) and includes any quantity that is easy, including a single verse.
The imperative indicates a command, and the absolute form means one verse is included.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (objection)
An objection is raised: if the absolute command includes everything easy, why does less than a verse not suffice? Understand the objection fully.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes between a verse and less than a verse. A verse is Quran both in reality (haqiqatan) and legally (hukman); less than a verse is only Quran in reality, not legally, because it can be recited by those in major impurity.
Hence less than a verse is excluded from the absolute command.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فاقرء وأما تيسر من القرآن ہے اس طور پر ایک مطلق ہے اس میں آمین کے لئے اترے ال آیت کی کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے لہذا جس طرح ما فوق الآیۃ جواز صلوۃ کے لئے کافی ہے اس طرح ایک آیت بھی کافی ہے اور وجہ اس کا کہ آیت واحد حقیقتا بھی قرآن ہے اور حکما ابھی حقیقتا قرآن ہونا تو ظاہر ہے اور حکما اس لئے ہے کہ ایک آیت کی قرآت حائن پر حرام ہے پس آیت واحد من القرآن کے اطلاق میں داخل ہوگئی لیکن اس پر اشکال ہوگا وہ یہ کہ اگر فافرة وأما تبن ی تخفیف تک القران مطلق ہے اور اس میں کوئی تفصیل نہیں تو جس طرح ایک آیت نماز جائز ہونے کے لئے کافی ہے اس طرح ایک آیت حاصل ۔ ساتھ بھی نماز جائز ہونی چاہیے تھی اس لئے کہ اطلاق دونوں کو شامل ہے حالانکہ مادون آریہ کے ساتھ نماز جائز نہیں ہوتی پس رہتے ہیں کہ ایک آیت کے ساتھ بھی نماز جائز نہ ہونی چاہئے حالانکہ امام صاحب جواز کے قائل ہیں۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مادون الآمیر ہا ہے کہ اطمینان من القرآن کے اطلاق میں داخل نہیں ہے کیونکہ مطلق جب بولا جاتا ہے تو اس سے اس کا فر یامل مراد ہوتا ہے اور قرآن کا فرد اس صورت میں ہے جو حقیقتا بھی قرآن ہو اور حکما بھی قرآن ہو مادون الآمیتہ اگر چہ حقیقت قرآن ہے لیکن حکما قرآن نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مارون ويقرأ في کی قرآت جنبی اور حائضہ کے لئے جائز ہے پس مادون الآیۃ بالا جماع فاقر و اما تیسر من القرآن کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر کوئی یہ کہے کہ جب مادون الآية من القرآن کے اطلاق کے تحت داخل نہیں تو آیت کو بھی اس کے ساتھ انزالی ستین جائے۔ تو اس کا جواب صاحب ہدایہ نے یہ دیا کہ آیت مادون الآیتہ کے معنی میں نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے آیت مادون الآیۃ کے سات اربعین و با نہیں ہوگی۔
Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran.' This is an absolute expression; there is no detail in it regarding 'amen' or anything else. Therefore, just as more than one verse suffices for the validity of prayer, so does one verse suffice. The reason is that a single verse is Quran in reality and also in legal consideration. Its being Quran in reality is obvious, and in legal consideration because reciting a single verse is forbidden for a menstruating woman. Thus a single verse is included in the absolute 'of the Quran.' However, there is an objection: if the absolute 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' is absolute and has no detail, then just as one verse suffices, less than a verse should also suffice, since the absolute includes both, but in fact prayer is not valid with less than a verse. So what is the reason that prayer should not be valid with one verse either, while Imam Abu Hanifa holds it valid? The answer is that less than a verse is not included in the absolute 'of the Quran' because when an absolute is used, it refers to its customary individual, and the individual of the Quran is that which is Quran both in reality and in legal consideration. Less than a verse, although Quran in reality, is not Quran in legal consideration because its recitation is permissible for the junub and menstruating woman. Therefore, less than a verse, by consensus, is not included under 'So recite what is easy of the Quran.' And if someone says: when less than a verse is not included in the absolute, then the verse too should be for equality with it? The author of Hidayah answers: a verse is not in the meaning of less than a verse, for this reason a verse is not like less than a verse.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing Imam Abu Hanifa's position that reciting a single complete verse (ayat) in prayer is sufficient for validity, based on the absolute command in Surah al-Muzzammil (73:20). The commentator first presents the proof: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' is an absolute statement without specification of quantity. Hence, one verse qualifies. He then explains that a verse is Quran both in reality (haqiqatan) and legally (hukman) — the latter because it is forbidden for a menstruating woman to recite it. Then an objection is raised: if the absolute is truly unconditional, then less than a verse (ma dun al-ayah) should also be valid, but it is not. The response is that the absolute expression refers to the customary individual of Quran, which is that which is Quran both in reality and in legal ruling. Less than a verse, though Quranic in reality (since it is part of a verse), is not legally considered Quran because its recitation is permitted for a person in major impurity (junub) or a menstruating woman. Therefore it is excluded from the absolute command. A second objection asks why a verse should be treated differently from less than a verse when both are not fully Quran legally? The author of Hidayah replies that a verse is not equivalent to less than a verse in meaning; hence the analogy fails. The passage thus defends the Hanafi position that one full verse suffices, while less than a verse does not.

Key Terms
مطلق (muthlaq): An unqualified expression that applies to all members of its category without restriction.
مادون الآية (ma dun al-ayah): Less than a complete verse; a portion of a verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why does less than a verse (ma dun al-ayah) not suffice for prayer validity?
A) It is not considered Quran in reality.
B) It is not considered Quran legally (hukman) because its recitation is permitted for the junub and menstruating woman.
C) The absolute command in the Quran explicitly excludes it.
D) It was never practiced by the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Prayer is valid with recitation of one complete verse because the absolute Quranic command includes it, even though less than a verse is excluded due to its legal status.

Recitation in travel prayer
States the sunnah recitation for Fajr in travel and its evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah recitation for Fajr in travel, distinguish between the rulings for haste and settled conditions, and explain the qiyas basis for lightening recitation.

Core Idea
Travel lightens both the number of rak'ahs and the length of recitation: any surah suffices, but longer is better when settled.

This passage from al-Hidayah explains the recommended recitation in Fajr prayer while traveling. It presents a hadith proof and a qiyas argument, and also distinguishes two travel conditions. We'll analyze how the Hanafi school derives this ruling and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its sunnah level
Determine what is being ruled upon (recitation after al-Fatihah in Fajr during travel) and its hukm level (sunnah muakkadah). Note that omitting the surah does not invalidate the prayer.
Hanafis distinguish sunnah muakkadah from wajib; here, reciting any surah is confirmed practice.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The author cites the hadith that the Prophet recited the Mu'awwidhatain in Fajr during travel. Identify the chain and meaning: the Prophet's action demonstrates permissibility of short surahs.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i from Uqbah ibn Amir; its thubut is zanni.
3
Follow the qiyas argument
Since travel reduces the number of rak'ahs (qasr) due to difficulty, it should more appropriately reduce the length of recitation. Identify the asl (qasr), far' (recitation), and illah (difficulty of travel).
The illah is mashaqqat al-safar (hardship of travel), which is jali (clear) and established by tahqiq al-manat.
4
Distinguish between haste and settled conditions
Note the two scenarios: when the traveler is in a hurry (ajalah al-sayr) and when settled (amanah wa qarar). In haste, any short surah suffices; when settled, longer surahs like al-Buruj and al-Inshiqaq are recommended to observe both lightening and sunnah.
This distinction shows the flexibility of the sunnah: the ruling adapts to the traveler's state.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
For a traveler in a hurry, reciting a short surah like al-Ikhlas is fine. For a traveler at a rest stop, reciting a medium surah like al-Buruj is better. The key is to balance ease (takhfif) with following the sunnah (ittiba').
This practical application confirms the Hanafi emphasis on contextual rulings.

Ruling on recitation in travel prayer: And in travel, he recites Surah al-Fatihah and whichever surah he wishes, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited in Fajr prayer during travel the two Mu'awwidhats. And because travel has an effect in dropping half of the prayer, so it more properly has an effect in lightening recitation. This is when he is in haste during the journey. If he is in security and settled, he recites in Fajr something like Surah al-Buruj and Surah al-Inshiqaq, because he can observe the sunnah with lightening. Translation: And in travel, recite al-Fatihah and whichever surah you wish, because it is reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) in his travel in Fajr prayer recited the Mu'awwidhats. And because travel is involved in dropping half of the prayer, so it more properly has an effect in lightening recitation. This ruling applies when he is in haste. If he is in a state of security and settlement, he recites in Fajr like Surah al-Buruj and Surah al-Inshiqaq, because lightening is also achieved and sunnah is observed. The author mentions that in travel, the sunnah is to recite al-Fatihah and any surah; even if a short surah is recited, the sunnah is fulfilled. The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and Nasa'i from Uqbah ibn Amir. The author says that this lightening is when he is in a hurry; if he is in a state of security and settlement, e.g., staying at a stop with intention to leave calmly, then in Fajr he should recite Surah al-Buruj and Surah al-Inshiqaq, because in that situation lightening and observance of sunnah are both achieved.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the recommended recitation (qira'ah) in the Fajr prayer while traveling. The author states that the sunnah is to recite Surah al-Fatihah and whichever other surah one wishes, even a very short one like al-Mu'awwidhatain. Two proofs are given: first, a hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited the two Mu'awwidhats (Surah al-Falaq and Surah al-Nas) in Fajr during travel; second, a rational proof (qiyas) — since travel causes the reduction of the number of rak'ahs from four to two, it should more appropriately cause reduction in the length of recitation. However, this leniency is conditional: it applies when the traveler is in a hurry. If the traveler is settled at a stop in security and not in haste, then the sunnah is to recite longer surahs such as al-Buruj and al-Inshiqaq, because one can observe both the sunnah of longer recitation and the general lightening appropriate to travel. The commentator explains that even with a short surah, the sunnah is fulfilled, but a longer recitation is better when possible. The hadith is cited from Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i. The passage also mentions that reciting a surah after al-Fatihah is a sunnah, not an obligation; if one recites only al-Fatihah, the prayer is valid but contrary to the sunnah.

Key Terms
مسنون (masnun): Recommended or sunnah act; omission does not invalidate but is contrary to the Prophetic practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When he is in a hurry during the journey.
B) When he is in a state of security and settled, not in haste.
C) Only when leading prayers for a large congregation.
D) When he is alone without any companions.

Key Takeaway
Travel lightens recitation: any surah suffices in haste, but longer is better when settled, balancing ease and sunnah.

Quantity of Recitation in Fajr Prayer (Residence)
Provides the recommended amount of recitation for Fajr in residence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended range of Quranic recitation in Fajr prayer for a resident, and explain how the imam should adjust the quantity based on the congregation's eagerness and circumstances.

Core Idea
The Prophet varied his recitation in Fajr – flexibility, not a fixed number.

In this passage, the author addresses the quantity of recitation (qira'ah) after Surah al-Fatihah in the Fajr prayer when one is not travelling (hadar). While there is a basic recommendation of 40-50 verses, multiple narrations from the Prophet show a range from 40 to 100 verses. The key is that the imam should consider the condition of the congregation and the season. This lesson will help you understand the flexibility within the Hanafi school and the method of reconciling the various traditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
Determine that recitation after Fatiha in Fajr is sunnah muakkadah, not fard or wajib. The quantity is recommended but flexible.
The hukm level is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Recall the basic recommendation
The text states 40 or 50 verses in total (20-25 per rak'ah) besides Fatiha.
This is the starting point.
3
Recognize the range from various narrations
Other narrations mention 40-60 or 60-100 verses. All are authentic (athar).
The author of al-Hidayah reconciles them.
4
Apply the method of reconciliation
The imam adjusts based on the congregation's eagerness: 100 for eager, 40 for lazy, 50-60 for average. Also consider night length and occupations.
This shows the ruling is not rigid.
5
Evaluate the practical application
Today's imams can use this principle to choose a surah length suitable for their congregation.
Flexibility is key.

Quantity of recitation in Fajr prayer in residence: And he recites in residence in Fajr in the two rak'ahs forty or fifty verses besides Surah al-Fatihah. And it is narrated from forty to sixty, and from sixty to one hundred, and each is supported by tradition. The method of reconciliation is that he recites with the eager ones one hundred, with the lazy ones forty, and with the average ones between fifty and sixty. And it is said that he should consider the length and shortness of the nights, and the abundance or scarcity of occupations. Explanation: The ruling is that in residence, in the two rak'ahs of Fajr, besides Fatiha, recite forty or fifty verses (i.e., twenty or twenty-five per rak'ah). One narration says forty to sixty, another says sixty to one hundred. The author of Hiday says that each is supported by tradition. For example, Ibn Abbas reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) on Friday recited Surah al-Sajdah (thirty verses) and Surah al-Insan (thirty-one verses). In Sahih Muslim, Jabir ibn Samurah reports that the Prophet used to recite in Fajr 'Qaf' (?) and Abu Hurairah says he recited between sixty and one hundred verses. The method of reconciliation: if the followers are eager to hear, recite up to one hundred; if lazy, forty; if average, fifty to sixty. Also consider the length of nights (longer in winter, shorter in summer) and the busyness of people.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the recommended quantity of recitation (qira'ah) in the Fajr prayer for a resident (hadar). The basic recommendation is to recite in two rak'ahs approximately 40-50 verses in addition to Surah al-Fatihah. However, there are several transmitted narrations giving different amounts: from 40 to 60, and from 60 to 100. The author reconciles these by showing that the Prophet varied his recitation according to circumstances: when the followers were eager and attentive, he would recite longer (up to 100 verses); when they were lazy or in a hurry, he would recite less (around 40); and for those in between, around 50-60. Another consideration is the length of nights (longer in winter allowing more recitation) and the occupation of the people (less recitation when people are busy). The commentator provides examples: on Fridays, the Prophet recited Surah al-Sajdah (30 verses) and Surah al-Insan (31 verses) in Fajr, totaling 61 verses. Jabir ibn Samurah reports he recited 'Qaf' (Surah Qaf, 45 verses) and Abu Hurairah reports between 60 and 100. Hence the imam should judge the situation. The passage also implies that reciting a surah after Fatiha is sunnah muakkadah, and the quantity can be adjusted. The final part mentions that the imam should also consider seasonal variations.

Key Terms
اثر (athar): A narration or tradition from the Prophet or Companions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 40 verses
B) 60 verses
C) 100 verses
D) Between 50 and 60 verses

Key Takeaway
The quantity of recitation in Fajr after Fatiha is sunnah and flexible, adjusted based on congregation and circumstances.

Fajr Recitation in Travel: Ruling and Condition of Haste
Ruling on Fajr recitation in travel with condition of haste

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Fajr recitation during travel and identify the condition that modifies the recommended amount.

Core Idea
Travel allows reducing Fajr recitation, but only when in haste; at ease, recite medium surahs.

This passage addresses the quantity of recitation in Fajr prayer for a traveler. While the Prophet (ﷺ) demonstrated reduction with two short surahs, the author of Hidayah clarifies that this concession is conditional on haste. If the traveler is settled and not in a rush, he should recite medium surahs to observe both the sunnah of reduction and the sunnah of reciting from the Mufassal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is recitation in Fajr prayer during travel. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) to reduce the quantity.
The overall qira'ah is wajib, but the choice of surahs is sunnah.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith: When the Prophet descended for Fajr, he led the people with two short surahs (e.g., Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun and Qul huwa Allahu ahad). This proves the recommended practice.
This is a Sunnah ahad, zanni al-thubut, but the meaning (dalala) is clear.
3
Trace the secondary dalil (qiyas awla)
The text provides a rational proof: since travel causes half the prayer (rak'ats) to be dropped, then reduction in recitation (an attribute) follows even more strongly. This is qiyas awla (a fortiori analogy).
The asl is the reduction of rak'ats; the far' is recitation.
4
Note the condition (takhsis from Hidayah)
Al-Marghinani adds: this reduction applies when the traveler is in haste. If he is at ease (aman wa qarar), he should recite medium surahs like 'Wa al-sama’i dhat al-buruj' and 'Idha al-sama’u inshaqqat'.
This shows that takhfif is not absolute but conditional.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon ruling: reduce recitation when in a hurry; otherwise recite medium Mufassal surahs to balance reduction and sunnah.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and confirmed by later Hanafi masters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفۃ الصلوة سے روایت کی ہے اور اس کے آخر میں ہے فلما نزل لصلاة الصبح صلى بهما صلاة الصبح للناس یعنی جب حضور نماز صبح کے لئے اترے تو لوگوں کو انہیں دونوں سورتوں کے ساتھ نماز پڑھائی۔ منقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نصف نماز ساقط کرنے میں سفر کو بہت بڑا دخل ہے جب سفر کونصف نماز ساقط کرنے میں دخل ہے تو قرآت کی تخفیف میں بدرجہ اولی دخل ہوگا۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب سفر کی وجہ سے اصل نماز میں کچھ کمی ہو گئی تو اس کے وصف یعنی قرآت میں بدرجہ اولی کمی ہوگی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس قدر تخفیف اس وقت ہے جب یہ شخص عجلت میں ہو اور اگر امن اور قرار کی حالت میں ہے مثلا کسی منزل پر شہر اور ارادہ یہ کہ اطمینان سے شہر کر روانہ ہو گا تو ایسی صورت میں فجر کی نماز میں و السماء ذات البروج اور اذا السماء انشقت پڑھے کیونکہ اس صورت میں تخفیف بھی ہوگئی اور سنت کی رعایت بھی ہوگئی۔
Chapter on Description of Prayer. It is narrated and at its end is: When he descended for the Fajr prayer, he led the people in Fajr prayer with those two surahs, meaning when the Prophet descended for Fajr prayer, he led the people in prayer with those two surahs. The naqli proof is that travel has a great effect in dropping half of the prayer. When travel has an effect in dropping half of the prayer, then in the reduction of recitation it will have an effect in the first degree. The conclusion is that when due to travel some reduction occurred in the original prayer, then in its attribute, i.e., recitation, reduction will occur in the first degree. The author of Hidayah says that this reduction is when the person is in haste. And if he is in a state of peace and settlement, for example, if he is at a station and intends to travel leisurely, then in such a case, in Fajr prayer, he should recite 'Wa al-sama’i dhat al-buruj' and 'Idha al-sama’u inshaqqat', because in this case reduction is also achieved and observance of sunnah is also achieved.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage begins with the chapter on the description of prayer. It first presents a hadith: when the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) descended for Fajr prayer, he led the people with two specific surahs (likely Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun and Qul huwa Allahu ahad, as known from other narrations). Then it provides a rational proof: since travel causes half of the prayer (rak'ats) to be dropped, then the reduction in recitation (one of its components) follows even more strongly. Therefore, the ruling is that in travel, Fajr recitation should be shortened. The author of Hidayah adds a condition: this reduction applies when the traveler is in haste. If he is settled and not in a rush, he should recite longer surahs like 'Wa al-sama’i dhat al-buruj' and 'Idha al-sama’u inshaqqat', as this still involves some reduction while also preserving the sunnah of reciting from the Mufassal section. The key point is that the extent of recitation in travel depends on the traveler's situation.

Key Terms
تخفیف (takhfif): Reduction in the quantity of recitation due to travel
سنت (sunnah): Recommended practice of the Prophet; leaving it is not sinful but is discouraged

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Only when the journey is on foot
D) Only when praying in congregation

Key Takeaway
In travel, Fajr recitation is reduced only when in haste; at ease, recite medium Mufassal surahs to balance reduction and sunnah.

Recitation Quantity in Fajr Prayer and Reconciling Varying Narrations
Ruling on Fajr recitation quantity with reconciliation of narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the amount of recitation in Fajr prayer for residents and explain how the various hadith narrations are reconciled based on the condition of the muqtadis.

Core Idea
The imam adjusts Fajr recitation length based on the congregation's eagerness, not a fixed number.

The amount of recitation in Fajr prayer for residents is a matter of divergent hadith narrations, ranging from forty to one hundred verses. The Hanafi school reconciles these by considering the nature of the followers (muqtadis) and other factors like seasonal variations. In this lesson, we examine the ruling, the evidence, and the method of tawfiq (reconciliation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The quantity of recitation in Fajr prayer for non-travelers. Determine the hukm level: the obligation of recitation itself is wajib, but the specific amount is sunnah muakkadah.
The matn gives the basic range: 40-50 verses per two rak'ats.
2
List the narrations and their ranges
The text mentions multiple narrations: 40-60, 60-100, and specific examples from the Prophet's practice (Surah al-Sajdah and Hal ata, Surah Qaf, and between 60 and 100). Identify each.
From Ibn Abbas: 30+31 verses; Jabir: Surah Qaf (~45); Abu Huraira: 60-100.
3
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for non-obligatory matters. The variation itself proves flexibility. Analyze the wajh al-dalalah: the Prophet's varying practice shows permissibility of different lengths.
Dalil type: Sunnah ahad; both thubut and dalala are zanni.
4
Apply wajh al-tawfiq
The author of Hidayah reconciles by considering the muqtadis: eager ones get longer recitation, lazy ones shorter, average in between. Also seasonal factors (night length) and occupations. This is the Hanafi method of harmonization.
This is a key usul technique: reconciling conflicting narrations by examining circumstances.
5
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
The mufta bihi is to recite 40-60 verses on average, with flexibility. The imam should gauge the congregation. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah, not fard.
This gives practical guidance for imams today.

Amount of recitation in Fajr prayer in residence: He recites in Fajr in the two rak'ats forty or fifty verses besides Surah al-Fatihah. And it is narrated from forty to sixty and from sixty to one hundred, and with all of these a tradition has come. And the way of reconciliation is that he recites with the eager ones one hundred, with the lazy ones forty, and with the average ones between fifty and sixty. Urdu translation: And in the state of residence in both rak'ats of Fajr, he recites forty or fifty verses besides Surah al-Fatihah. And it is narrated from forty to sixty and from sixty to one hundred, and on each a tradition is reported. The way of reconciliation is that with eager congregants he recites one hundred verses, with lazy ones forty, with average ones fifty to sixty. And it was said that he should look at the length and shortness of nights and the abundance and scarcity of occupations. Explanation: The issue is that in residence, in both rak'ats of Fajr, besides Surah al-Fatihah, he recites forty verses or fifty verses, i.e., twenty or twenty-five verses per rak'at. In one narration, from forty to sixty, and in another from sixty to one hundred. The author of Hidayah said that for each a tradition has come. Thus from Ibn Abbas (ra): The Prophet recited in Fajr on Friday 'Alif Lam Mim Tanzil al-Sajdah' and 'Hal ata ala al-insani'. The first surah has 30 verses, the second has 31. In Sahih Muslim from Jabir ibn Samurah: The Prophet used to recite in Fajr 'Qaf'. And from Abu Huraira: The Prophet recited in Fajr between sixty and one hundred verses. Reconciliation of different narrations: The author of Hidayah said that the way of reconciliation is that if the muqtadis are eager to hear recitation, he recites up to one hundred verses; if they are lazy, he recites forty; if middle, fifty to sixty. Some say consider the length and shortness of nights, i.e., in winter nights recite more, in summer less. And the imam should consider the abundance and scarcity of the muqtadis' occupations, i.e., if they are busy, he recites briefly.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage discusses the amount of recitation in Fajr prayer for residents (non-travelers). The matn states that the imam recites forty or fifty verses per two rak'ats beyond Surah al-Fatihah, but narrations vary from forty to sixty, or sixty to one hundred. The author reconciles these by considering the condition of the muqtadis: eager ones get more, lazy ones less, average in between. Additionally, the length of nights (winter vs. summer) and the occupations of the people are factors. The proof comes from multiple hadith: Ibn Abbas reports the Prophet recited long surahs like Alif Lam Mim Tanzil al-Sajdah (30+ ayat) and Hal ata (31 ayat) on Friday; Jabir reports recitation of Surah Qaf (about 45 ayat); Abu Huraira reports between sixty and a hundred. Thus, all are valid. The Hanafi position is that the imam has flexibility to choose based on the congregation's needs. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah, not fard, but the obligation of qira'ah is wajib.

Key Terms
وجہ توفیق (wajh al-tawfiq): Method of reconciling between different narrations by considering the context of the audience
مقتدی (muqtadi): A follower in congregational prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary factor in reconciling the different narrations?
A) The length of the surah
B) The condition of the muqtadis
C) The season
D) The imam's personal preference

Key Takeaway
The imam’s recitation length in Fajr is flexible, guided by the congregation's disposition and contextual factors, as proven by multiple hadith.

Recitation in Asr, Isha, and Maghrib: Mufassal Sections
Ruling with proof on recitation sections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi classification of recitation lengths for Asr, Isha, and Maghrib, identify the proof from Umar's letter, and explain the rationale behind the classification.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, Asr and Isha require middle Mufassal surahs; Maghrib requires short surahs — based on Umar's directive and the nature of each prayer.

This passage from the Hidayah specifies the recommended recitation lengths for Asr, Isha, and Maghrib prayers. While Fajr and Zuhr use the long section of the Mufassal, Asr and Isha use the middle, and Maghrib uses the short. The ruling is based on a directive from Umar (ra) and the practical consideration of time and ease. Understanding this classification helps the student apply the sunnah in salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for each prayer
Note the matn: Asr and Isha both use the middle of Mufassal (awsat al-mufassal); Maghrib uses the short (qisar al-mufassal). This is a sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the letter of Umar (ra) to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, which explicitly assigns the sections.
The letter is a sunnah ahad, zanni al-thubut but accepted in practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Umar's directive indicates the recommended practice; the word 'اقرأ' (recite) is a command but understood as istihbab (recommendation) due to other evidences.
4
Understand the rationale
Maghrib is based on haste, so short surahs; Asr and Isha have recommended delay, so medium surahs to avoid prolonging into disliked time.
The rationale strengthens the proof.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, an imam should choose surahs from the respective Mufassal sections. Violation does not invalidate the prayer but abandons the sunnah.

Source Text

And Asr and Isha are equal: in them one recites from the middle of Mufassal. And in Maghrib, less than that: one recites from the short of Mufassal. The origin in this is the letter of Umar to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: Recite in Fajr and Zuhr from the long of Mufassal, and in Asr and Isha from the middle of Mufassal, and in Maghrib from the short of Mufassal. And because Maghrib is based on haste and lightening, and Asr and Isha, delay is recommended therein, and if prolonged, they fall into a time that is not recommended, so they are restricted to the middle. Urdu translation: And Asr and Isha are equal; in both recite from the middle section of Mufassal. And in Maghrib, less than that; in Maghrib recite from the short section of Mufassal. The origin in this matter is the directive of Umar to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: Recite in Fajr and Zuhr from the long of Mufassal, in Asr and Isha from the middle of Mufassal, and in Maghrib from the short of Mufassal. And because Maghrib is based on haste, reduction is appropriate; and in Asr and Isha, delay is recommended, and if prolonged, they would fall into a disliked time, so they are confined to the middle. Explanation: Quduri said that in spacious time, Asr and Isha are equal, so in both, one recites from the middle of Mufassal.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage addresses the recitation in Asr, Isha, and Maghrib prayers. The matn states that Asr and Isha are similar: both use the middle of the Mufassal section (which is from Surah al-Buruj to the end? Actually the Mufassal is divided into three: long (tiwal: from Qaf to al-Mulk), middle (awsat: from al-Mulk to al-Bayyinah?), short (qisar: from al-Bayyinah to the end). But here it specifies: Fajr and Zuhr use the long (tiwal), Asr and Isha use the middle (awsat), Maghrib uses the short (qisar). This is based on the letter of Umar (radiyallahu anhu) to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. The rationale: Maghrib is brief by nature (due to haste), so very short surahs; Asr and Isha have recommended delay, so medium surahs; Fajr and Zuhr have more time, so longer surahs. The Hanafi position is to follow this classification. The proof is both the directive of Umar and the rational consideration of time and ease.

Key Terms
مفصل (Mufassal): The section of the Qur'an from Surah Qaf to the end, divided into long, middle, short
طوال مفصل (tiwal al-mufassal): Long surahs of Mufassal (from Qaf to al-Mulk?)
اوساط مفصل (awsat al-mufassal): Middle surahs of Mufassal (from al-Mulk to al-Bayyinah?)
قصار مفصل (qisar al-mufassal): Short surahs of Mufassal (from al-Bayyinah to the end)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, recitation in Asr and Isha should be from the middle Mufassal, and in Maghrib from the short Mufassal, based on a directive from Umar and the nature of each prayer.

Recitation in Zuhr Prayer: Similar to Fajr or Shorter?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Zuhr recitation length with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on Zuhr recitation amount and explain the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
Zuhr recitation may be shortened from Fajr to avoid congregational hardship.

In this lesson, we explore a nuanced intra-Hanafi difference. While the amount of recitation in Salah is generally a recommended practice (sunnah), the specific length for Zuhr prayer is debated between Imam Abu Hanifa and his student Imam Muhammad. Their disagreement reflects deeper principles about considering the congregation's circumstances, particularly their worldly occupations. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh evidence and apply fiqh in real-world leadership.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the specific fiqh question: How much should an imam recite in Zuhr prayer? This is a matter of sunnah, not obligation.
The two positions are about the preferred length, not validity.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa (in al-Asl) holds that Zuhr recitation should be similar to Fajr, because both prayers have equally spacious time. He cites hadith of the Prophet reciting similar surahs in both.
Equality of time is the key rationale.
3
Examine Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad (in al-Mabsut) prefers shorter recitation in Zuhr because it is a time when people are engaged in work. Prolonged recitation may cause boredom. He cites the Prophet's practice of reciting about thirty verses (like Surah al-Mulk).
Avoiding hardship (haraj) is the overriding principle.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is that an imam may choose to recite shorter surahs in Zuhr to accommodate busy congregations.
Both positions are valid; context determines preference.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view (following Imam Muhammad and later scholars like Al-Marghinani) is to shorten recitation in Zuhr to avoid hardship, though Abu Hanifa's view remains a strong alternative.
The principle of 'raf' al-haraj' (removing hardship) supports Imam Muhammad.

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on the description of prayer. It first states a general principle: the imam should consider the worldly occupations of his congregation when deciding the length of recitation. Then it specifically addresses the amount of recitation in Zuhr prayer. The text presents two positions within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa (reported in al-Asl) holds that Zuhr recitation should be like Fajr (e.g., Surah al-A'la or similar), because both have ample time. Imam Muhammad, in al-Mabsut, prefers a shorter recitation in Zuhr because it is a time when people are often engaged in work and may become bored if prayers are too long. The commentary supports this with hadith, such as the Prophet's practice of reciting 'Alif Lam Tanzil as-Sajda' in Zuhr and narrations about the number of verses. The rational argument (that Zuhr time is busy) is also cited. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and the mufta bihi depends on context, but the general principle of avoiding hardship is upheld.

Recitation in Asr, Isha (Medium) and Maghrib (Short)
Specifies recommended recitation lengths for Asr, Isha, and Maghrib prayers based on Umar's letter and prophetic practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi recommended recitation lengths for Asr, Isha, and Maghrib prayers, identify the primary evidence (Umar's letter), and explain the rational basis for these distinctions.

Core Idea
Maghrib's short recitation reflects its haste; Asr and Isha's medium recitation balances time and completeness.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on how much Quran to recite in the sunset (Maghrib), late afternoon (Asr), and night (Isha) prayers. The school prescribes specific portions of the Mufassal section (short surahs at the end of the Quran) for these prayers, based on the practice of the Caliph Umar and the Sunnah of the Prophet. Understanding this ruling helps an imam lead prayer in the most recommended manner, avoiding excessive prolongation or undue shortening.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings for each prayer
The passage states that in Asr and Isha, one should recite from medium Mufassal, and in Maghrib from short Mufassal. Note that these are recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory.
The prayer is valid even with different recitation, but following the sunnah is better.
2
Examine the primary evidence: Umar's letter
The text cites the letter of Caliph Umar to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari as the origin of this classification. Umar directly commands: 'Recite in Fajr and Zuhr from long Mufassal, in Asr and Isha from medium Mufassal, and in Maghrib from short Mufassal.'
Hanafis consider this letter authoritative as it reflects the Prophet's sunnah.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
Two hadiths support the ruling: Jabir ibn Samurah reports the Prophet recited specific surahs (e.g., al-Buruj) in Asr; Mu'adh's incident shows the Prophet advised shorter recitation in Isha. These indicate moderate length.
These hadiths confirm that the recitation should not be too long in these prayers.
4
Understand the rational argument
Maghrib is based on haste (due to its short time window), so shortening is appropriate. Asr and Isha have a recommended delay, and prolonged recitation could push them into a disliked time, hence medium recitation is prescribed.
This rational consideration (istihsan) complements the textual proof.
5
Apply to practice
A Hanafi imam should classify surahs into long, medium, and short Mufassal and choose accordingly. For Asr and Isha, surahs like al-Buruj to al-Bayyinah; for Maghrib, surahs from al-Bayyinah to the end.
If unsure, any Quranic recitation is valid, but following the sunnah is optimal.

کرے۔ دلیل جابر بن سمرہ کی روایت ہے ان النبی صلی الله عليه وسلم كان يقرأ في الركعتين الأوليين من العصرو السماء ذات البروج والسماء والطارق یعنی حضور عصر کی پہلی دو رکعت میں و السماء ذات البروج اور والسماء والطارق پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ اور دوسری دلیل معاذ بن جبل رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث ہے ان قومـه شـكـوا الى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم تطويل قرائته فى العشاء فقال له النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم افتان انت يا معاذ این انت من سبح اسم ربک الاعلى والشمس وضحها يعنى معاذ بن جبل رضی اللہ عنہ کی قوم نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے شکایت کی کہ معاذ عشاء کی نماز میں تطویل قرآت کرتے ہیں تو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے معاذ سے کہا کہ اے معاذ کیا تو لوگوں کو مبتلائے فتنہ کرنا چاہتا ہے کہاں ہے تو سبح اسم ربک الاعلی اور والشمس وضحها سے یعنی تو ان سورتوں کو کیوں نہیں پڑھتا بہر حال یہ دونوں روایتیں اس بات پر دلالت کرتی ہیں کہ عصر اور عشاء میں اوساط مفصل میں سے قرآت کرنا مستحب اور اولی ہے۔ اور مغرب کی نماز میں قصار مفصل کے ساتھ قرآت کرے اور دلیل یہ روایت ہے انه عليه السلام قرأ في صلاة المغرب بالمعوذتین یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مغرب کی نماز میں معوذتین کی قرآت کی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ تمام نمازوں کی مستحب قرآت کے بارے میں اصل وہ فرمان ہے جو خلیفہ ثانی امیر المؤمنین سیدنا عمر بن الخطاب رضی اللہ عنہ نے ابو موسیٰ اشعری رضی اللہ عنہ کے نام بھیجا تھا ۔ ان اقرأ في الفجر والظهر بطوال المفصل وفي العصر والعشاء باوساط المفصل وفى المغرب بقصار المفصل یعنی ظہر اور فجر میں طوال مفصل میں سے پڑھ اور عصر اور عشاء میں اوساط مفصل اور مغرب میں قصار مفصل پڑھ ۔ عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مغرب کا مبنی ثبت اور جلدی پر ہے اور عجلت کے مناسب تخفیف ہے۔ اور عصر اور عشاء میں تا خیر مستحب ہے پس اگران میں طویل قرآت شروع کر دی گئی تو یہ دونوں نمازیں غیر مستحب وقت میں واقع ہوں گی ۔ اس لئے ان دونوں نمازوں میں اوساط مفصل کا تعین کیا گیا۔
And Asr and Isha are equal: one recites in them from the medium of Mufassal. And in Maghrib, less than that: one recites in it from the short of Mufassal. The basis for this is the letter of Umar to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: 'Recite in Fajr and Zuhr from the long of Mufassal, and in Asr and Isha from the medium of Mufassal, and in Maghrib from the short of Mufassal.' And because the foundation of Maghrib is on haste and lightening... And Asr and Isha, delaying is recommended, and they may fall by prolonging into a non-recommended time, so they are limited to medium. Translation: And Asr and Isha are equal; one recites in them from medium Mufassal. And in Maghrib less than that; one recites short Mufassal. The basis is the command of Umar to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Commentary: Al-Quduri said that Asr and Isha are equal in spaciousness of time, so they recite medium Mufassal. Proof: Hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah that the Prophet recited in the first two rak'ahs of Asr 'Wa as-sama'i dhat al-buruj' and 'Wa as-sama'i wa at-tariq'. Second proof: Hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal that his people complained about his long recitation in Isha, so the Prophet said, 'O Mu'adh, are you causing tribulation? Why don't you recite 'Sabbi isma rabbika al-a'la' and 'Wa ash-shamsi wa duhaha'?' These narrations indicate that reciting medium Mufassal in Asr and Isha is recommended. In Maghrib, recite short Mufassal, proof: the Prophet recited al-Mu'awwidhatain in Maghrib. The author of al-Hidayah said the principle is the letter of Umar. Rational proof: Maghrib is based on haste...
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage details the recommended recitation lengths for Asr (late afternoon), Isha (night), and Maghrib (sunset) prayers. For Asr and Isha, the recommended (mustahabb) recitation is from the 'medium Mufassal' (awsat al-mufassal), while for Maghrib, it is from the 'short Mufassal' (qisar al-mufassal). The primary authority cited is the letter of Caliph Umar ibn al-Khattab to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, which explicitly prescribes these categories. Additional hadith evidence includes the Prophet's practice in Asr and Mu'adh's incident in Isha, which show that recitation should not be too long. The rational argument (dalil aqli) explains that Maghrib is built on haste (due to its short time window), so shortening is appropriate; Asr and Isha have a recommended delay, so if recitation is too long, they may slip into a disliked time. Therefore, medium recitation is prescribed for them.

Key Terms
أوساط المفصل (awsaṭ al-mufaṣṣal): The medium portion of Mufassal (the short surahs at the end of the Quran), typically from Surah al-Buruj to Surah Lam Yakun (according to one definition).
قصار المفصل (qiṣār al-mufaṣṣal): The short portion of Mufassal, from Surah Lam Yakun (or al-Bayyinah) to the end of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the Hanafi ruling that Asr and Isha recitation should be from medium Mufassal?
A) A direct Quranic command
B) The letter of Caliph Umar to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari
C) Consensus of all scholars
D) A hadith from the Prophet in Sahih Muslim

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes medium Mufassal for Asr and Isha, and short Mufassal for Maghrib, based on Umar's letter and the principles of time management in prayer.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
