The View that Congregational Prayer is Wajib: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute over jama'ah ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of jama'ah and evaluate the strength of the evidence for each position.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, the ruling of congregational prayer is disputed: the majority and an isolated transmission from Imam Muhammad say it is wajib, but the relied-upon position is sunnah mu'akkadah.

In this lesson, we explore an internal Hanafi dispute about the legal status of congregational prayer. While the author of Al-Hidayah and the authoritative texts (zahir al-riwayah) hold that jama'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah, Imam Muhammad himself, in a non-core transmission, and the majority of later Hanafi scholars consider it wajib. The evidence centers on the famous hadith of the Prophet's intention to burn houses of those who miss the congregation. Understanding this dispute illuminates how the Hanafi school weighs different transmissions and how a ruling can have strong practical implications even when not the official position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The passage presents two views within the Hanafi school: jama'ah as sunnah mu'akkadah (official zahir al-riwayah) and as wajib (Imam Muhammad's non-core transmission and majority).
2
Examine the evidence for the wajib view
The proof is the hadith of burning houses. Note the interpretation: it refers to missing congregation, not the prayer itself.
The hadith is narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the authority weight
The sunnah mu'akkadah view comes from the core six books; the wajib view from a non-core source (ghayr riwayat al-usul). Yet the majority accepts it.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if wajib, missing congregation without excuse is a sin; if sunnah, it is a loss of great reward. The mufta bihi is sunnah, but the majority view leads to strong recommendation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حضرت امام محمد نے غیر روایت اصول میں ذکر کیا کہ جماعت واجب ہے۔ احناف میں سے عامتہ المشائخ اس کے قائل ہیں۔ دلیل حضور کا یہ قول ہے لقد هممت ان امر بالمؤذن فيؤذن ثم آمر رجلا فيصلي بالناس ثم انطلق برجال معهم حزم الحطب الى قوم يتخلفون عن الصلوة فاحرق عليهم بيوتهم بالنار، رواه الشيخان یعنی حضور اقدس صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ میں نے ارادہ کیا کہ مؤذن کو حکم دوں کہ وہ اذان پڑھے پھر ایک مرد کو حکم دوں کہ وہ لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائے پھر کچھ لوگوں کو لے کر جن کے ساتھ لکڑیوں کے گھڑ ہوں ایسی قوم کی طرف چلوں جو نماز سے پیچھے رہ جاتی ہے پھر آگ سے ان کے گھروں کو جلا دوں اس حدیث میں بالکلیہ نماز کا ترک کرنا مراد نہیں بلکہ جماعت کا
Imam Muhammad mentioned in a non-Zahir al-Riwayah source that congregational prayer is obligatory (wajib). The generality of Hanafi scholars (jumhur) are of this view. The proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'I intended to order the muezzin to give the adhan, then order a man to lead the people in prayer, then go with men carrying bundles of firewood to the people who lag behind from the prayer and burn their houses with fire.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. That is, the Holy Prophet (peace be upon him) said: I intended that... [interpretation] In this hadith, the complete abandonment of prayer is not intended, but rather congregational prayer.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal status of congregational prayer. The author (sahib al-Hidayah) previously stated that jama'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah, which is the position of the zahir al-riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad). However, here it is mentioned that Imam Muhammad himself, in a non-Zahir al-Riwayah source (ghayr riwayat al-usul), stated that jama'ah is wajib (obligatory). Moreover, the majority of Hanafi scholars (jumhur) hold this view. The proof cited is the famous hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) where he intended to burn the houses of those who missed the congregational prayer. The threat of burning indicates that missing jama'ah is a major sin, and the punishment is severe. The text interprets this hadith not as referring to complete abandonment of prayer (i.e., not praying at all), but specifically to missing the congregational prayer. This interpretation strengthens the argument that jama'ah is obligatory. The dispute is significant: while the official Hanafi position is that jama'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah, many scholars, including Imam Muhammad in one narration, consider it wajib. This shows that the term 'wajib' in Hanafi fiqh is sometimes applied to sunnah mu'akkadah in certain contexts, but here it is presented as a distinct view. The student should note the authority weight: the sunnah mu'akkadah view is from the zahir al-riwayah (the more authoritative source), while the wajib view is from ghayr riwayat al-usul (a less authoritative transmission). Nevertheless, the text mentions that the majority of Hanafi scholars accept the wajib view, indicating that in practice, jama'ah is treated with near-obligatory importance.

Key Terms
غیر روایت اصول (ghayr riwayat al-usul): A transmission that is not from the six core books of Imam Muhammad (the Zahir al-Riwayah); it is considered of lesser authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the primary evidence for the view that congregational prayer is wajib?
A) The hadith 'الجماعة من سنن الهدى'
B) The hadith of burning houses
C) The hadith of 25 degrees reward
D) Consensus of all scholars

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds two views on jama'ah, but the mufta bihi is sunnah mu'akkadah, though the majority and strong evidence support wajib.

The Ruling of Congregational Prayer: Sunnah Mu'akkadah with Proofs
States the ruling of congregational prayer as sunnah mu'akkadah with proofs and responses to opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer, identify its key proofs, and explain the differences between the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Hanbali positions on the matter.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah that cannot be abandoned without excuse, based on the Prophet's hadith.

In this lesson, we delve into the opening of the chapter on imamate from Ashraf al-Hidayah. The text establishes the legal status of congregational prayer within the Hanafi school and presents the primary evidence. It also addresses internal Hanafi differences and critiques the positions of other madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Congregational prayer (al-jama'ah). What is the hukm level? Sunnah mu'akkadah.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is a distinct category in Hanafi fiqh, between wajib and nafl.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The text cites the hadith 'al-jama'atu min sunan al-huda' and later the hadith of burning houses.
The hadith of burning houses is used by those who consider it wajib.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The Prophet's severe warning (intention to burn houses) indicates that abandoning congregation is a major sin, making it a confirmed sunnah that cannot be left without excuse.
The warning outweighs the mere recommendation of a regular sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi: Imam Muhammad and many mashayikh say wajib. Inter-madhhab: Ahmad and Dawud say fard 'ayn; al-Karkhi, al-Tahawi, and most Shafi'is say fard kifayah.
The passage dismisses the fard kifayah argument as weak.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is sunnah mu'akkadah, but with the understanding that it is not to be taken lightly. The text states that if a city abandons it, they are to be commanded and even fought.
This shows the practical emphasis despite the ruling level.

باب الإمامة
(یہ) باب امامت کے (احکام کے بیان میں) ہے جماعت کی شرعی حیثیت
الجماعة سنة مؤكدة لقوله عليه السلام الجماعة من سنن الهدى لا يتخلف عنها الا منافق
ترجمہ: جماعت سنت مؤکدہ ہے کیونکہ حضور نے فرمایا کہ جماعت سنن الهدى میں سے ہے اس سے نہیں بچھڑے گا مگر منافق۔
تشریح: مصنف علیہ الرحمۃ نے سابق میں امام کے افعال کا ذکر کیا ہے یعنی وجوب جہر اور وجوب اختفاء اور تحدید قرآت اور مقتدی کے افعال کو ذکر کیا یعنی وجوب استماع اور انسات کو اب یہاں سے مشروعیت امامت کی صفت کا بیان ہے چنانچہ سب سے پہلے مستحق امامت کا ذکر کیا اس کے بعد امامت کے خواص کا بیان ہے۔
جماعت سنت مؤکدہ ہے کیونکہ حضور نے فرمایا کہ جماعت سنن الهدى میں سے ہے اس سے منافق ہی پیچھے رہتا ہے۔
سنت کی دو قسمیں ہیں ایک سنت الهدى، دوم سنت زائد۔ سنت الهدى وہ ہے جس پر نبی کریم نے بطریق عبادت مواظبت فرمائی مگر کبھی کبھار ترک کے ساتھ اس کا ترک کرنا ضلالت ہے اور یہ شعائر اسلام میں سے ہے۔ اور سنت زائد وہ ہے جس کو آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بطریق عادت کیا ہو اس کے ترک کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ جیسے تہجد کی نماز۔
بہر حال جماعت سنت مؤکدہ ہے بغیر عذر کے اس کا ترک کرنا جائز نہیں حتیٰ کہ اگر اہل شہر نے جماعت کو ترک کر دیا تو ان کو اقامت جماعت کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔ اگر انہوں نے اس پر عمل کیا فیها ورنہ ان سے قتال کرنا حلال ہوگا۔
جماعت کے سنت مؤکدہ ہونے کی تائید ان احادیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے جو جماعت کی فضیلت میں وارد ہوئی ہیں۔ چنانچہ حضور فرمایا: صلاة الجماعة افضل من صلاة أحدكم وحده بخمسة وعشرين درجة یعنی جماعت سے نماز پڑھنا بہ نسبت تنہا نماز پڑھنے کے پچیس درجہ افضل ہے۔ اور ایک روایت میں ہے کہ ۲۷ درجہ افضل ہے۔
امام ابوداؤد، ترمذی اور ابن ماجہ نے ابی بن کعب کی حدیث روایت کی: صلاة الرجل مع الرجل ازكى من صلاته وحده، وصلاة الرجل مع الرجلين ازكى من صلاته مع رجل، وما زاد فهو أحب إلى اللہ تعالی یعنی دو مردوں کا جماعت سے نماز پڑھنا افضل ہے اور تین کی جماعت دو کی جماعت سے بہتر ہے اور جو زیادہ ہو اللہ کو زیادہ پسند ہے۔
حضرت امام محمد نے غیر روایت اصول میں ذکر کیا کہ جماعت واجب ہے۔ احناف میں سے عامۃ المشائخ اس کے قائل ہیں۔ دلیل حضور کا یہ قول ہے: لقد هممت ان امر بالمؤذن فيؤذن ثم آمر رجلا فيصلي بالناس ثم انطلق برجال معهم حزم الحطب إلى قوم يتخلفون عن الصلاة فاحرق عليهم بيوتهم بالنار، رواه الشيخان یعنی حضور اقدس نے فرمایا کہ میں نے ارادہ کیا کہ مؤذن کو حکم دوں کہ وہ اذان پڑھے پھر ایک مرد کو حکم دوں کہ وہ لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائے پھر کچھ لوگوں کو لے کر جن کے ساتھ لکڑیوں کے گٹھے ہوں ایسی قوم کی طرف چلوں جو نماز سے پیچھے رہ جاتی ہے پھر آگ سے ان کے گھروں کو جلا دوں۔ اس حدیث میں بالکلیہ نماز کا ترک کرنا مراد نہیں بلکہ جماعت کا ترک کرنا مراد ہے۔
امام احمد بن حنبل اور داؤد ظاہری کہتے ہیں کہ جماعت فرض عین ہے۔ یہ حضرات استدلال کرتے ہیں: لا صلاة لجار المسجد إلا في المسجد، حتی قال ابن عباس: تعني لا صلاة كاملة. ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں صلوۃ کاملہ کی نفی کی گئی ہے جیسے لا صلاة للعبد الآبق ولا للمرأة الناشز۔ قرآن کے زیادہ جائے میں نماز کاملہ کی نفی کی گئی ہے۔
امام کرخی، امام طحاوی اور اکثر اصحاب شافعی کے نزدیک جماعت فرض کفایہ ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقصود فرض العلم میں تعارض ہو جائے؟ شعائر اسلام کا اظہار ہے اور یہ مقصود بعض کے فعل سے حاصل ہو جاتا ہے۔ مگر یہ استدلال انتہائی کمزور ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے عہد مبارک میں مسجد میں جماعت ہوتی تھی اس کے باوجود آپ نے تارکین جماعت کے لئے سخت وعید فرمائی ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔ جمیل احمد
Chapter of Imamate
(This) chapter is about the rulings of imamate. The legal status of congregation: Congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Congregation is from the sunan of guidance; only a hypocrite lags behind it.'
Translation: Congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah because the Prophet said that congregation is from the sunan of guidance; only a hypocrite lags behind it.
Explanation: The author (may Allah have mercy on him) previously mentioned the actions of the imam—i.e., the obligation of reciting aloud and the obligation of reciting silently, and the determination of recitation—and the actions of the follower—i.e., the obligation of listening and being silent. Now from here, the description of the legitimacy of the imam's quality is explained. Thus, first he mentions who deserves the imamate, then the characteristics of imamate.
Congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah because the Prophet said that congregation is from the sunan of guidance; only a hypocrite lags behind it.
Sunnah is of two types: one is sunnat al-huda (sunnah of guidance), the second is sunnah za'idah (additional sunnah). Sunnat al-huda is that upon which the Prophet consistently performed as an act of worship, though occasionally he omitted it; abandoning it is error, and it is from the symbols of Islam. Sunnah za'idah is that which the Prophet (peace be upon him) did habitually; there is no harm in abandoning it. Like the tahajjud prayer.
In any case, congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah. Abandoning it without a valid excuse is not permissible. Even if the people of a city abandon congregation, they will be commanded to establish it. If they act upon it, fine; otherwise, fighting them becomes permissible.
The confirmation of congregational prayer being a confirmed sunnah is also supported by the hadiths that have come regarding its merit. Thus, the Prophet said: 'The prayer in congregation is superior to the prayer of any one of you alone by twenty-five degrees.' That is, praying in congregation is twenty-five degrees more excellent than praying alone. In another narration, it is twenty-seven degrees.
Imams Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah narrated from Ubayy ibn Ka'b: 'The prayer of a man with another man is purer than his prayer alone, and the prayer of a man with two men is purer than his prayer with one man, and the more people the more beloved to Allah Almighty.' That is, two men praying in congregation is better, and the congregation of three is better than that of two, and the more numerous, the more beloved to Allah.
Imam Muhammad mentioned in a non-zahir al-riwayah source that congregational prayer is wajib. The general mashayikh of the Hanafis are of this view. Their proof is the saying of the Prophet: 'I intended to command the caller to give the adhan, then command a man to lead the people in prayer, then set out with men carrying bundles of firewood to a people who stay away from the prayer and burn their houses down with fire'—narrated by the two Shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim). That is, the Prophet said: I intended to order the mu'adhdhin to give the adhan, then order a man to lead the people in prayer, then go with some men who have bundles of firewood to a people who lag behind from prayer and burn their houses with fire. In this hadith, abandoning prayer entirely is not meant, rather abandoning congregation is meant.
Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal and Dawud al-Zahiri say that congregational prayer is fard 'ayn (individual obligation). These scholars adduce the hadith: 'There is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque,' to the extent that Ibn Abbas said: meaning no complete prayer. Our answer is that the hadith negates complete prayer, just as 'no prayer for the runaway slave and no prayer for the disobedient wife' negate complete prayer. In many places of the Quran, complete prayer is negated.
Imam al-Karkhi, Imam al-Tahawi, and most Shafi'i scholars hold that congregational prayer is fard kifayah (communal obligation). Their proof is that the purpose is the manifestation of the symbols of Islam, and this purpose is achieved by the action of some. But this argumentation is extremely weak because in the blessed era of the Prophet (peace be upon him), congregation was held in the mosque, yet he gave a severe warning against those who abandon it. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah opens the chapter on imamate (leading prayer) by establishing the legal ruling of congregational prayer (al-jama'ah) in the Hanafi school. The text begins by stating clearly that congregation is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah), citing the Prophet's hadith that it is from the 'sunan al-huda' (guidance practices) that only a hypocrite abandons. The author then explains the two categories of sunnah: sunnat al-huda, which is consistently performed by the Prophet and whose abandonment without excuse is sinful, and sunnah za'idah, which is habitual and may be omitted without harm. Congregation belongs to the first category, meaning it is not merely recommended but is a strong practice that cannot be abandoned without valid excuse, even to the extent that if a city completely abandons it, the authorities should compel it and even fight if necessary.

The text then brings supporting hadiths about the merit of congregation (25 or 27 degrees superior to individual prayer) and the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b showing that more participants is better. Then it addresses the internal Hanafi difference: Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) and many later Hanafi mashayikh consider congregation wajib (obligatory), citing the famous hadith where the Prophet intended to burn the houses of those who stay away from congregation. The text clarifies that this hadith refers to abandoning congregation, not abandoning prayer entirely.

The passage then presents the inter-madhhab dispute: Imam Ahmad and Dawud al-Zahiri consider it fard 'ayn (individual obligation), arguing from the hadith 'la salata li-jar al-masjid illa fi al-masjid' (no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque). The Hanafi response, following the majority, interprets this as a negation of perfect prayer, not its validity. The Shafi'i majority and Hanafi scholars like al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi consider it fard kifayah (communal obligation). The Hanafi text dismisses this as weak, because the strong warning against abandonment contradicts the notion that it is merely a communal obligation that can be dropped if some fulfill it. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that congregation is sunnah mu'akkadah, though the severe warning indicates it must not be taken lightly.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): Congregational prayer, consisting of at least an imam and a follower.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah that the Prophet continuously performed and rarely omitted; its abandonment without excuse is disliked and considered sinful.
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An individual obligation that every qualified Muslim must perform; failure to do so is sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of congregational prayer in the Hanafi school (the main position)?
A) Fard 'ayn
B) Fard kifayah
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Congregational prayer in the Hanafi school is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) that carries the weight of an obligation in terms of emphasis, and its abandonment without excuse is a sinful act.

Qualifications of the Imam: Knowledge of Sunnah vs. Quran Recitation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imam qualifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on imam qualifications, explain Abu Yusuf's counter-argument, and apply the tarjih to determine the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The imam's knowledge of prayer rulings outweighs superior recitation alone.

When choosing a prayer leader, should we prioritize deep knowledge of fiqh or perfect Quran recitation? This passage presents an intra-Hanafi debate: Imam Abu Hanifa argues that comprehensive knowledge of the sunnah (the rulings of prayer) is more essential, while his student Abu Yusuf contends that recitation is needed in every prayer and knowledge only occasionally. By examining their proofs and the supporting hadith, we will see why the school ultimately sides with Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Recognize that Imam Abu Hanifa holds the one with more knowledge of sunnah (a'lamuhum bi al-sunnah) is most deserving, while Abu Yusuf holds the one with better recitation (aqra'uhum) is preferred.
Both require basic competence in the other area.
2
Examine the proofs
Abu Yusuf argues recitation is an indispensable pillar in every rakah, while knowledge is only needed when an incident invalidates the prayer. The Hanafi response counters that recitation serves only one pillar, whereas knowledge is required for all pillars and for correcting any issues.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on necessity.
3
Analyze the hadith support
The text cites a hadith from al-Hakim that places afqahuhum fi al-din (most understanding of religion) before aqra'uhum, explicitly favoring knowledge over recitation when other qualities are equal.
This hadith strengthens Abu Hanifa's position.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, preferring the one with superior knowledge of the sunnah (fiqh of prayer).
Abu Yusuf's view is acknowledged but not operative for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان تساووا فاقرؤهم كان اقرأهم
وترجمہ: پھر اگر کتاب اللہ کا بہتر قاری ہو وہ اولیٰ ہے۔
اور اولى الناس بالامامة اعلمهم بالسنة وعن أبي يوسف اقرؤهم لان القراءة لابد منها والحاجة الى العلم انما تظهر عند نائبة
ترجمہ: اور جو شخص جماعت والوں میں سے سنت کا زیادہ عالم ہو وہ امامت کے لئے اولیٰ ہے اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ ان میں جو اقراء ہو وہ اولیٰ ہے کیونکہ قرآت نماز کے لئے ضروری ہے اور علم کی حاجت اس وقت ہے جب کوئی واقعہ پیش آئے۔
ونحن نقول القراءة مفتقر اليها لركن واحد والعلم لسائر الاركان
ترجمہ: اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ قرآت کی جانب احتیاج ایک رکن کے لئے ہے اور علم کی احتیاج تمام ارکان کے لئے ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امامت کا سب سے زیادہ مستحق وہ شخص ہے جو سنت کا زیادہ جانے والا ہو یعنی ان احکام شرعیہ کا جانے والا ہو جو نماز کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں مثلا نماز کی شرطیں، نماز کے ارکان، نماز کی سنتیں اور اس کے آداب بشرطیکہ ما يجزئ به الصلاة قرأت پر قدرت رکھتا ہو۔
امام ابو یوسف سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ امامت کا زیادہ مستحق وہ ہوگا جو قرآت قرآن میں سب سے اچھا ہوگا بشرطیکہ بقدر ضرورت علم رکھتا ہو۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآت نماز کا ایک ایسا رکن ہے جس کے بغیر چارہ نہیں اور علم کی ضرورت اس وقت پیش آئے گی جب کہ کوئی عارض مفسد پیش آئے تاکہ علم کے ذریعہ نماز کو درست کر سکے۔ اور عارض نماز کے اندر بھی پیش آتا ہے اور کبھی پیش نہیں آتا۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ قرآت کا علم زیادہ ضروری ہے اس لئے اقرأ کو اعلم بالسنۃ پر مقدم کیا گیا۔
لیکن ہم طرفین کی طرف سے جواب یہ دیں گے کہ قرآت کی جانب احتیاج فقط ایک رکن کے لئے ہے اور علم کی طرف احتیاج تمام ارکان کے لئے ہے کیونکہ نماز کو فاسد کرنے والی چیزوں کی معرفت بھی علم کے ذریعہ ہوگی اور نماز کو درست کرنے والی چیزوں کی معرفت بھی علم کے ذریعہ ہوگی۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ علم کی ضرورت نسبت قرآت کے زیادہ ہے اس لئے اعلم بالسنۃ کو اقرأ پر ترجیح دی گئی۔
طرفین کے قول کی تائید حاکم کی روایت سے بھی ہوتی ہے حضور نے فرمایا: يؤم القوم أقدمهم هجرة، فإن كانوا في الهجرة سواء فافقههم في الدين، فإن كانوا في الفقه سواء فاقرأهم للقرآن
(شرح نقایہ)
یعنی قوم کی امامت وہ کرے جو ہجرت میں مقدم ہو پس اگر ہجرت میں سب برابر ہوں تو افقہ فی الدین امامت کرے اور اگر فقہ میں سب برابر ہوں تو اقرأ للقرآن امامت کرے۔ اس حدیث میں افقہ فی الدین یعنی اعلم کو اقرأ پر مقدم کیا گیا ہے۔
حضرت انس رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث ہے: ان الذين جمعوا القرآن على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اربعة [؟] ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ دوسرے اعترات [؟]
Then if they are equal, then the one who is most reciter (aqra'uhum) is the one with best recitation.
Translation: Then if (they are equal) then the better reciter of the Book of Allah, he is more deserving.
And the most deserving of people for imamate is the one with most knowledge of sunnah, and from Abu Yusuf it is narrated: the one with best recitation, because recitation is indispensable, and the need for knowledge only appears when an incident occurs.
Translation: And the person among the congregation who is most knowledgeable of the sunnah, he is more deserving for imamate. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that among them the one with best recitation is more deserving, because recitation is necessary for prayer, and the need for knowledge is only when an incident occurs.
And we say: recitation is needed for one pillar, and knowledge for the rest of the pillars.
Translation: And we say that the need for recitation is for one pillar, and the need for knowledge is for all pillars.
Explanation of the issue: The most deserving of imamate is the person who is most knowledgeable of the sunnah, i.e., knowledgeable of the legal rulings related to prayer, such as the conditions, pillars, sunnahs, and etiquettes of prayer, provided he has the ability to recite that which is sufficient for prayer.
From Imam Abu Yusuf, there is a narration that the most deserving of imamate is the one who is best in Quran recitation, provided he has sufficient knowledge.
Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that recitation is a pillar of prayer without which there is no alternative, and the need for knowledge arises only when an invalidating incident occurs so that through knowledge he can correct the prayer. An incident may occur during prayer or may not. So it is clear that knowledge of recitation is more necessary; therefore, the one with best recitation is given priority over the one with most knowledge of sunnah.
But we, from both sides, will give this answer: that the need for recitation is only for one pillar, and the need for knowledge is for all pillars, because the knowledge of things that invalidate prayer and things that correct prayer both come through knowledge. So it is established that the need for knowledge is greater than the need for recitation; therefore, the one with most knowledge of sunnah is given preference over the one with best recitation.
The sayings of both sides are also supported by the narration of al-Hakim: the Prophet said: 'The one who leads the people in prayer should be the one with the most advanced hijrah (migration); if they are equal in hijrah, then the one with most understanding of religion (afqahuhum fi al-din); if they are equal in understanding, then the one with best recitation of the Quran.' (Sharh al-Niqayah)
That is, the one who is foremost in hijrah should lead; if they are equal in hijrah, then the one with most understanding in religion should lead; if they are equal in understanding, then the one with best recitation of the Quran should lead. In this hadith, understanding in religion (i.e., knowledge) is given priority over recitation.
The hadith of Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Those who collected the Quran in the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) were four [؟]' and the rule is that other objections [؟]
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage addresses the qualifications for leading congregational prayer. The main Hanafi position, attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, is that the person most deserving to lead prayer is the one with the most knowledge of the sunnah (a'lamuhum bi al-sunnah), i.e., deep understanding of the rulings of prayer (fiqh). This includes conditions, pillars, sunnahs, and etiquettes, provided he can recite enough Quran for the prayer to be valid. The text then presents a narration from Abu Yusuf who preferred the one with the best Quran recitation (aqra'uhum), arguing that recitation is an indispensable pillar in every prayer, while knowledge of fiqh is only needed occasionally when something goes wrong. The Hanafi response (wahna naqool) counters that recitation is needed for only one pillar (qira'ah), whereas knowledge (fiqh) is needed for all pillars and for correcting any issues that arise during prayer. Therefore, knowledge is more essential overall. The passage then supports Abu Hanifa's view with a hadith from al-Hakim where the Prophet prioritized understanding (fiqh) over recitation. This hadith explicitly places the one with more fiqh ahead of the one with better recitation when they are equal in other qualities. Thus, the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that knowledge of the sunnah (fiqh of prayer) is the primary qualification for an imam.

Key Terms
أولى الناس بالإمامة (awla al-nas bi al-imamah): The person most entitled to lead the congregational prayer.
اعلمهم بالسنة (a'lamuhum bi al-sunnah): The one with the most knowledge of the prophetic practice, particularly the rulings of prayer (fiqh).
اقرؤهم (aqra'uhum): The one with the best Quran recitation, including proper tajweed and memorization.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The one with the most beautiful voice
B) The one who is oldest
C) The one with more knowledge of the sunnah (fiqh of prayer)
D) The one who has memorized the most Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes the imam's comprehensive knowledge of prayer rulings over superior recitation, supported by the hadith that places understanding (fiqh) before recitation.

Criteria for Imamate: Knowledge vs. Recitation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imamate priorities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on who should lead prayer, explain Abu Yusuf's alternative view, and apply the tarjih mechanism to resolve the dispute.

Core Idea
Knowledge of prayer's rules takes precedence over mere recitation skill because knowledge covers all pillars, recitation only one.

Who should lead the prayer: the one who knows the most fiqh or the one with the best voice? This lesson explores a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on this question. The passage from Al-Hidayah presents the primary ruling and the reasoning that leads to the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing qualifications
The matn states the preferred imam is 'the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah' (اعلمهم بالسنة). Abu Yusuf transmits a view preferring 'the best reciter' (اقرؤهم). Note the key terms: knowledge vs. recitation.
The dispute is about priority, not validity; both candidates are qualified, but we must choose the more deserving.
2
Analyze the proofs for each position
Abu Yusuf's proof: recitation is indispensable (لابد منها) in every prayer, while knowledge is only needed when an unexpected issue occurs. Abu Hanifa's proof: recitation is needed for only one pillar (the Qur'an recitation itself), whereas knowledge of the Sunnah is needed for all pillars (conditions, integrals, nullifiers). Thus knowledge is more comprehensive and deserves priority.
The Hanafi response uses quantitative reasoning: one pillar vs. all pillars.
3
Examine the hadith cited
The text cites the hadith: 'The one who recites most should lead; if equal, then the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah.' This appears to prioritize recitation. But the commentator clarifies that among the Companions, the best reciters were also most knowledgeable because they learned the Quran with its rulings.
This is a key contextual argument: the hadith's application is now different.
4
Understand the tarjih
Because in later times the best reciter may not be the most knowledgeable, we revert to the principle that knowledge is more essential. Thus the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is Abu Hanifa's: the most knowledgeable in Sunnah should lead.
This is a common pattern in Hanafi fiqh: contextual factors can shift the application of a general ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإمامة
واولى الناس بالامامة اعلمهم بالسنة وعن أبي يوسف اقرؤهم لان القراءة لابد منها والحاجة الى العلم انما تتم عند نائبة ونحن نقول القراءة مفتقر اليها لركن واحد والعلم لسائر الاركان
فان تساووا فاقرؤهم لقوله عليه السلام يؤم القوم اقرأهم لكتاب الله فان كانوا سواء فاعلمهم بالسنة وفرضهم كان اعلمهم لانهم كانوا يتلقونه باحكامه فقدم في الحديث ولا كذلك في زماننا فقدمنا الاعلم
Chapter of Imamate
And the most deserving people for imamate is the one most knowledgeable among them of the Sunnah, and from Abu Yusuf: the one who recites most, because recitation is indispensable, and the need for knowledge only arises when an incident occurs. And we say: recitation is needed for one pillar, and knowledge for all the pillars.
So if they are equal, then the one who recites most, because of his saying peace be upon him: 'The one who recites most of the Book of Allah should lead the people in prayer. If they are equal, then the one most knowledgeable of the Sunnah.' And among the Companions, the one who recited most was also the most knowledgeable, because they used to learn it with its rulings, so it was given precedence in the hadith. But it is not so in our time, so we give precedence to the most knowledgeable.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the primary qualification for leading congregational prayer (imamate). The ruling statement from the matn (base text) is that the one most knowledgeable in the Sunnah (اعلمهم بالسنة) is the most entitled to be imam. Abu Yusuf transmits a narration preferring the best reciter (اقرؤهم) because recitation is essential in every prayer, while knowledge is only needed when an unexpected issue arises. Abu Hanifa's response, endorsed by the commentator, is that recitation is needed only for one pillar (رکن واحد, i.e., the recitation of Qur'an in prayer), whereas knowledge of the Sunnah is needed for all other pillars (conditions, integrals, nullifiers, etc.). Thus knowledge is more comprehensive and deserves priority. The text then addresses the case when candidates are equal in knowledge: then the best reciter is preferred, based on the hadith: 'The one who recites most of the Book of Allah should lead the people. If they are equal, then the one most knowledgeable of the Sunnah.' This hadith seems to prioritize recitation over knowledge, but the commentator explains that among the Companions, the best reciters were also the most knowledgeable because they learned the Quran with its rulings. In later times, this is not necessarily true, so the Hanafi school gives precedence to knowledge (اعلم) over recitation (اقرأ). This resolves the apparent conflict between the hadith and the madhhab's position.

Key Terms
الإمامة (al-imāmah): Leading congregational prayer.
اعلمهم بالسنة (a‘lamuhum bi’s-sunnah): The one most knowledgeable of the prophetic way, i.e., the rulings of prayer (conditions, pillars, sunan, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hafiz, because recitation is indispensable.
B) The scholar, because knowledge of Sunnah covers all pillars.
C) They should draw lots.
D) The one who is older.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the most knowledgeable person in the rulings of prayer takes precedence over the best reciter for leading congregational prayer.

Preferring the Knowledgeable over the Better Reciter in Imamate
Hanafi ruling on preferring a'lam over aqra' in imamate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that in choosing an imam, a'lam (knowledgeable in Sunnah) is given precedence over aqra' (better reciter) when they conflict, and explain the contextual reasoning from the hadith.

Core Idea
In imamate, knowledge of Sunnah outweighs mere recitation skill when they conflict.

When selecting an imam for congregational prayer, which quality takes precedence: beautiful recitation or deep knowledge of the Sunnah? This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses that very question, showing how the Hanafi school uses a contextual reading of a famous hadith to determine that in our time, the more knowledgeable person (a'lam) should lead, even if another is a better reciter (aqra'). Let us walk through the ruling, its proof, and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
The passage first recounts that the Prophet (peace be upon him) chose Abu Bakr over four better reciters from the Ansar, establishing that knowledge takes precedence. Then it quotes the hadith: 'Let the most reciter lead... if equal, then the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah.' Your task is to see that the Hanafi ruling is to prefer a'lam over aqra' when they conflict, and that this is based on the contextual reality of the Sahaba.
Note: the ruling is about preference (sunnah), not obligation.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith is the core proof. Identify it and its form: 'يؤم القوم أقرأهم لكتاب الله فإن كانوا سواء فأعلمهم بالسنة'. This is a hadith ahad, zanni in transmission and meaning.
The hadith seems to order aqra' first, then a'lam.
3
Trace the Hanafi interpretation (wajh al-dalalah)
The Hanafi school explains that in the Sahaba's era, the best reciter was automatically the most knowledgeable because they learned the Quran with its rulings. So the hadith's order was consistent with preferring knowledge. Today, a great reciter may lack fiqh knowledge, so we give precedence to a'lam. This interpretation relies on the principle that haqiqah (reality) takes precedence over metaphor, and the imperative form is actually declarative (indicating legislation, not obligation).
The comment: 'وقدمنا الاعلم' – 'so we advance the knowledgeable one'.
4
Analyze the two objections and their Hanafi responses
The passage presents two objections: (1) the imperative form implies obligation to follow the order, (2) the hadith contradicts the Hanafi position. The Hanafi response: 'يؤم القوم' is not imperative but declarative, so no obligation; and the order was valid in the Sahaba's context but not applicable now. Identify how each objection is refuted.
This step strengthens your proof analysis skills.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Consider a mosque committee choosing between Candidate A: hafiz with perfect recitation but minimal knowledge of fiqh, and Candidate B: scholar of hadith and fiqh with average recitation. According to the Hanafi position, Candidate B (a'lam) should be preferred. State the reasoning: because today recitation does not imply comprehensive knowledge.
The practical difference: the mufta bihi ruling.

Chapter of Imamate. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 2. All of them were from the Ansar: Ubayy ibn Ka'b, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, Zayd ibn Thabit, and Abu Zayd. These were more knowledgeable in recitation than Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, such that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'The most reciter among you is Ubayy.' That is, during the era of Prophethood, four persons were complete in the Quran, all from the Ansar: Ubayy ibn Ka'b, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, Zayd ibn Thabit, and Abu Zayd, may Allah be pleased with them all. So these four were more knowledgeable in Quranic recitation than Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him. Despite this, the Prophet, peace be upon him, advanced al-Siddiq al-Akbar for imamate. So it became known that when there is conflict between a reciter and a knowledgeable person, the knowledgeable one is preferred, not the reciter. If they are equal in knowledge of Sunnah, who deserves imamate? Then if they are equal, the one who is a better reciter, because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'Let the one who is the most reciter of the Book of Allah lead the people. If they are equal, then the one who is most knowledgeable of the Sunnah.' And the reciter among them was also the most knowledgeable because they used to receive it with its rulings. So he advanced in the hadith, but it is not so in our time, so we advance the knowledgeable one. Then if all are equal in knowledge, the better reciter is more deserving because the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Let the one who is the best reciter of the Book of Allah lead the people.' Then if these are equal, then the one most knowledgeable of the Sunnah leads. And among the Companions, the one who was a better reciter was also more knowledgeable because they learned the Quran with its rulings. Therefore, in the hadith, the reciter was given precedence. But in our time, it is not so, so we give precedence to the knowledgeable one. Explanation of the issue: If the entire congregation is equal in knowledge of Sunnah, then among them the better reciter is more deserving. The proof is the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Let the one who is the most reciter of the Book of Allah lead the people. If they are equal, then the one most knowledgeable of the Sunnah.' The reasoning from this hadith is apparent, but there are two objections. First: 'Let him lead' is in the imperative form, and the imperative indicates obligation. So the order mentioned in the hadith must be observed, i.e., giving precedence to the reciter over the knowledgeable one, but that is not the case because the mentioned order is for expressing superiority, not for permissibility. Second: This hadith is against the claimant, who advocates giving precedence to the knowledgeable one in Sunnah, while the hadith indicates giving precedence to the reciter of the Book. So how is it correct to present this hadith as proof? Answer to the first objection: 'Let him lead' is not in the imperative meaning; rather, it is a declarative form indicating legislation. This is the reality, and the rule is that as long as acting on the reality is possible, one does not resort to metaphor. So here, one will not resort to metaphor, and this form will not be in the imperative meaning. Answer to the second objection: Among the Companions, the one who was a reciter was also knowledgeable because in that time, people learned the Quran with its rulings. As narrated from Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, that he learned Surah al-Baqarah in twelve years. It is apparent that Umar's learning Surah al-Baqarah in such a long period was with its rulings. So because in the era of the Companions, the reciter was also knowledgeable, the hadith gives precedence to the reciter over the knowledgeable one. And in our time, since it is not so, we give precedence to the knowledgeable one over the reciter.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling with proof on the priority of qualifications for the imam in congregational prayer. It begins by recalling that during the Prophet's time, four companions (Ubayy, Mu'adh, Zayd, and Abu Zayd) were more knowledgeable in Quranic recitation than Abu Bakr, yet the Prophet chose Abu Bakr to lead prayer. This establishes that when there is a conflict between a more knowledgeable person (a'lam) and a better reciter (aqra'), the a'lam is given precedence. The text then quotes the hadith: 'Let the one who is the most reciter of the Book of Allah lead the people. If they are equal, then the one most knowledgeable of the Sunnah.' The Hanafi commentator explains that in the Sahaba's era, the best reciter was also the most knowledgeable, so the hadith's order (putting aqra' first) was consistent with preferring a'lam. However, in later times, a good reciter may not be knowledgeable, so a'lam is preferred. The passage then addresses two objections: (1) that the imperative form implies obligation, so the order must be followed; (2) that the hadith contradicts the Hanafi position. The answer to the first is that 'let him lead' is not imperative but declarative, indicating legislation, so no obligation. The answer to the second is that in Sahaba's time, the reciter was also knowledgeable, so the hadith's order was consistent with preferring knowledge; but today we distinguish.

Key Terms
اعلم (a'lam): The person most knowledgeable in the Sunnah (i.e., the rulings and meanings of the Quran and hadith).
اقرأ (aqra'): The person best in Quranic recitation (tilawah), including tajwid and memorization.
امامة (imamah): The act of leading congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, why did the Prophet choose Abu Bakr over better reciters like Ubayy to lead prayer?
A) Abu Bakr was the best reciter.
B) Abu Bakr was more knowledgeable in the Sunnah.
C) Abu Bakr was older in age.
D) Abu Bakr was more pious.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives precedence to the knowledgeable in Sunnah (a'lam) over the better reciter (aqra') when choosing an imam, because today recitation no longer implies comprehensive knowledge.

Preferring the Pious and the Elder for Imamate
Hanafi ruling on further qualifications for imam after knowledge and recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of preference for imam after knowledge and recitation, explain the proofs for preferring piety and age, and apply the criteria to a scenario.

Core Idea
After knowledge and recitation, piety, then age, then character, then beauty determine the imam.

When candidates for imam are equal in knowledge and recitation, further criteria are needed. The Hanafi school prioritizes piety (wara' and taqwa) based on Prophetic guidance, then age, then character, and finally appearance. This lesson explains the proofs and order, including the debated hadith on piety.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi order beyond knowledge and recitation
List the criteria in order: piety (awra'), then age (asinn), then character (akhlaq), then beauty (jamal). This order is based on the text.
This is a recommended order (sunnah muakkadah), not obligatory.
2
Examine the proof for preferring piety
The text cites the hadith: 'Whoever prays behind a pious scholar, it is as if he prayed behind a prophet.' However, Mulla Ali Qari declared it fabricated. Despite this, the ruling stands due to other considerations such as the consensus of the earlier scholars.
The hadith is zanni in thubut and dalala, but the principle is supported by other evidences.
3
Understand the distinction between wara' and taqwa
Wara' is refraining from doubtful matters; taqwa is avoiding clear prohibitions. The text clarifies that wara' is a higher level, so the most pious (awra') is preferred over the merely God-fearing (atqa).
This nuance affects the selection when candidates differ in these qualities.
4
Analyze the proof for preferring age
The Prophet instructed the sons of Abu Mulaykah: 'Let the older of you lead the prayer.' Also, giving precedence to an elder increases the congregation's reward and honors the elder, in line with the hadith 'Whoever does not honor our elder is not from us.'
Age is a tiebreaker after piety; it is not a primary criterion.
5
Note the additional criteria of character and beauty
If equal in age, character is preferred based on 'The best of you are those with the best character.' If equal in character, beauty is considered. However, the author of Hidayah did not explicitly mention these, but later commentators include them.
Beauty is the least emphasized criterion and may be overlooked in practice.

Commentary
This passage continues the Hanafi discussion of qualifications for the imam in congregational prayer. After establishing that knowledge of Sunnah is primary, and recitation secondary, the text addresses further criteria. If candidates are equal in knowledge and recitation, then the most pious (awra') is preferred. The proof is a hadith: 'Whoever prays behind a pious scholar, it is as if he prayed behind a prophet.' However, the commentator notes that Mulla Ali Qari declared this hadith as fabricated (mawdu'), yet the ruling stands based on other considerations. The distinction between wara' (refraining from doubtful things) and taqwa (avoiding clear prohibitions) is explained. Next, if equal in piety, then the eldest in age (asinn) is preferred, based on the Prophet's instruction to the sons of Abu Mulaykah and the principle that honoring elders increases the congregation's reward. The text then adds that if equal in age, the one with better character (akhlaq) is preferred, citing the hadith 'The best of you are those with the best character.' If equal in character, the most handsome physically is preferred, though this is a minority view. The passage concludes with a remark that the most deserving imam combines all virtues: recitation, knowledge, piety, lineage, character, and beauty. It also notes that a sinful person should not be given precedence, and that the Prophet himself led prayer despite possessing all perfect qualities.

Key Terms
ورع (wara'): Refraining from doubtful matters (shubuhat) that are not clearly prohibited but may lead to sin.
تقوی (taqwa): Avoiding clear prohibitions (muharramat).
سن (sin): Age, specifically older age is preferred for imamate among equals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Piety (wara' and taqwa)
D) Beauty

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order for imam selection after knowledge and recitation is piety, then age, then character, then beauty, based on Prophetic guidance and communal practice.

Criteria for Choosing an Imam: Piety and Age
Rules for preferring an imam when congregation equals in knowledge and recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy for preferring an imam when the congregation is equal in knowledge and recitation, and explain the proofs for each criterion.

Core Idea
When knowledge and recitation are equal, piety (wara') takes precedence, then age — because the Prophet ﷺ said so and elders draw greater congregation.

Choosing an imam for congregational prayer is not arbitrary; the Hanafi school provides a clear hierarchy when candidates are equal in knowledge and recitation. This lesson unpacks that hierarchy, including the proofs from hadith and a critique of one hadith's authenticity, demonstrating how the school maintains its ruling through sound principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selecting an imam for salah. The ruling is a recommendation (mandub) to prefer certain qualities; it is not obligatory (wajib).
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: one stating the merit of praying behind a pious learned scholar, and another instructing to let the older lead. Identify each in the text.
The first hadith is attributed to the Prophet, but Mulla Ali Qari classified it as fabricated.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith indicates preference for wara' through the phrase 'as if he prayed behind a prophet'. The second hadith explicitly commands age priority.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and response
Mulla Ali Qari's critique of the first hadith does not change the ruling; the Hanafi school relies on the underlying principle (istihsan or other proofs) that piety is superior.
The text still presents the hierarchy as valid, showing that even a weak hadith can support a ruling if the principle is established.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position is: first piety (wara'), then age, then character, then appearance. This is based on the Hidayah and other sources.
If all criteria are equal, drawing lots (istiham) is an option.

باب الامامة

علم اور قرآت میں سب برابر ہوں تو کون مستحق امامت ہے؟
فان تساووا فاورعهم لقوله عليه السلام من صلى خلف عالم تقى فكانما صلى خلف نبي
ترجمہ: پھر اگر علم اور قرآت میں برابر ہوں تو ان میں ورع والا اولی ہے کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس نے عالم متقی کے پیچھے نماز پڑھی گویا اس نے نبی کے پیچھے نماز پڑھی۔ تشریح: ورع اور تقوی میں فرق یہ ہے کہ ورع کہتے ہیں شبہات سے پرہیز کرنا اور تقوی کہتے ہیں محرمات سے بچنے کو۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر تمام اہل جماعت علم اور قرآت میں برابر ہوں تو ان میں ورع والا اولی ہے۔ دلیل حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا قول: "من صلى خلف عالم تقى فكأنما صلى خلف نبی" اس حدیث کے بارے میں ملا علی قاری نے کہا کہ یہ حدیث موضوع ہے۔

علم، قرآت، تقوی میں سب برابر ہوں تو کون مستحق امامت ہے؟
فان تساووا فاستهم لقوله عليه السلام لابني ابى مليكة وليؤمكما اكبركما سنا ولان في تقديمه تكثير الجماعة
ترجمہ: پھر اگر امور مذکورہ میں سب برابر ہوں تو جو ان میں سے از راہ عمر بڑا ہو وہ اولی ہے کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ابو ملیکہ کے صاحبزادوں سے فرمایا کہ تم دونوں میں سے بڑا امامت کرے اور اس لئے کہ بزرگ کو مقدم کرنے میں جماعت کی زیادتی ہوگی۔ تشریح: اگر مذکورہ چیزوں میں اہل جماعت سب برابر ہیں تو ان میں از راہ عمر جو بڑا ہو وہ امامت کے لئے زیادہ مناسب ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بڑے بزرگ کی امامت کرنے میں جماعت کی دعوت کی زیادتی ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ جماعت کی زیادتی اللہ تعالی کو زیادہ پسند ہے۔ اور حدیث میں فرمایا: "من لا يوقر كبيرنا فليس منا" اور جب اس کو اپنا امام بنالیا تو اس کی توقیر کی بے ادبی نہیں رہی۔

ہماری طرف: مصنف ہدایہ نے یہ نہیں کہا کہ اگر سب عمر میں برابر ہوں حالانکہ ان کے علاوہ نے ذکر کیا کہ اگر سب عمر میں برابر ہوں تو ان میں اخلاق والا اولی ہے کیونکہ حدیث شریف میں فرمایا گیا کہ "خياركم أحسنكم أخلاقا" اور اگر اخلاق میں سب برابر ہوں تو ان میں سے جو زیادہ خوبصورت ہو وہ اولی بالامامت ہوگا۔
Chapter of Imamate. When they are equal, then the most God-fearing (wara') among them, because the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever prays behind a learned pious scholar, it is as if he prayed behind a prophet.' Explanation: The difference between wara' and taqwa is that wara' is abstaining from doubtful matters, while taqwa is avoiding prohibitions. The ruling: if all members of the congregation are equal in knowledge and recitation, then the one with more wara' is preferable. The proof is the Prophet's saying. Mulla Ali Qari said this hadith is fabricated. When they are equal in knowledge, recitation, and taqwa, then who deserves imamate? If they are equal, then cast lots, because of the Prophet's saying to the sons of Abu Mulaikah: 'The older of you should lead you,' and because in preferring him there is increase in the congregation. Explanation: If equal in the mentioned matters, the elder in age is preferable because of the hadith and because preferring the elder increases the congregation. Another proof: 'Whoever does not respect our elder is not of us.' Additional note: The author of Hidayah did not mention that if equal in age, then the one with better character is preferable, but others have mentioned it because of the hadith 'The best of you are those with the best character.' And if equal in character, then the most handsome.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on imamate addresses the criteria for selecting an imam when the congregation is equal in knowledge and recitation. The Hanafi ruling establishes a hierarchy: when individuals are equal in knowledge and recitation, the most pious (wara') is preferred. The commentator distinguishes wara' (abstaining from doubtful matters) from taqwa (abstaining from prohibitions). The proof cited is a hadith: 'Whoever prays behind a learned and pious scholar is as if he prayed behind a prophet.' Although Mulla Ali Qari classified this hadith as fabricated, the ruling remains based on the principle of preferring the more pious. If they are equal in piety, then the oldest in age is preferred, based on the Prophet's instruction to the sons of Abu Mulaikah: 'Let the older of you lead the prayer.' The rationale is that preferring an elder increases the congregation's reward and unity. The commentator notes that the Hidayah does not mention further criteria, but other scholars add that if age is equal, the one with the best character is preferred, and if character is equal, the one with the best appearance. This is based on hadith 'The best of you are those with the best character.' The overall principle is that the imam should be chosen to maximize the congregation's benefit and respect.

Key Terms
ورع (wara'): Abstaining from doubtful matters (shubuhat) to avoid falling into anything impermissible.
تقوى (taqwa): Avoiding what is explicitly prohibited (muharramat).
امامت (imamat): Leading the congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The older one
B) The more pious one (wara')
C) The one with better character
D) The more handsome one

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hierarchy for imam selection after equal knowledge/recitation is: piety (wara'), then age, then character, then appearance.

Rulings on Leading Prayer by Specific Individuals
Hanafi rulings on leading prayer by specific individuals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leading prayer by individuals with specific qualities (slave, bedouin, fasiq, blind, illegitimate child) and explain the proofs and responses to opposing schools.

Core Idea
The prayer behind a fasiq is valid but disliked: preserving congregation over personal sin.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the imamate of individuals who may lack religious knowledge or piety. The ruling balances the ideal of a righteous imam with the practical need for congregational prayer, maintaining validity even when the imam is less than perfect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the individuals and the general ruling
List the five types: slave, bedouin, fasiq, blind, and illegitimate child. State the Hanafi ruling: it is makruh (disliked) to appoint them, but if they lead, the prayer is valid.
The dislike is tanzihi (slight), not tahrimi.
2
Understand the reasons for dislike
For each, identify the specific reason: slave lacks time to learn; bedouin is often ignorant; fasiq does not care for religious matters; blind cannot avoid impurities; illegitimate child lacks paternal guidance leading to ignorance.
The general reason is that such appointments may cause aversion in the congregation.
3
Locate the primary proof
The hadith 'صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر' (Pray behind every righteous and sinful person) establishes the validity of the prayer regardless of the imam's personal sins.
This is a zanni al-thubut hadith, but sufficient for validity.
4
Analyze the objections and responses
Shafi'i objects regarding the slave, citing 'Listen and obey even if a slave is appointed' and Abu Sa'id's practice. The Hanafi response distinguishes political authority from imamate. Maliki objects regarding the fasiq, but Hanafis cite the Companions' practice of praying behind Hajjaj.
This shows the Hanafi method of ta'wil (interpretation) and reliance on sahabi practice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Shafi'i: no dislike for a learned slave; Maliki: prayer behind a fasiq is invalid. Hanafi: valid but disliked, preserving congregational unity.
The practical consequence is whether the prayer must be repeated or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلام، دیہاتی، فاسق اور نابینے کی امامت کا حکم

ويكره تقديم العبد لانه لا يتفرغ للتعلم والاعرابي لان الغالب فيهم الجهل والفاسق لانه لايهتم لامر دينه والاعمى لانه لا يتوقى النجاسة وولد الزناء لانه ليس له اب يشفقه فيغلب عليه الجهل ولان تقديم هؤلاء تنفير الجماعة فيكره وان تقدمو اجاز لقوله عليه السلام صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر

ترجمہ: اور غلام کو آگے کرنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ وہ سیکھنے کے لئے فراغت نہیں پاتا ہے اور اعرابی کا کیونکہ اعراب میں جہالت غالب ہے اور فاسق کا کیونکہ فاسق اپنے امر دین کے لئے اہتمام نہیں کرتا۔ اور اندھے کا کیونکہ وہ نجاست سے بچاؤ نہیں رکھتا اور ولد الزنا کا کیونکہ اس کا کوئی باپ نہیں جو اس پر شفقت کرے پس اس پر جہل غالب ہوگا اور اس لئے کہ ان لوگوں کو آگے کرنے میں جماعت کو نفرت ہوتی ہے اس لئے مکروہ ہے اور اگر یہ لوگ آگے بڑھ گئے تو جائز ہے کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ ہر نیکوکار اور بدکار کے پیچھے نماز پڑھ لو۔

تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ غلام کو امامت کے لئے آگے بڑھانا مکروہ ہے اگرچہ وہ آزاد کر دیا گیا ہو یعنی اگر آزاد کردہ غلام اور اصلی آزاد جمع ہو گئے تو اصلی آزاد مستحق امامت ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ غلام نماز کے احکام سیکھنے کے لئے فراغت نہیں پاتا اس لئے اس کے پیچھے نماز مکروہ ہے۔ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ اگر آزاد اور غلام دونوں قرآت علم اور ورع میں برابر ہوں تو آزاد کو غلام پر ترجیح نہیں دی جائے گی کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد ہے: "اسمعوا واطيعوا ولو امر عليكم عبد حبشي اجدع" سنو اور اطاعت کرو اگرچہ تم پر حبشی غلام امیر بنا دیا گیا ہو۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ابو سعید مولی اسید سے روایت ہے انه قال: دعوت رهطا من اصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيهم ابوذر فحضرت الصلوة فقدمني وانا يومنذ عبد یعنی ابوسعید کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے اصحاب نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم میں سے ایک جماعت کی دعوت کی ان میں ابوذر بھی تھے پس نماز کا وقت آ گیا تو امامت کے لئے مجھے آگے بڑھایا اور میں اس زمانے میں غلام تھا۔ یہ واقعہ دلالت کرتا ہے کہ غلام کو آگے بڑھانا مکروہ نہیں ہے۔

ہماری طرف سے پہلی حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ غلام کو آگے بڑھانا تقلیل جماعت کا سبب بنے گا کیونکہ لوگ اس کی متابعت کرنے سے منہ چڑھائیں گے اور جو چیز تقلیل جماعت کا سبب ہو وہ مکروہ ہے اور حدیث میں امارت مراد ہے نہ کہ امامت اور ابوسعید کی حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ صحابہ نے ابوسعید کو صاحب خانہ ہونے کی وجہ سے آگے بڑھایا کیونکہ صاحب خانہ احق بالامامت ہوتا ہے۔

اعرابی (گنوار) کو بھی امامت کے لئے آگے بڑھانا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ ان میں جہالت کا غلبہ ہوتا ہے نیز حضور کا قول: "لا يؤمن امرأة رجلا ولا اعرابی" عورت مرد کی امامت کرے اور نہ اعرابی۔

اور فاسق کو بھی آگے بڑھانا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ وہ دین کے معاملے میں اہتمام نہیں کرتا۔ امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ اس کے پیچھے نماز جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ جب اس کی طرف سے امور دینیہ میں خیانت ظاہر ہوگئی تو وہ نماز جیسے اہم امور میں بھی امین نہیں ہوگا لیکن ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ عبداللہ بن عمر، انس بن مالک اور ان کے علاوہ دوسرے صحابہ اور تابعین نے حجاج بن یوسف رئیس الفساق کے پیچھے نماز پڑھی ہے۔

امامت کے لئے نابینا کو آگے بڑھانا بھی مکروہ ہے کیونکہ وہ اندھا ہونے کی وجہ سے نجاست سے بچاؤ نہیں رکھتا اور ولد الزنا کو بھی آگے بڑھانا مکروہ ہے۔
The ruling on leading prayer by a slave, bedouin, sinful person, blind person, and illegitimate child. It is disliked to put forward a slave because he does not have free time to learn; a bedouin because ignorance prevails among them; a sinful person because he does not care about his religious affairs; a blind person because he does not avoid impurity; and an illegitimate child because he has no father to show him affection, so ignorance dominates him. And because putting these forward causes aversion among the congregation, it is disliked. But if they do lead, it is valid because of the Prophet's saying: 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person.' Explanation: The ruling is that making a slave lead is disliked even if he is freed; if a freed slave and a free-born person are together, the free-born person is more deserving of imamate. The proof: the slave lacks time to learn. Imam Shafi'i said: if a free person and a slave are equal in recitation, knowledge, and piety, the free person is not given preference over the slave, citing the hadith: 'Listen and obey even if a slave is appointed over you.' And the report of Abu Sa'id, a slave who was asked to lead prayer. The Hanafi response: the hadith refers to political authority, not imamate; Abu Sa'id was the host, and the host has more right to lead. For the bedouin: it is disliked, and the Prophet said: 'A woman should not lead a man, nor a bedouin.' For the sinful person: it is disliked; Imam Malik said praying behind him is invalid, but the Hanafi response is that companions prayed behind Hajjaj. For the blind person and illegitimate child: also disliked.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi ruling on leading prayer by a slave, bedouin, sinful person (fasiq), blind person, and illegitimate child. The Hanafi position is that it is makruh (disliked) to appoint such persons as imam, but if they do lead, the prayer is valid. The reasons for the dislike are specific: a slave lacks time to learn the rules of prayer; a bedouin is often ignorant; a fasiq does not care for religious matters; a blind person cannot avoid impurities; an illegitimate child lacks paternal guidance, leading to ignorance. Overall, appointing them can cause aversion among the congregation. The validity is established by the hadith: 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person.' The commentator addresses objections: from Imam Shafi'i, who argues a slave is not disliked, citing the hadith 'Listen and obey even if a slave is appointed over you' and the practice of Abu Sa'id, a slave who led prayer. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the hadith referring to political leadership (imarah) not imamate, and Abu Sa'id's case being due to his being the host (sahib al-khanah), who has more right to lead. From Imam Malik, who argues the prayer behind a fasiq is invalid, the Hanafi response is that companions like Ibn Umar and Anas prayed behind the notorious fasiq Hajjaj ibn Yusuf, proving validity. Thus, the Hanafi ruling balances dislike with validity, emphasizing the importance of congregational prayer over the imam's personal shortcomings.

Key Terms
عبد (abd): A slave, i.e., a person who is owned by another, lacking freedom.
اعرابی (a'rabi): A bedouin, i.e., a desert Arab, often considered ignorant of religious rulings.
فاسق (fasiq): A sinful person who openly commits major sins without repentance.
اعمى (a'ma): A blind person, who cannot see to avoid impurities.
ولد الزنا (walad al-zina): An illegitimate child, born from adultery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on leading prayer by a sinful person (fasiq)?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated
B) It is disliked but valid
C) It is prohibited
D) It is preferred

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that leading prayer by a slave, bedouin, fasiq, blind person, or illegitimate child is disliked but valid, supported by the hadith 'صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر' and the practice of the Companions.

Salah — Prayer

The Imam Should Not Prolong the Prayer
Ruling with proof that imam must consider congregation's weakness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding the imam prolonging the prayer and explain the evidence from the Sunnah, including the incident of Mu'adh and the Prophet's shortening of Fajr.

Core Idea
The imam must pray lightly, considering the weakest in the congregation.

The leadership of prayer carries a responsibility to care for the congregation. This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling that the imam should not prolong the prayer, supported by direct prophetic commands and practical examples from the Prophet's own conduct. Understanding this ruling helps ensure that congregational prayer remains accessible to all, including the sick, elderly, and those with urgent needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act being ruled upon (the imam prolonging the prayer) and the hukm level (sunnah muakkadah or makruh tanzihi).
The primary ruling is that prolongation is disliked (makruh tanzihi) if it causes hardship.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith: 'Whoever leads a people in prayer, let him pray with them the prayer of the weakest among them.'
This is a sahih hadith reported by al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith yields the ruling. The imperative 'فليصل' indicates desirability (sunniyyah) in Hanafi usul, and the reason ('among them are the sick, elderly, etc.') shows the consideration.
The command is understood as recommending lightness, not obligating it, because the hadith also indicates permissibility of prolongation in some cases.
4
Examine additional evidence
Consider the incident of Mu'adh ibn Jabal and the Prophet's own shortening of Fajr due to a child's cry.
These incidents reinforce the principle of considering the congregation's condition.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
Conclude that the imam should assess the congregation and avoid undue length; if he prolongs excessively causing hardship, the prayer is still valid but he is sinful.
The mufta bihi position is that it is sunnah to be light; prolongation is makruh tanzihi when causing difficulty.

ولا يطول الامام بهم الصلوة لقوله عليه السلام من ام قوما فليصل بهم صلوة اضعفهم فان فيهم المرية والكبير وذا الحاجة
ترجمہ: اور امام مقتدی کے ساتھ نماز کو طول نہ دے کیونکہ حضور نے فرمایا جو شخص کسی قوم کا امام با تو ان کو نماز پڑھائے ان میں سب سے ضعیف کی اس لئے کہ ان میں بیمار بھی ہیں بوڑھے بھی ضرورت مند بھی۔
تشریح: مسئلہ امام لوگوں کو لمبی نماز نہ پڑھائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس نے قوم کی امامت کی وہ ان کو ان میں سے اضعف کی نماز پڑھائے کیونکہ مقتدیوں میں بیمار بھی ہیں، بوڑھے بھی ہیں اور ضرورت مند بھی ہیں اور معاذ بن جبل رضی اللہ عن حدیث بھی مستدل ہے جبکہ معاذ نے اپنی قوم کو لمبی نماز پڑھائی تو قوم کے لوگوں نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے شکایت کی تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فر فرمایا انت یا معاذ یہ حدیث سابق میں گذر چکی ہے اور یہ بات بطریق صحت ثابت ہے کہ ایک روز حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فجر کی نماز میں تین کی قرآت کی جب آپ نماز سے فارغ ہو گئے تو صحابہ نے عرض کیا کہ اللہ کے رسول اللہ آج آپ نے بڑا اختصار کیا تو فرمایا کہ بچے کے رونے کی وجہ سے مجھے خوف ہوا کہ اس کی ماں فتنہ میں نہ پڑ جائے اس واقعہ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ امام کے لئے اپنی قوم کے مال رعایت کرنا مناسب ہے۔
Translation: And the imam should not prolong the prayer for them due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Whoever leads a people in prayer, let him pray with them the prayer of the weakest among them, for among them are the sick, the elderly, and the one with a need.'
Commentary: The issue is that the imam should not lengthen the prayer. The proof is the hadith. Also the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal (may Allah be pleased with him) is used as evidence when Mu'adh prolonged the prayer for his people and they complained to the Prophet (peace be upon him), who said: 'Are you causing division, O Mu'adh?' This incident was mentioned earlier. And it is authentically established that one day the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited three verses in Fajr prayer. When he finished, the Companions said: 'O Messenger of Allah, you shortened a lot today.' He replied: 'I heard the cry of a child and feared that his mother would be troubled.' This incident shows that it is appropriate for the imam to consider the condition of his congregation.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that the imam must not prolong the prayer beyond the capacity of the weakest members of the congregation. The primary proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) commands that the prayer be light, considering the sick, elderly, and those with urgent needs. The text also cites the famous incident of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, who was rebuked for prolonging prayer, and the incident of the Prophet shortening Fajr prayer out of concern for a mother. The Hanafi position is that it is wajib (obligatory) to consider the congregation's condition and avoid undue prolongation. The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, and the mufta bihi position is that it is recommended (sunnah) not to prolong, but if the imam does, the prayer is still valid unless it causes hardship.

Key Terms
اضعف (ad'af): The weakest, referring to the person with the least stamina among the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He heard a child crying and feared troubling the mother.
C) He forgot the recitation.
D) He was ill.

Key Takeaway
The imam should pray lightly, considering the weakest, as commanded by the Prophet and demonstrated by his actions.

Women Praying in Congregation Alone is Disliked
Ruling with proof on women praying in congregation without men

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women praying in congregation alone, identify the dalil and its interpretation, and explain why it is makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
Women's own congregation is disliked because it entails risk of exposure and imitation of men; Aisha's precedent is specific to early Islam.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on women forming their own congregation (jama'ah) for prayer. While the act is valid if performed, it is considered prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) due to the potential for exposure of the imam (standing in the middle like men) and the imitation of male congregation. The lesson explores the proof from the sunnah and the reasoning behind the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is women praying in congregation without any male present. The ruling is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram; the prayer is valid but sinful without excuse.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the action of Aisha (RA) who led a group of women and stood in the middle of the row.
The dalil is a type of Sunnah ahad, transmitted by Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The text interprets Aisha's action as specific to the early period of Islam (haml 'ala ibtida' al-Islam), not as a general practice. Also, stepping forward causes more exposure of the woman (imam), which is prohibited.
The interpretation limits the applicability of the proof.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Many later scholars (including some Hanafis) allow women's congregation, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is dislike.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position is makruh tahrimi, based on Zahir al-Riwayah. The ruling is that it is best to avoid.
This is the operative rule for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره للنساء ان يصلين وحدهن الجماعة لانها لاتخلوا عن ارتكاب محرم وهو قيام الامام وسط الشعر فيكره كالعراة وان فعلن قامت الامام وسطهن لأن عائشة فعلت كذلك وحمل فعلها الجماعة على ابنه الاسلام ولان في التقديم زيادة الكشف
ترجمہ: اور عورتوں کے لئے تنہا جماعت سے نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ عورتوں کی جماعت ارتکاب حرام سے خالی نہیں ہے اور وہ وسط صف میں کھڑا ہوتا ہے پس یہ فعل مکروہ ہوگا جیسے نگے مردوں کا حکم ہے اور اگر عورتوں نے جماعت کی تو امام ان کے بیچ میں کھانا کیونکہ ام المؤمنین عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا نے ایسا ہی کیا اور ام المؤمنین کا فعل جماعت ابتداء اسلام پر محمول کیا گیا اور اس وجہ سے کہ آگے بڑھنے میں کشف عورت زیادہ ہے۔
تشریح: مسئلہ عورتوں کے لئے تنہا جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنا مکروہ تحریمی ہے کیونکہ عورتوں کی جماعت فعل حرام (مردوں کی مشابہت یا کشف) سے خالی نہیں ہے۔
Translation: And it is disliked for women to pray in congregation by themselves because their congregation is not free from committing something prohibited, and that is the imam standing in the middle of the row. So it is disliked, like the ruling of naked men. And if they do perform it, the imam stands in their middle because Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) did so. But her action is interpreted as being from the early days of Islam, and also because stepping forward causes more exposure of the woman.
Commentary: The issue is that it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) for women to form their own congregation because it involves an impermissible act (imitation of men or exposure).
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that it is disliked for women to form their own congregation without men. The reason given is that it necessarily involves something prohibited: the imam standing in the middle of the row (as per man's practice) or exposure when stepping forward. The text cites the precedent of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who led women and stood in the middle. However, the Hanafi interpretation is that this was specific to the early days of Islam and is not general practice. The ruling is makruh tahrimi according to the Hanafi school, meaning it is forbidden to do so, but if done, the prayer is still valid. The mufta bihi position is that it is disliked, and it is preferred for women to pray individually or in a mosque behind a male imam.

Key Terms
مکروه تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): A disliked act that is close to haram, based on a weak proof that suggests prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it disliked for women to form their own congregation according to the Hanafi school?
A) Women cannot lead prayer.

D) It is invalid under all circumstances.

Key Takeaway
Women's congregation alone is valid but prohibitively disliked due to risk of exposure and imitation of men; Aisha's precedent is interpreted as specific to early Islam.

Ruling on Putting a Person Without a Father Forward as Imam
Ruling on making a child without a father lead prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on appointing a person without a father as imam, explain the proof from hadith and the rationale based on causing aversion, and distinguish between the act of appointment and the validity of the prayer.

Core Idea
Appointing a fatherless imam is disliked, but his prayer leading is valid based on a general command.

In this passage, al-Hidayah addresses a social sensitivity: appointing as imam a person who lacks a father's upbringing. The ruling distinguishes between the act of appointment and the validity of the prayer itself, relying on a hadith that commands prayer behind every Muslim, regardless of personal state. Understanding this distinction prevents both unnecessary prohibition and disregard for communal feelings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is putting forward a man without a father as the imam. The ruling is that this action is makruh (disliked).
The karahah applies to the appointment, not to the prayer led by such a person.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites the hadith 'Pray behind every righteous and wicked person.' This hadith is the source for the validity of the prayer.
The hadith is quoted in Arabic: 'صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر'.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The command is general and unconditional. It indicates that the personal virtue or background of the imam does not affect the validity of the prayer, as every person is either righteous or wicked.
In Hanafi usul, a general command (amm) indicates obligation or permissibility unless specified otherwise.
4
Note the rationale for karahah
The karahah is due to the potential aversion among the congregation. A fatherless person may be seen as lacking discipline and care, causing discomfort.
This is based on the principle of avoiding harm (la darar wa la dirar).
5
Distinguish between appointment and actual leading
The karahah attaches only to the intentional appointment. If such a person steps forward on his own, the prayer is valid without dislike.
The hadith overrides the karahah in the case of actual leading.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آگے بڑھانا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ اس کا کوئی باپ نہیں جو اس پر شفقت کرے، اس کو ادب سکھائے اور اس کو تعلیم دے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے مشتر کہ دلیل کے طور پر کہا کہ ان لوگوں کو آگے بڑھانے میں اہل جماعت کو نفرت دلانا ہے اس ۔ ان کو نہ صہ بڑھانا مکروہ ہے ہاں اگر یہ لوگ خود آگے بڑھ گئے تو نماز جائز ہو جائے گی کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے صلوا خلف كل برو فاجر کا استدلال یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ لوگوں میں سے ہر ایک نیک ہوگا یا فاجر پس اس کے پیچھے ہر حال میں نماز جائز ہے۔
Putting forward is disliked because he has no father to show him affection, teach him manners, and educate him. The author of al-Hidayah said as a common evidence that putting these people forward causes aversion among the congregation. So putting them forward is disliked. However, if these people themselves step forward, the prayer becomes valid because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Pray behind every righteous and wicked person.' The reasoning is that each of these people is either righteous or wicked, so prayer behind him is permissible in all cases.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof. It addresses the case of a person who has no father—likely an orphan or a boy without proper upbringing—being put forward as an imam. The ruling is that it is makruh (disliked) to intentionally appoint such a person because he lacks the discipline and care that a father would provide, and his appointment may cause resentment among the congregation. However, if he himself steps forward to lead, the prayer is valid, based on the general command of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to pray behind every righteous and wicked person. This demonstrates that the karahah is in the act of appointing, not in the validity of the prayer itself. The hadith establishes that the imam's personal deficiencies do not invalidate the followers' prayer.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): An action that is disliked and discouraged; in this context, it refers to the act of intentionally putting a person without a father forward as imam.

D) It is permissible without any dislike.

Key Takeaway
Appointing a fatherless imam is makruh due to potential aversion, but the prayer behind him remains valid based on the general command to pray behind every Muslim.
