The Hanafi Ruling on Women's Congregational Prayer
Ruling that women's congregation alone is makruh tahrimi, with proof from Aisha's action and abrogation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's congregational prayer (makruh tahrimi), explain the reason (kashf al-awrah), and apply the exception regarding imam's position.

Core Idea
Women praying in congregation is prohibitively disliked because it exposes awrah; if done, the imam must stand in the middle.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses whether it is permissible for women to form their own congregational prayer without men. The Hanafi school rules that it is makruh tahrimi due to the increased exposure of the awrah. However, if women do pray in congregation, the imam should stand in the middle, based on the action of Aisha. This lesson explains the ruling, the proof, and the reasoning behind the karahah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Here, it is women praying in congregation by themselves (without men). What is the hukm level? The text says 'makruh tahrimi' (prohibitively disliked).
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram, established by a zanni proof.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The action of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) leading women in congregation. This is a qawl al-sahabi (saying/action of a companion).
The dalil is zanni in both thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this dalil prove the ruling? The action of Aisha is used to establish the position of the imam (if women do pray) but is not taken as unconditional permissibility because it is considered abrogated. The karahah is based on the illah of kashf al-awrah.
The illah is the exposure of awrah, analogized to naked men praying.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and its resolution
An objection is raised: since Aisha did it, why is it makruh? The answer: her action was in early Islam and has been abrogated. A chronological objection about Aisha's age is then addressed, concluding that 'abrogated' means the ruling allowing women's congregation was later superseded.
The text shows a dialectical method common in later Hanafi works.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that women's congregation is makruh tahrimi. If performed, the imam stands in the middle. This is the view of the author of al-Hidayah.
The authority weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin (later fatwa works).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورتوں کی تنہا جماعت کا حکم
ويكره للنساء ان يصلين وحدهن الجماعة لانها لاتخلوا عن ارتكاب محرم وهو قيام الامام وسط الشعر فيكره كالعراة وان فعلن قامت الامام وسطهن لأن عائشة فعلت كذلك وحمل فعلها الجماعة على ابنه الاسلام ولان في التقديم زيادة الكشف
ترجمہ اور عورتوں کے لئے تنہا جماعت سے نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ عورتوں کی جماعت ارتکاب حرام سے خالی نہیں ہے اور و وسط صف میں کھڑا ہوتا ہے پس یہ فعل مکروہ ہوگا جیسے نگے مردوں کا حکم ہے اور اگر عورتوں نے جماعت کی تو امام ان کے بیچ میں کھانا کیونکہ ام المؤمنین عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا نے ایسا ہی کیا اور ام المؤمنین کا فعل جماعت ابتداء اسلام پر محمول کیا گیا اور اس وجہ سے کہ نہ بڑھنے میں کشف عورت زیادہ ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ عورتوں کے لئے تنہا جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنا مکروہ تحریمی ہے کیونکہ عورتوں کی جماعت فعل حرام (مردہوا۔
صاحب قدری نے کہا کہ اگر کراہت تحریمی کے باوجود عورتوں نے جماعت کی تو عورتوں کی امام ان کے بیچ میں کھڑی ہو کیونکہ حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا نے ایسا ہی کیا لیکن اب اشکال یہ ہوگا کہ جب حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا نے جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی ہے تو پھر مکروہ تحریمی کیوں ہے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ام المؤمنین کا یہ فعل ابتداء اسلام پر محمول کیا جائے گا مگر اس جواب پر اشکال ہے ود یہ کہ نبوت کے بعد آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے تیرہ سال مکہ المکرمہ میں قیام فرمایا پھر مدینہ منورہ میں حضرت عائشہ سے چھ سال کی عمر میں نکاح کیا پھر جب نو برس کی ہوئیں تو ان کو زفاف میں لیا یعنی عائشہ کی رخصتی ہوئی اور آپ کی حیات میں 9 برس رہیں پس حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہا کا امامت کرنا بالغ ہونے کے بعد ہوا ہوگا تو اس صورت میں یہ ابتداء اسلام کا فعل کہاں سے ہوگا۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ابتداء اسلام پر محمول کرنے سے مراد یہ ہے کہ عورتوں کی جماعت کا حکم منسوخ ہے۔
The ruling on women's congregation by themselves: It is disliked for women to pray in congregation by themselves because it is not free from committing something forbidden, and that is the imam standing in the middle of the row, so it is disliked like naked men. And if they do it, the imam stands in their middle because Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) did so, and her action is taken as abrogated in early Islam, and because advancing exposes more awrah.
Translation: And it is disliked for women to pray in congregation by themselves because the women's congregation is not free from committing something forbidden, and the imam stands in the middle of the row, so this action is disliked like the ruling of naked men. And if women do it, the imam should stand in their middle because the Mother of the Believers Aisha did so, and her action is taken as (being) in early Islam, and because in advancing there is more exposure of awrah.
Explanation: The ruling is that women praying in congregation alone is makruh tahrimi because it involves the imam standing in the middle (which violates the sunnah of men's congregation) and causes exposure. The author of al-Hidayah said: If they do it despite the karahah, the imam should stand in the middle, as Aisha did. But then there is an objection: If Aisha did it, why is it makruh? The answer is that her action is abrogated. Then an objection is raised about the timeline of Aisha's life in relation to early Islam. The final answer is that 'abrogated' means the ruling allowing women's congregation was later abrogated.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding women's congregational prayer. The Hanafi position is that it is makruh tahrimi for women to gather for congregational prayer by themselves (without a mahram or in a group of only women). The reason is that such a congregation necessitates either the imam standing in front (leading from the front row) or standing in the middle, both of which lead to increased exposure of the women's awrah (the imam being more visible) or violation of the proper congregational arrangement. The ruling is analogized to the case of naked men praying in congregation, which is also makruh due to exposure. However, if women do perform such a congregation despite the karahah, the imam (who must be a woman) should stand in the middle of the row, not in front, following the action of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her). The text addresses a potential contradiction: if Aisha did it, why is it makruh? The answer is that her action was from the early period of Islam and has been abrogated. The passage then deals with a chronological objection about Aisha's age, concluding that 'abrogated' here means that the ruling allowing women's congregation was later superseded. Thus, the relied-upon position is karahah. The key point is that while women's congregation is not absolutely prohibited, it is strongly disliked, and if done, must follow a specific formation to minimize exposure.

Key Terms
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An action that is prohibited in the sense of being forbidden, but not as severely as haram; it is to be avoided, and if done, it is sinful but the act (prayer) may still be valid.
کشف عورت (kashf al-'awrah): Exposure of the awrah (parts of the body that must be covered in prayer). In women, this is the entire body except face and hands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is sunnah and recommended.
B) It is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
C) It is haram and invalid.
D) It is permissible without any dislike.

Key Takeaway
Women's congregational prayer alone is makruh tahrimi in Hanafi fiqh; if performed, the imam must stand in the middle to minimize awrah exposure.

Position of a Single Male Follower in Congregation
Ruling with proof on the position of a single male follower in congregational prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah position for a single male follower in congregational prayer and identify the consequence of violating it.

Core Idea
One male follower stands on the right of the imam; standing behind is valid but sinful.

In congregational prayer, the placement of followers is governed by prophetic practice. For a single male follower, the sunnah is clear. This lesson examines the ruling from the hadith of Ibn Abbas and addresses a common misconception about where to stand.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine what the passage states as the preferred position for a single male follower.
The passage explicitly says to stand on the right.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: the hadith of Ibn Abbas.
The Prophet (peace be upon him) made Ibn Abbas stand on his right.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling: the Prophet's action demonstrates the sunnah.
It is a definitive indication of the recommended practice.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Identify Imam Muhammad's alternative view and the author's preference.
Imam Muhammad said to align fingers with the imam's heel; the author says the first view is more apparent.
5
State the consequence of violation
Determine the ruling if the follower stands behind or on the left.
The prayer is valid but he is sinful for opposing the sunnah.

( متفق علیہ ) یعنی ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما نے کہا کہ میں اپنی خالہ میمونہ کے یہاں رات سویا ہا کہ میں نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی رات کی نماز کو دیکھوں پر آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اٹھ کر کہا آنکھیں سو گئیں اور ستارے ڈوب گئے اور جی قیوم
Whoever prays with one person, should make him stand on his right, because of the hadith of Ibn Abbas: The Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed with him and made him stand on his right. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) because the Prophet prayed with him and made him stand on his right. And the follower should not lag behind the imam. And from Imam Muhammad that the follower places his fingers at the heel of the imam. And the first is apparent. And if this single follower prayed behind him or on his left, it is permissible but he is sinful because he opposed the sunnah.
Explanation: The ruling is that when there is one male follower, he should stand on the right of the imam. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas, who narrated that the Prophet made him stand on his right during night prayer. The full hadith is given: Ibn Abbas stayed at his aunt Maymunah's to observe the Prophet's night prayer. The Prophet woke, recited, performed wudu and began prayer. Ibn Abbas stood on his left, but the Prophet took him by the ear and made him stand on his right. The text also mentions Imam Muhammad's opinion that the follower should align his fingers with the imam's heel, but the first ruling (standing on the right) is the apparent one. If the follower stands behind or on the left, the prayer is valid but he is sinful for abandoning the sunnah.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the position of a single male follower in congregational prayer. The primary ruling is that he should stand on the right side of the imam, based on the authentic hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet (peace be upon him) positioned him on his right after he initially stood on the left. The text also mentions a transmission from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that the follower should place his fingers at the imam's heel (i.e., stand slightly behind, not fully aligned), but the author states that the first opinion (standing on the right) is more apparent (الاول هو الظاهر). If the follower stands behind the imam (as in the usual case with more than one follower) or on his left, the prayer is valid but he is sinful because he has violated the sunnah. The Hanafi position is that the sunnah for one follower is to stand on the right, not behind. This differs from other schools that may allow standing behind. The passage underscores the importance of following the prophetic practice in congregational arrangement.

Key Terms
مقتدی (muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind the imam.
سنت (sunnah): In this context, the prophetic practice that is recommended; violating it is sinful but does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Women's Congregational Prayer: Makruh Tahrimi
Ruling with proof and response to objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's congregational prayer and explain the proof and response to the objection based on Aisha's action.

Core Idea
Women's congregational prayer is makruh tahrimi because the unavoidable dislike outweighs the sunnah of congregation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that women performing congregational prayer led by a woman is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The text presents two reasons: either the imam stands ahead, causing greater exposure of her ‘awrah, or she stands among the women, which forces her to leave the proper imam position—both disliked acts. Since congregation is sunnah, leaving it to avoid these disliked elements is preferred. The ruling is then challenged by the historical practice of Sayyida Aisha (ra) leading women in congregation, but the Hanafi response is that her action was in early Islam and is now abrogated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
The passage states that women's congregational prayer is makruh tahrimi. This is a level between haram and makruh tanzihi; commission is sinful but the prayer itself is valid if performed.
2
Understand the two disliked scenarios
The women's imam either stands ahead of the followers (causing full exposure of her ‘awrah) or among them (forcing her to leave the imam position). Both are disliked, and the sunnah of congregation is abandoned to avoid them.
3
Analyze the qiyas to naked people's congregation
The ruling is analogized to the congregation of naked people, which is also disliked because of exposure. This strengthens the ruling by linking it to a well-known disliked act.
4
Examine the objection from Aisha's practice
An objector (Sahib Qadri) cites that Aisha led women in congregation, implying permissibility. The Hanafi response is that her action was in the early days of Islam and is now abrogated.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response on abrogation
The text further clarifies that 'early Islam' here means before the abrogation, not literally the earliest period. The ruling is that women's congregation is no longer permissible (makruh tahrimi), and Aisha's precedent is not valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم
99
باب الامامة
ارتکاب سے خالی نہیں اس لئے کہ ان کی امام اقتداء کرنے والی عورتوں سے آگے کھڑی ہوگی یا ان کے درمیان میں کھڑی ہوگی ۔ پہلی صورت میں کشف عورت زیادہ ہے درالحالیکہ یہ مکروہ ہے اور دوسری صورت میں امام کا اپنے مقام کو چھوڑ نا لازم آتا ہے حالانکہ یہ بھی مکروہ ہے اور جماعت سنت ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ بہ نسبت ارتکاب مکروہ کے سنت کو ترک کرنا اولی ہے اس لئے عورتوں کے حق میں جماعت کی سنت کو ترک کر دیا گیا اور عورتوں کا حال ننگوں کے حال کے مانند ہو گیا یعنی جس طرح ننگوں کی جماعت مکروہ ہے اس طرح عورتوں کی جماعت مکروہ ہے۔
صاحب قدری نے کہا کہ اگر کراہت تحریمی کے باوجود عورتوں نے جماعت کی تو عورتوں کی امام ان کے بیچ میں کھڑی ہو کیونکہ حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا نے ایسا ہی کیا لیکن اب اشکال یہ ہوگا کہ جب حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا نے جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی ہے تو پھر مکروہ تحریمی کیوں ہے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ام المؤمنین کا یہ فعل ابتداء اسلام پر محمول کیا جائے گا مگر اس جواب پر اشکال ہے ود یہ کہ نبوت کے بعد آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے تیرہ سال مکہ المکرمہ میں قیام فرمایا پھر مدینہ منورہ میں حضرت عائشہ سے چھ سال کی عمر میں نکاح کیا پھر جب نو برس کی ہوئیں تو ان کو زفاف میں لیا یعنی عائشہ کی رخصتی ہوئی اور آپ کی حیات میں 9 برس رہیں پس حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہا کا امامت کرنا بالغ ہونے کے بعد ہوا ہوگا تو اس صورت میں یہ ابتداء اسلام کا فعل کہاں سے ہوگا۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ابتداء اسلام پر محمول کرنے سے مراد یہ ہے کہ عورتوں کی جماعت کا حکم منسوخ ہے۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 2, page 99, section on Imamate: It is not free from commission (of disliked acts) because their (women's) imam will stand ahead of the women following or stand among them. In the first case, exposure of the woman is greater while it is disliked, and in the second case, the imam must leave her place while this is also disliked. Congregation is sunnah, and the rule is that compared to committing a disliked act, leaving the sunnah is more virtuous. Therefore, the sunnah of congregation was abandoned for women, and the case of women became like the case of naked people, meaning just as the congregation of the naked is disliked, so is the congregation of women. Sahib Qadri said that if despite the tahrimi dislike, women performed congregation, then the woman imam should stand in their middle, because Sayyida Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) did the same. But then there is an objection: when Sayyida Aisha performed prayer with congregation, why is it tahrimi makruh? The answer is that the action of the Mother of the Believers is to be interpreted as in the early days of Islam. But there is an objection to this answer: after prophethood, the Prophet (peace be upon him) stayed in Mecca for thirteen years, then in Medina he married Aisha when she was six years old, then when she was nine, he took her in marriage, and she remained with him for nine years. So Aisha's leading prayer must have been after she reached puberty, so how can it be an action of early Islam? The answer is that by interpreting it as early Islam, it is meant that the ruling on women's congregation is abrogated.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the dislike (karahah tahrimiyah) of women performing congregational prayer led by a woman. The author explains that a women's congregation is disliked because either the imam stands ahead (causing more exposure) or in the middle (forcing her to leave the proper imam position), both of which are disliked. Since congregation is sunnah, leaving it to avoid dislike is preferable. The ruling is analogized to the congregation of naked people, which is also disliked. Then an objection is raised: if it is disliked, how did Sayyida Aisha lead women in congregation? The response that her action was in early Islam and abrogated is challenged by historical chronology. The final resolution is that 'early Islam' refers to the time before the abrogation of the ruling, meaning her action is not a valid precedent.

Key Terms
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An act that is prohibited but with less certain evidence than haram; its commission is sinful but does not necessitate repeating the act if done involuntarily.
جماعت (jama'ah): Congregational prayer performed behind an imam.
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; a ruling that has been replaced by a later ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is women's congregational prayer considered makruh tahrimi?
A) Because women are not required to pray at all.
B) Because it either causes greater exposure of the imam or forces her to leave her position, both disliked.
C) Because women cannot lead prayer under any circumstances.
D) Because congregation is fard and women cannot perform fard.

Key Takeaway
Women's congregational prayer is makruh tahrimi in the Hanafi school, and the practice of Aisha is considered abrogated.

Positioning of a Single Male Follower in Congregational Prayer
Ruling and evidence for single male follower positioning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where a single male follower should stand relative to the imam, explain the evidence from the hadith of Ibn Abbas, and distinguish between the preferred and alternative positions within the school.

Core Idea
A single follower stands to the imam's right; it is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib, so prayer is valid but sinful if omitted.

This lesson addresses a specific aspect of congregational prayer: the positioning when there is only one male follower. The Hanafi school has a preferred practice based on the sunnah, but also acknowledges valid alternative positions. We will examine the primary evidence and the reasoning behind the chosen view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the positioning of a single male follower during congregational prayer. The ruling is a sunnah (recommended) position, not a condition of validity.
The text clearly states that if the follower stands behind or left, the prayer is valid but he is sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) placed him on his right side during night prayer.
Hadith is narrated by Bukhari and Muslim (muttafaq 'alayh), so transmission is certain (qati' al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action is considered indicative of a sunnah practice because his actions in worship are generally for emulation unless there is evidence of specificity.
Here, the action is explicit and no counter-evidence, so it establishes a preferred method.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Zahir al-Riwayah reports that the single follower stands behind the imam. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the follower aligns his toes with the imam's heels.
The author considers these views, then states that the first (right side) is apparent (al-awwal huwa al-zahir).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author's choice of the right side as the apparent view means it is the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) for fatwa, despite the other transmissions.
This is a common pattern: the school sometimes prefers a position that contradicts Zahir al-Riwayah based on strength of evidence.

ترجمہ اور جو شخص ایک شخص کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے تو اس کو اپنے دائیں کھڑا کرے۔ دلیل ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما کی حدیث ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کو نماز پڑھائی اور ان کو اپنے دائیں طرف کھڑا کیا اور مقتدی امام سے پیچھے نہ رہے اور امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ مندی اپنی انگلیوں کو امام کی ایڑی کے برابر رکھے اور اول ہی ظاہر ہے اور اگر اس ایک مقتدی نے امام کے پیچھے یا بائیں طرف نماز پڑھی تو بھی جائز ہے اور وہ گنہ گار ہے کیونکہ اس نے سنت کے خلاف کیا۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک مرد ایک مرد مقتدی کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے تو اس مقتدی کو اپنے دائیں کھڑا کرے۔ دلیل حدیث ابن عباس ہے۔ پوری حدیث یہ ہے بت عند خالتي ميمونه لا راقب صلوة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بالليل فانتبه فقال نامت العيون وغابت النجوم وبقى الحى القيوم ثم قرء اخر سورة ال عمران ان فى خلق السموات والارض واختلاف الليل والنهار..... الى اخرها ثم قام الى شن معلق فتوضأ وافتتح فقمت وتوضات ووقفت على يساره واخذ باذنی وادارنی خلفه حتى اقامنى عن يمينه . ( متفق علیہ ) یعنی ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما نے کہا کہ میں اپنی خالہ میمونہ کے یہاں رات سویا ہا کہ میں نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی رات کی نماز کو دیکھوں پر آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اٹھ کر کہا آنکھیں سو گئیں اور ستارے ڈوب گئے اور جی قیوم باقی ہے پھر آپ نے سورۃ آل عمران کی آخری آیتین ان في خلق السموات والارض و اختلاف الليل والنهار سے آخرت پڑھا پھر آپ نے ایک لٹکے ہوئے مشکیزہ سے پانی لے کر وضو کیا اور نماز شروع کی پس میں نے بھی اٹھ کر وضو کیا اور میں آپ کی بائی جہاں ان کو اللہ طرف کھڑا ہو گیا پس آپ نے میرا کان پکڑ کر مجھے اپنے پیچھے سے گھمایا یہاں تک کہ مجھ کو اپنی دائیں طرف کھڑا کیا۔ اس حدیث - اقتداء کرنا جانت معلوم ہوا کہ اگر امام کے ساتھ ایک مقتدی ہو تو اس کو دائیں طرف کھڑا کرنا مختار ہے۔ ظاہر الروایہ میں ہے کہ مقتدی واحد امام کے پیچھے کھڑا ہو۔ اور امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ مقتدی اپنی انگلیوں کو امام کی ایڑی کے برابر رکھے۔ اور اول ظاہر ہے۔ اور اگر ایک مقتدی نے ان ی تمام نمازوں کے پیچھے یا بائیں نماز پڑھی، تب بھی جائز ہے یعنی نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی البتہ گنہ گار ہوگا کیونکہ اس نے سنت کے خلاف عمل کیا۔
One follower: let him stand to the imam's right. Whoever prays with one person should make him stand on his right due to the hadith of Ibn Abbas, for the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed with him and made him stand on his right. And he should not be behind the imam. From Muhammad (al-Shaybani) it is narrated that he places his fingers at the imam's heel. The first is apparent. And if he prays behind him or on his left, it is permissible but he is doing wrong because he opposed the sunnah. Translation: And a person who prays with one person should make him stand on his right. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) led him in prayer and made him stand on his right side. The follower should not remain behind the imam. From Imam Muhammad it is narrated that he places his fingers at the level of the imam's heel. The first is apparent. And if this single follower prays behind the imam or on the left side, it is permissible but he is sinful because he opposed the sunnah. Explanation: The issue is that if a man prays with one male follower, he should make that follower stand on his right. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas. The full hadith is: (Ibn Abbas said) I stayed at the house of my aunt Maimunah to observe the Prophet's night prayer. He woke up and said, 'Eyes have slept, stars have set, and the Living, the Self-Subsisting remains.' Then he recited the end of Surah Al-Imran: 'Indeed in the creation of the heavens and the earth and the alternation of night and day...' to the end. Then he went to a hanging waterskin, performed wudu, and started prayer. So I got up, performed wudu, and stood on his left. He took hold of my ear and brought me around behind him until he made me stand on his right. (Agreed upon by Bukhari and Muslim). That is, Ibn Abbas said: I slept at my aunt Maimunah's to see the Prophet's night prayer. The Prophet got up and said... then he recited the last verses of Surah Al-Imran... then he took water from a hanging waterskin, made wudu, and began prayer. So I also got up, made wudu, and stood on his left. Then he took my ear and turned me behind him until he made me stand on his right. From this hadith, it is learned that if there is one follower with the imam, making him stand on the right is the preferred (mukhtar) way. In Zahir al-Riwayah, it is said that the single follower stands behind the imam. From Imam Muhammad it is narrated that the follower places his fingers at the imam's heel. The first is apparent. And if a single follower prays behind or on the left, it is also permissible, meaning the prayer is not invalid, but he will be sinful because he acted contrary to the sunnah.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the positioning of a single male follower in congregational prayer. The author states that the preferred (mukhtar) position is for the follower to stand on the imam's right, citing the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet placed him on his right. It also mentions Imam Muhammad's opinion that the follower should align his toes with the imam's heels. The text clarifies that while Zahir al-Riwayah says the follower stands behind, the first view (right side) is more apparent. If the follower stands behind or to the left, the prayer is valid but he is sinful for abandoning the sunnah. The full hadith is provided for context. The commentary emphasizes that the ruling is about the optimal sunnah position, not a condition of validity.

Key Terms
مختار (mukhtar): The preferred or chosen opinion among multiple valid opinions.
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted opinions from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, which are the primary sources of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a single male follower stands behind the imam (instead of to the right)?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but the follower is sinful for abandoning the sunnah.
C) The prayer is valid and there is no sin because it is permissible.
D) The prayer is invalid if done intentionally.

Key Takeaway
Standing to the imam's right for a single male follower is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah); following it earns reward, leaving it without excuse is sinful but does not invalidate the prayer.

Position of the Imam with Two Male Followers
Ruling on imam's position when leading two male followers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's position when leading two male followers, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and apply the preferred position (mufta bihi) in a practical scenario.

Core Idea
Imam stands ahead; standing between is permissible but not preferred.

When an imam leads two male followers, a key question arises: should he stand ahead of them or between them? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue, where Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf differ, each relying on different evidence. Understanding this ruling clarifies an important detail of congregational prayer etiquette (adab).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? Leading two male followers in obligatory prayer. Identify the legal classification (hukm) of the imam's position according to the preferred Hanafi view.
The hukm is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
State the position of Abu Hanifa (imam ahead) and Abu Yusuf (imam between them). Note that the dispute is within the Hanafi school itself.
Abu Yusuf's view is based on an athar from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud.
3
Examine the proofs (dalil)
What evidence does each side present? Abu Hanifa relies on the Prophet's action with Anas and the orphan. Abu Yusuf relies on the practice of Ibn Mas'ud. Understand the nature of each proof: prophetic sunnah vs. companion's action (athar).
The Prophet's action is for virtue; the athar indicates permissibility.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
Why does the text prefer Abu Hanifa's view? The Prophet's action is primary. Additionally, Ibn Mas'ud's action may have been due to space constraints, weakening its evidentiary value.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is imam ahead.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? In practice, the imam may choose either position, but standing ahead is more virtuous and recommended. Standing between is permissible but less excellent.
This affects the prayer's completeness of merit (afdaliyyah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رو مقتدی ہوں تو امام مقدم ہو جائے
اور ہمارے
نہیں بنا کی جاتے
اخروهن
وان ام اثنين تقدم عليهما وعن ابى يوسف يتوسطهما ونقل ذلك عن عبد الله بن مسعود ولنا انه عليه السلام تشريح. تقدم على انس واليتيم حين صلى بهما فهذا للافضلية والاثر دليل الاباحة ترجمہ اور اگر دو مردوں کی امامت کی تو امام دونوں پر مقدم ہو۔ اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ امام دونوں کے بیچ میں کھڑا ہو ۔ اور علاوہ مکان حصہ ابن مسعود سے منقول ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم انس اور یتیم سے آگے کھڑے ہوئے جب کہ دونوں کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی امام بننے کا حق پس یہ افضلیت کے لئے ہے اور اثر مباح ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔
اور بعض
تشریح اور اگر امام کے علاوہ دو مقتدی ہوں تو امام ان دونوں سے آگے کھڑا ہو اور امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ امام ان دونوں سے کیا ہے چنا نچے درمیان میں کھڑا ہو اور درمیان میں کھڑا ہونا عبداللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے منقول ہے چنانچہ روایت کیا گیا کہ ابن مسعود رضی را کو مقدم کرتا ۔ تعالٰی عنہ نے علقمہ اور اسود کو نماز پڑھائی اور ابن مسعود دونوں کے درمیان کھڑے ہوئے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب حضور ہے۔ رہا بچہ کے انس اور یتیم کو نماز پڑھائی تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم ان دونوں سے آگے کھڑے ہوئے پس آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا آگے کھڑا ہونا افضلیت کی دلیل ہے؟ جا نہیں ہو۔ ابن مسعود کا اثر مباح ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ ابراہیم تھی نے کہا کہ ان مسعودؓ سے روایت کی گئی کہ جگہ کے تنگ ہونے کی وجہ سے ایسا کیا گیا پس اب ابن مسعودؓ کے اثرسے لباد جائے کیا ہے بھی ثابت نہیں ہو گی۔
If there are two followers, the imam takes precedence. And according to Abu Yusuf, he stands between them, and that is narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. And our proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) took precedence over Anas and the orphan when he prayed with them; this is for superiority, and the effect (athar) is evidence of permissibility. Translation: And if he leads two men, the imam takes precedence over them. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the imam stands between them, and this is also narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. And our proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood ahead of Anas and the orphan when he prayed with them. So this (standing ahead) is for virtue, and the effect (from Ibn Mas'ud) is evidence of permissibility. And some explanation: And if there are two followers besides the imam, the imam stands ahead of both. And from Imam Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the imam stands between them, and standing between them is narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. Thus it is reported that Ibn Mas'ud led Alqamah and Aswad in prayer and he stood between them. And our proof is that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) led Anas and the orphan in prayer, he stood ahead of both. So the Prophet's standing ahead is evidence of virtue, not obligation. Ibn Mas'ud's effect is evidence of permissibility. Ibrahim (an-Nakha'i) said that it is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud that he did so because of the narrowness of the place. So now permissibility cannot be established from Ibn Mas'ud's effect.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the imam's position when leading two male followers. The Hanafi position (as stated by Imam Abu Hanifa) is that the imam stands ahead of the followers, based on the Prophet's practice with Anas and an orphan. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the imam stands between them, citing the practice of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. The text provides evidence for each: the Prophet's action indicates the preferred/optimal way (afdaliyyah), while Ibn Mas'ud's action shows permissibility (ibahah). Additionally, a report from Ibrahim an-Nakha'i suggests that Ibn Mas'ud's action was due to space constraints, thus it cannot be used to establish general permissibility. The preferred (mukhtar) position is that the imam stands ahead.

Key Terms
اثر (athar): A narration from a Companion (Sahabi) rather than from the Prophet; here referring to the practice of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud.
افضلیت (afdaliyyah): Superiority or virtue; an action that is better or more excellent but not obligatory.
مباح (mubah): Permissible; an action that is legally allowed without blame or reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view in this passage, where should the imam stand when leading two male followers?
A) Between the two followers.
B) Ahead of the two followers.
C) Behind the two followers.
D) Either ahead or between, both are equally virtuous.

Key Takeaway
The imam should stand ahead of two male followers as a sunnah; standing between is permissible but less virtuous.

Position of Imam with One or Two Followers
Rulings on where the imam stands relative to followers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred positions for one and two followers relative to the imam, explain the difference between sunnah and permissible, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
The preferred position for a single follower is the right; for two, the imam stands ahead.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies the rulings on where followers should stand in congregational prayer. The hadith of Anas (RA) provides the basis for the preferred positions. However, there are nuanced differences within the Hanafi school regarding what is considered sunnah versus merely permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act being ruled: the position of the follower(s) relative to the imam. Distinguish cases: one follower and two followers.
2
Locate the dalil from hadith
The author cites the hadith of Anas (RA) where the Prophet (SAW) placed him on the right. Identify the specific phrase used as proof.
The key phrase: 'ثم أخذ بأذني فحولني عن يمينه'
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith indicate preference (istihbab) rather than obligation? The Prophet's action demonstrates sunnah, not fard.
The Prophet's action is taken as evidence for preferability, not obligation.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Abu Yusuf holds a different view for two followers: the imam should stand between them. What is his proof?
The narration from Ibn Mas'ud (RA) is cited as evidence for permissibility.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The author prefers the view that the imam stands ahead for two, and the single follower on the right. State the tarjih basis.
The hadith of the Prophet (SAW) is given priority as evidence for preference.

باب الامامة
باقی ہے پھر آپ نے سورۃ آل عمران کی آخری آیتین ان في خلق السموات والارض و اختلاف الليل والنهار سے آخرت پڑھا پھر آپ نے ایک لٹکے ہوئے مشکیزہ سے پانی لے کر وضو کیا اور نماز شروع کی پس میں نے بھی اٹھ کر وضو کیا اور میں آپ کی بائی جہاں ان کو اللہ طرف کھڑا ہو گیا پس آپ نے میرا کان پکڑ کر مجھے اپنے پیچھے سے گھمایا یہاں تک کہ مجھ کو اپنی دائیں طرف کھڑا کیا۔ اس حدیث - اقتداء کرنا جانت معلوم ہوا کہ اگر امام کے ساتھ ایک مقتدی ہو تو اس کو دائیں طرف کھڑا کرنا مختار ہے۔ ظاہر الروایہ میں ہے کہ مقتدی واحد امام کے پیچھے کھڑا ہو۔ اور امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ مقتدی اپنی انگلیوں کو امام کی ایڑی کے برابر رکھے۔ اور اول ظاہر ہے۔ اور اگر ایک مقتدی نے ان ی تمام نمازوں کے پیچھے یا بائیں نماز پڑھی، تب بھی جائز ہے یعنی نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی البتہ گنہ گار ہوگا کیونکہ اس نے سنت کے خلاف عمل کیا۔
وان ام اثنين تقدم عليهما وعن ابى يوسف يتوسطهما ونقل ذلك عن عبد الله بن مسعود ولنا انه عليه السلام تقدم على انس واليتيم حين صلى بهما فهذا للافضلية والاثر دليل الاباحة
Chapter of Imamah. Then he recited the last two verses of Surah Al-Imran from 'Inna fi khalq al-samawati wal-ard' to the end, then he took water from a hanging waterskin, performed wudu, and started prayer. So I also got up, performed wudu, and stood on his left, so the Prophet grabbed my ear and turned me around from behind until he made me stand on his right. From this hadith it is known that if there is one follower with the imam, it is chosen to make him stand on the right. In Zahir al-Riwayah, the single follower stands behind the imam. And from Imam Muhammad it is narrated that the follower aligns his toes with the imam's heels. The first is more apparent. And if one follower prays behind or to the left, it is also permissible, i.e., the prayer is not invalid, but he will be sinful for acting against the sunnah. And if he leads two, he stands ahead of them. From Abu Yusuf: he stands between them, and that is narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. Our proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood ahead of Anas and the orphan when he prayed with them. So this is for preference, and the athar (narration from Ibn Mas'ud) is evidence of permissibility.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya addresses the position of the imam relative to the followers in congregational prayer. It begins with a hadith narration: the Prophet (SAW) led Anas (RA) in prayer, and initially Anas stood on the left, but the Prophet turned him to the right. From this, the preferred position for a single male follower is on the imam's right. However, the Zahir al-Riwayah (the authoritative transmission within the Hanafi school) states that a single follower stands directly behind the imam. Imam Muhammad adds that the follower should align his toes with the imam's heels. The author notes that the first view (right side) is more apparent. If a follower prays behind or to the left, the prayer is valid but sinful due to violating the sunnah. For two followers, the imam stands ahead of them (Hanafi position). Abu Yusuf holds that the imam should stand between them, a view also attributed to Ibn Mas'ud. The Hanafi proof is the hadith where the Prophet stood ahead of Anas and the orphan, indicating that this is superior; the narration from Ibn Mas'ud is taken as evidence of permissibility, not obligation.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in congregational prayer
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The authoritative transmitted rulings in the six core books of Imam Muhammad

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The prayer is valid but he is sinful for violating the sunnah
C) The prayer is valid and he earns reward equal to standing on the right
D) The prayer is invalid only if he stands on the left

Key Takeaway
The position of followers is sunnah, not fard; violating the sunnah is sinful but does not invalidate the prayer.

Men Following a Woman or Child in Prayer: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling and evidence for impermissibility of men following a woman or child in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on men following a woman or child in prayer, explain the hadith evidence, and apply the principle that strong (fard) cannot be built on weak (nafl).

Core Idea
A woman or child cannot lead men in prayer because the strong cannot be built on the weak.

This lesson examines a core ruling in congregational prayer: who may lead whom. The Hanafi position holds that an adult male may not follow a woman or a pre-pubescent boy. This ruling is based on clear prophetic guidance and a fundamental principle of fiqh. We will unpack the evidence, explore the internal Hanafi dispute over taraweeh and sunan, and understand why the chosen view prohibits it in all prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the core ruling: men cannot follow a woman or child in prayer. Note the exception for a child following a child.
2
Analyze the evidence for women
Examine the hadith 'اخر من حيث اخرهن الله' and how it proves women should not lead men. Understand the linguistic and legal implications.
The word 'حيث' indicates physical placement in prayer rows.
3
Analyze the evidence for children
Understand why a child's prayer is considered nafl even if he intends fard, and why a fard prayer cannot be built on a nafl prayer.
Key principle: al-qawi la yabni ala al-da'if.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify the different views among Hanafi scholars: Abu Yusuf and scholars of Balkh allowed following a child in absolute nafl, taraweeh, and sunan; Muhammad and scholars of Ma wara'an Nahr did not.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The mukhtar (chosen) position is impermissibility in all prayers. Understand the tarjih based on the deficiency of a child's prayer and the consensus that no qada is required upon invalidation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز للرجال ان يقتدوا بامرأة أو صبى اما المرأة فلقوله عليه السلام اخروهن من حيث اخرهن الله لا يجوز تقديمها واما الصبى فلانه متنفل فلا يجوز اقتداء المفترض به وفى التراويح والسنن المطلقة جوزه مشائخ بلخ ولم يجوزه مشائخنا و منهم من حقق الخلاف فى النفل المطلق بين ابی یوسف و بین محمد والمختار انه لايجوز في الصلوات كلها لان نقل الصبي دون نقل البالغ حيث لا يلزمه القضاء بالافسان بالاجماع ولا يبنى القوى على الضعيف بخلاف المظنون لانه مجتهد فيه فاعتبر العارض عدما وبخلاف اقتداء الصبي بالصبي لان الصلوة متحدة
It is not permissible for men to follow a woman or a boy. As for the woman, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Put them back where Allah put them,' so it is not permissible to put her forward. As for the boy, because he is performing supererogatory prayer (nafl), so it is not permissible for one performing obligatory prayer to follow him. Regarding taraweeh and the absolute sunan, the scholars of Balkh allowed it, but our scholars did not allow it. And among them, some investigated the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding absolute nafl. The chosen view is that it is not allowed in all prayers because the nafl of a boy is less than the nafl of an adult, since he is not required to make it up by invalidating it by consensus, and the strong is not built on the weak. Contrary to the maznun (prayer performed under doubt) because it is a matter of ijtihad, so the impediment is considered non-existent. And contrary to the following of a boy by a boy, because the prayer is unified.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya provides the ruling that men (adult males) may not follow a woman or a pre-pubescent boy in congregational prayer. The proof for women is the Prophetic hadith: 'اخر من حيث اخرهن الله' (Put them back where Allah put them), indicating that women are to be behind men in prayer; thus a woman leading men would contradict this placement. For a boy, the reason is that he is performing nafl (voluntary) prayer even if he intends fard, because his prayer counts as nafl due to his non-obligation. Therefore, one performing fard (obligatory prayer) cannot follow a mutanawwil (one performing nafl). This is based on the legal principle that a person performing a higher obligation cannot rely on a person performing a lesser act. However, there was a dispute among later Hanafi scholars regarding taraweeh and the absolute sunan (sunan mutlaqa, including non-emphasized sunan like the regular sunan before and after fard prayers, as well as 'id, witr, etc. according to some). The scholars of Balkh allowed it, but the scholars of Ma wara'an Nahr (Transoxiana, e.g., Bukhara and Samarkand) did not. Some of our scholars detailed the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf allowed following a boy in absolute nafl, while Muhammad did not. The relied-upon (mukhtar) position is that it is not allowed in any prayer. The reasoning is that a boy's nafl is deficient compared to an adult's because if he invalidates it, he is not required to make it up (by consensus of the school), so his prayer is weaker; the stronger (adult's fard) cannot be built on the weaker (child's nafl). The exception is the 'maznun' prayer (a prayer performed under the assumption of obligation, where the person later discovers it was not obligatory). In that case, following is allowed because the maznun is a matter of ijtihad, and the apparent impediment is considered non-existent. Additionally, a child following another child is allowed because both are performing nafl, so their prayers are of the same category.

Key Terms
متنفل (mutanawwil): One performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer
مظنون (maznun): A prayer performed under the assumption that it is obligatory, later discovered not to be
سنن مطلقة (sunan mutlaqa): Absolute sunan, including the regular sunan (rawatib) tied to fard prayers, as well as 'id, witr (according to some), etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi mukhtar position prohibit men from following a child in prayer?
A) Because the child cannot make the proper intention
B) Because the child's prayer is considered nafl and is deficient, as he is not required to repeat it if invalidated
C) Because the child has not reached puberty and cannot be an imam at all
D) Because the hadith explicitly forbids it

Key Takeaway
Men cannot follow a woman or child in prayer because the strong (fard) cannot be built on the weak (nafl), and the hadith places women behind men.

Men may not follow a woman in prayer
Ruling that men cannot follow a woman in prayer, with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women leading men in prayer and explain the proof from the hadith 'أخرهن من حيث أخرهن الله' using both interpretations.

Core Idea
A woman cannot lead men in prayer because the Prophet commanded to 'delay them'—she may not be advanced in the imamate.

In this passage, the author presents the clear Hanafi ruling that it is impermissible for a woman to be the imam for men in prayer. The evidence is drawn from a prophetic command that indicates women are to be placed behind men, both physically and in authority. Understanding this proof requires examining the key term 'حيث' and its two possible meanings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that it is not permissible for men to follow a woman (or a child) in prayer. Focus on the woman's case.
2
Extract the primary evidence
The hadith 'أخرهن من حيث أخرهن الله' is cited as the proof.
This is a sunnah ahad, relying on the transmitter's reliability.
3
Analyze the term 'حيث'
Two interpretations are given: first, as a place (مکان), referring to the prayer rows; second, as a cause (تعلیل), indicating general deferment.
The Hanafi school uses both readings to support the ruling.
4
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
The imperative 'أخرهن' indicates obligation (wujub) per Hanafi usul. Therefore, the command to delay women is binding.
No context shifts the imperative from obligation.
5
Conclude the ruling
Since Allah has delayed women in place and in leadership, advancing them as imam is impermissible.
The ruling is haram and the prayer of men behind a woman is invalid.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم ترجمہ مردوں کو جائز نہیں کہ وہ عورت یا بچہ کی اقتداء کریں بہر حال عورت تو اس لئے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ عورتوں کو مؤخر کرو جہاں ان کو اللہ نے مؤخر کیا پس عورت کا مقدم کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ مردوں کے لئے نہ عورت کی اقتداء جائز ہے اور نہ بچہ کی عورت کی اقتداء جائز نہ ہونا تو اس لئے ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا أخرهن من حيث أخرهن الله وجه استدلال یہ ہے کہ لفظ حیث سے مراد مکان ہے اور جس مکان میں عورتوں کی تاخیر واجب ہو علاو و مکان صلوۃ کے کوئی مکان نہیں ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے عورتوں کو مکان صلوۃ میں مؤخر کیا ہے یعنی اس کو مردوں کے لئے امام بننے کا حق نہیں دیا ہے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ حيث تعلیل کے لئے ہے اب ترجمہ یہ ہوگا کہ عورتوں کو مؤخر کرو اس لئے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ان کو مؤخر کیا ہے چنانچہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ان کو شہادت دراخت سلطنت اور تمام ولایات میں مؤخر کیا ہے پس جب اللہ تعالی نے عورت کو مؤخر کیا تو اس کو مقدم کرنا یعنی امام بنانا بھی جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
Chapter of Imamate. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 2 Translation: It is not permissible for men to follow a woman or a child. As for a woman, because the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Delay women from where Allah has delayed them.' So advancing a woman is not permissible. Explanation of the issue: It is neither permissible for men to follow a woman nor a child. The reason a woman's following is impermissible is that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Delay them from where Allah has delayed them.' The point of inference is that the word 'where' refers to place, and there is no place where women are required to be delayed except the place of prayer. Thus it is established that Allah has delayed women in the place of prayer, i.e., He has not given them the right to be imams for men. Some have said that 'where' is for causation. The translation would then be: 'Delay women because Allah has delayed them,' meaning He has delayed them in testimony, inheritance, authority, and all positions of governance. So when Allah has delayed a woman, it is not permissible to advance her, i.e., make her an imam.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a woman cannot lead men in prayer. It is a ruling statement supported by proof. The author first mentions the general rule that men cannot follow a woman or a child. Then he focuses on the woman's case. The primary evidence is the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Delay them from where Allah has delayed them.' Two interpretations are given: First, 'where' means the place of prayer, so women are to be behind men in prayer rows. Second, 'where' indicates a cause, meaning women are deferred in all leadership roles. Therefore, a woman cannot be an imam for men. This ruling is agreed upon in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
حيث (haythu): In this context, it either means 'place' (makan) or 'cause' (ta'lil), both indicating where women are deferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Consensus of scholars
D) Analogy with inheritance

Key Takeaway
A woman cannot lead men in prayer because the prophetic command to defer women includes the role of imam, making it impermissible (haram).

Ruling on a Child Leading Prayer for Adults
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an adult praying behind a child and explain the proof, the intra-school dispute, and the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
An adult cannot follow a child in prayer because the child's prayer is weak—it lacks qada liability.

The question of whether an adult can pray behind a child is not merely practical but reveals how the Hanafi school evaluates prayer validity through the principle of qada (making up a broken prayer). This lesson unpacks the dispute between the scholars of Balkh and Transoxiana, and between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, to clarify the preferred ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
Identify the default position: an adult cannot follow a child in fard prayers because the child is performing nafl while the adult intends fard.
2
Identify the disputed scope
Note where the dispute arises: in taraweeh and absolute sunnah (nafl) prayers. The scholars of Balkh permitted it; the scholars of Transoxiana did not.
Also note the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on absolute nafl.
3
Compare the proofs
Hanafi proof: The child's nafl is weaker because if invalidated, no qada is required by consensus, whereas an adult must make up a broken nafl. Thus a strong act (adult's prayer) cannot be built on a weak one. The opposing proof: analogy (qiyas) to maznunah prayer, where following is allowed despite the imam's deficiency.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes maznunah (a matter of ijtihad, deficiency is temporary and overlooked) from the child's deficiency (permanent and not subject to ijtihad). Hence the analogy fails.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author (Sahib al-Hidayah) and the Transoxiana scholars adopt impermissibility in all prayers. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text

اور بہر حال بچہ تو اس لئے کہ وہ نفل پڑھنے والا ہے لہذا مفترض کو اس کی اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور تراویح اور سنن مطلقہ میں مشائخ بلخ نے اس کو جائز رکھا اور ہمارے مشائخ نے اس کو جائز قرار نہیں دیا۔ اور ہمارے مشائخ میں سے بعض نے ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے درمیان نفل مطلق کی صورت میں اختلاف محقق کیا۔ اور مختار یہ ہے کہ ی تمام نمازوں میں جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ بچہ کانفل بالغ سے مکمتر ہے اس لئے کہ فضل فاسد کر دینے سے بالا جماع بچہ پر قضاء لازم نہیں آتی اور نہیں بنا کی جاتی ہے قوی کی ضعیف پر بر خلاف نماز مظنون کے کیونکہ وہ مجتہد فیہ ہے پس اعتبار کیا گیا عارض معدوم بر خلاف بچہ کا اقتداء کرنا، کچھ کے ساتھ کیونکہ نماز متحد ہے۔
رہا بچہ کی امامت کا بیان تو اس کی امامت اس لئے جائز نہیں کہ وہ تو نفل ادا کرنے والا ہے لہذا فرض ادا کرنے کے لئے اس کی اقتداء باڑا نہیں ہوگی یعنی بالغ کی فرض نماز اس کے پیچھے جائز نہ ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا ہے کہ تراویح اور سنن مطلقہ میں اختلاف ہے۔ مشائخ تان کے قول کے مطابق تراویح اور سنن مطلقہ میں نابالغ بچہ کی اقتداء کرنا جائز ہے اور ہمارے مشائخ یعنی مشائخ ما وراء النهر نے اس کو جالا کیا ہے۔ سنن مطلقہ سے مراد وہ سنن رواتب ہیں جو فرائض سے پہلے اور فرائض کے بعد شروع ہوئیں ہیں۔ ایک روایت کے مطابق حید کی نماز بھی سنت ہے۔ اور وتر ، کسوف ، خوف اور استقاء کی نماز بھی صاحبین کے نزدیک سنت ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ سنت نمازوں میں اگر نا بالغ بچہ نے امامت کی تو مشائخ بلخ کے نزدیک بالغ مردوں کے لئے اس کی اقتداء کرنا جائز ے اور ماوراء انہ یعنی نار اور سمرقند کے علماء و مشائخ نے اس کو جائز کہا ہے۔ مشائخ بلخ نے مظنونہ نماز پر قیاس کیا ہے۔ مظنونہ نماز یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے یہ خیال کیا کہ اس کے ذمہ نماز واجب ہے پس اس نے اس گمان کے ساتھ وہ نماز ادا کرنی شروع کر دی پھر درمیان میں کوئی مفسد پیش آگیا اور نماز ٹوٹ گئی پھر معلوم نہوا کہ اس کے ذمہ واجب نہ تھی تو اب شروع کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کا قضاء کرنا واجب ہے پائیں؟ تو اس کے بارے میں ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک حکم یہ ہے کہ قضاء واجب نہیں ہے البتہ امام زفر کے نزدیک قضاء واجب ہے۔ پھر اگر نفل ادا کرنے والا بالغ آدمی مظنونہ نماز ادا کرنے والے کی اقتداء کرے تو جائز ہے۔ اب مشائخ بلخ کے قیاس کا حاصل یہ ہوگا کہ نفل نماز شروع کرنے سے واجب ہو جاتی ہے اور مظنونہ نماز واجب نہیں ہوتی ہے پیس

جواب یہ ہے اس
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد اشرف البدایہ شرر جب نفل پڑھنے والا مظنونہ نماز ادا کرنے والے کی اقتداء کر سکتا ہے تو ایسے ہی نفل ادا کرنے والا بچہ کی اقتداء کر سکتا ہے۔ ہو گا کہ تم میں سے اور ہمارے مشائخ میں سے بعض نے نفل مطلق کی صورت میں امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے درمیان اختلاف بیان کیا ہے چنانچہ راہ لیکن اگر کو ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ نفل مطلق میں بھی بالغ مرد کا بچہ کی اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور امام محمد نے اس کو جائز قرار دیا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ بالغ مرد کا بچہ کی اقتداء کرنا کسی بھی نماز میں جائز نہیں ہے خواہ نفل مطلق ہو یا موقت ہو۔ یہی ماوراءالنہر کے عورتوں سے معتقد مشائخ کا مذہب ہے اس مذہب مختار کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بچہ کی نفل نماز بالغ کی نفل نماز سے کمتر اور ادائی ہے کیونکہ بالا تفاق اگر بچے نفل نما نے ایک برڑھی شروع کر کے فاسد کر دے تو اس پر اس کی قضاء واجب نہیں ہوتی اور اگر بالغ نفل نماز فاسد کر دے تو اس کے ذمہ قضاء کرنا واجب ہے، میں ابو مالک اشتر قاعدہ ہے کہ قومی کی بنا ضعیف پر نہیں کی جاتی اس لئے بالغ کے نقل کی بنا ء بچے سے نفل پر نہیں کی جائے گی۔
ابناء كم حتى
بخلاف المظنون سے مشائخ بلخ کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بالغ کا بچہ کی اقتداء کرنے کو خان کی اقتداء تقدم فصف پیاس کرنا فاسد ہے کیونکہ نماز مظنون مختلف فیہ ہے، چنانچہ امام زفر کے نزدیک فاسد کرنے کی صورت میں خان پر قضاء کرنا واجب ہے کہا کہ اسے اشعہ بچہ کی نماز کہ اس کی قضاء بالا جماع واجب نہیں ہے۔ نیز طفولیت (بچنہ ) ایسا امر ہے جو بالغ ہونے تک بہر حال باقی رہے گا۔ پس بانی نماز دکھلاؤں پر کی نماز اس کی نماز سے متحد نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ فاسد کر دینے کی صورت میں بالغ پر قضاء واجب ہوتی ہے اور نا بالغ پر قضاء واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ پھر ابو مالک آگے اس کے برخلاف مظنون کہ فن ایک عارضی چیز ہے۔ لہذا اس کو معدوم معتبر کیا گیا پس اب اگر نفل پڑھنے والے نے مظنون نماز پڑھنے عقلی دلیل والے امام کے پیچھے اقتداء کی تو دونوں کی نماز متحد ہوسکتی ہے بالخصوص امام زفر کے نزدیک کیونکہ فساد کی صورت میں دونوں پر قضاء واجب ہو جاتی ہے۔
حاصل یہ کہ بالغ اور نا بالغ کی نماز غیر متحد ہے اور بالغ اور خان کی نماز متحد ہے بالخصوص امام زفر کے نزدیک پس اس فرق کے ہونے ہوئے اقتداء بالغ بالصحی کو اقتداء بالظان پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ اس کے بر خلاف نابالغ کا نا بالغ کی اقتداء کرنا جائز ہے کیونکہ دونوں کی نماز متحد ہے اس لئے کہ دونوں میں سے کسی پر قضاء واجب نہیں ہے پس یہ ضعیف کی بنا ضعیف پر ہوگی۔
And as for a child, it is because he is performing a nafl prayer, so one performing a fard cannot follow him. In taraweeh and absolute sunnah prayers, the scholars of Balkh permitted it, but our scholars did not permit it. Some of our scholars have established a disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad in the case of absolute nafl. The chosen view is that it is not permissible in any prayer because the child's nafl is inferior to the adult's nafl. This is because if a child starts a nafl and invalidates it, by consensus he is not required to make it up, unlike an adult. And the strong is not built on the weak. This is unlike the maznunah prayer because it is a matter of ijtihad; thus a temporary deficiency is considered nonexistent. This is contrary to following a child because the prayers are not unified. Now the explanation of the matter of the child's imamate: His imamate is not permissible because he is performing a nafl, so following him for a fard will not work, i.e., an adult's fard prayer behind him is not valid. The author of Hidayah says there is a difference of opinion in taraweeh and absolute sunnahs. According to the scholars of Balkh, it is permissible to follow a minor child in taraweeh and absolute sunnahs, but our scholars (of Transoxiana) have not permitted it. By absolute sunnahs are meant the regular sunnahs before and after the obligatory prayers. In one narration, Eid prayer is also sunnah. And witr, eclipse, fear, and rain prayers are also sunnah according to the Sahibayn. The upshot is that if a minor child leads in sunnah prayers, the scholars of Balkh permit adults to follow him, while the scholars of Transoxiana (Bukhara and Samarkand) do not. The scholars of Balkh analogized this to the maznunah prayer. The maznunah prayer is when a person thinks that a prayer is obligatory upon him, so he starts it, then during it something invalidates it, and it is discovered it was not obligatory. Then is it obligatory to make it up? According to the three Imams, it is not obligatory, but according to Imam Zufar it is. Then if an adult performing nafl follows someone performing maznunah, it is permissible. So the analogy of the Balkh scholars is: since a nafl becomes obligatory once started, and maznunah is not obligatory, but still following is allowed, similarly following a child should be allowed. The response: The difference is that the maznunah prayer is subject to ijtihad (disputed), so it can be unified, but the child's prayer is not disputed; it is clearly inferior. Therefore, an adult's prayer cannot be built on a child's weak prayer. In summary, the adult's and child's prayers are not unified, whereas the adult's and the maznunah-prayer person's prayers are unified, especially according to Imam Zufar. So comparing an adult following a child to an adult following a maznunah-prayer person is a dissimilar analogy. On the contrary, a minor following another minor is permissible because their prayers are unified since neither owes qada.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a detailed dispute about whether an adult can pray behind a child. It begins with the general ruling that a child leading an adult is impermissible because the child's prayer is considered inferior. However, a disagreement is recorded: the scholars of Balkh permitted it in taraweeh and absolute sunnahs (like regular nafl), while the scholars of Transoxiana did not. There is also an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Yusuf (who disallowed) and Imam Muhammad (who allowed in absolute nafl). The preferred view (mukhtar) adopted by the author is that it is not permissible in any prayer, including nafl. The proof is that a child's prayer, if invalidated, does not require qada (unlike an adult's), so it is weaker; a strong act cannot be based on a weak one. The Balkh scholars analogized to the maznunah (presumed) prayer, where an adult can follow another adult who thought a prayer was obligatory. The response refutes this: maznunah is a matter of ijtihad, so it can be considered unified with the follower's prayer, while the child's prayer is not unified because the child has no liability for qada. Hence the analogy is invalid. The passage concludes that a minor may follow another minor because their prayers are equally weak and unified.

Key Terms
مظنونہ نماز (maznunah salah): A prayer that a person starts thinking it is obligatory upon him, but it later turns out it was not obligatory. Its ruling on qada is disputed among the Hanafi imams.
مفترض (muftarid): A person performing an obligatory prayer (fard).
نفل مطلق (nafl mutlaq): Absolute supererogatory prayer, not tied to a specific time or occasion (as opposed to sunnah mu'akkadah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is an adult's following a child in prayer considered impermissible according to the preferred view?
A) Children cannot read Quran properly
B) The child's prayer is weaker because he is not responsible for qada if it breaks
C) Children are not allowed to enter mosques
D) The adult's prayer would be incomplete

Key Takeaway
An adult may not follow a child in any prayer because the child's lack of qada liability makes his prayer weak and unfit to support the adult's prayer.

Order of Rows in Congregational Prayer
Ruling on row arrangement with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the arrangement of rows in congregational prayer and cite the hadith proof, explaining its legal implication.

Core Idea
Row order: mature men first, then boys, then women — to preserve order and avoid fitna.

This lesson addresses the sunnah arrangement of rows behind the imam. The Hanafi school, following a specific hadith, orders the rows as men, then boys, then women. Understanding this arrangement helps maintain proper decorum and prevents potential corruption in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on row arrangement
The passage states that rows should be arranged: men, then boys, then women. The hukm is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
2
Locate the primary proof
The hadith: 'لِيَلِنِي مِنْكُمْ أُولُو الْأَحْلَامِ وَالنُّهَى' – a command from the Prophet ﷺ.
The imperative 'لِيَلِنِي' indicates recommendation.
3
Analyze the linguistic evidence
The term 'أولو الأحلام والنهى' refers to mature men with sound intellect and understanding. This establishes that they should be nearest to the imam.
The phrase specifies adult males.
4
Understand the secondary reasoning
The passage also mentions that adjacency (muhadhat) between unrelated men and women is a cause of corruption in prayer, so women are placed behind boys to avoid fitna.
This is an independent reason from the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صفوں کی ترتیب کیسے ہوگی؟ 
و يصف الرجال ثم الصبيان ثم النساء لقوله عليه السلام ليليني منكم اولو الاحلام والنهي ولان المحاذاة مفسدة فيؤخرون 
ترجمہ اور صف باندھیں مرد پھر بچے پھر عورتیں، کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ قریب رہیں مجھ سے تم میں سے بالغ مرد ، اور اس لئے کہ ہے اور مرد ہے عورت کی محاذات مفسد نماز ہے اس لئے عورتیں مؤخر کی جائیں۔ 
تشریح اس عبارت میں امام کے پیچھے کھڑے ہونے کی ترتیب کا بیان ہے، چنانچہ فرمایا کہ امام کے پیچھے سب سے پہلے مردگرے تشریح صور ہوں پھر ان کے پیچھے بچے کھڑے ہوں اور ان کے پیچھے عورتیں کھڑی ہوں ۔ دلیل حضور کایہ قول ہے لیلینی منکم اولوا الاحلام والنهي امر کا صیغہ ہے ولی سے ماخوذ ہے جس کے معنی قریب ہونے کے ہیں۔ احلام حکم با ضم کی جمع ہے علم وہ چیز جو سونے 14 فاسد نہ ہو۔ اور کے دیکھتا ہے لیکن اس کا غالب استعمال خواب کی دلالت بلوغ کی چیز میں ہے اور نبی نبیہ کی جمع ہے معنی عقل ہیں ، اب حدیث کا مطلب بالاتفاق فاسد نہیں
How should the rows be arranged? And they line up: men, then boys, then women, because of his statement ﷺ: 'Let those who are sensible and mature be near me,' and because adjacency [between unrelated men and women] is a source of corruption, so they are delayed. Translation: And line up: men, then boys, then women, because the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Let the adult men be close to me,' and because the adjacency of a woman and a man is a cause of corruption in prayer, therefore women are to be placed at the back. Explanation: This passage states the order of standing behind the imam. So it says: behind the imam, first the men, then behind them the boys, and behind them the women. The proof is the Prophet's saying: 'Let those of you who are mature and understanding be near me.' 'لي' is from 'ولی' meaning closeness. 'أحلام' is the plural of 'حلم' meaning intelligence. 'النهى' is the plural 'نبی'? meaning intellect. So the meaning of the hadith is by consensus... [the text becomes unclear]
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage explains the sunnah arrangement of rows in congregational prayer. The order is: first men (baligh males), then behind them boys (children who have not reached puberty), and behind them women. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet: 'Let those of you who are mature and sensible be near me.' The word 'oloo al-ahlam' refers to men with understanding and maturity. Another reason given is that a woman standing directly adjacent to a man (muhadhaat) is a cause of corruption of the prayer, so women are delayed to avoid mixing. This arrangement ensures order and prevents fitna.

Key Terms
أولو الأحلام والنهى (ulu al-ahlam wa al-nuha): Men who have reached puberty and possess sound intellect and understanding; i.e., mature, responsible males.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct order of rows behind the imam?
A) Men, then women, then boys
B) Women, then men, then boys
C) Men, then boys, then women
D) Boys, then men, then women

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school orders rows as men, then boys, then women, based on the hadith and to avoid fitna.

Adult Following a Child in Nafl Prayer: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute with rational proof and qiyas ma' al-fariq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an adult following a child in nafl prayer, explain the reasoning based on the weakness of the child's prayer, and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
An adult cannot follow a child in prayer because strength cannot be built upon permanent weakness.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: whether an adult (baligh) may validly follow a child (sabi) in supererogatory (nafl) prayer. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that it is impermissible in all prayers, including absolute nafl. We will explore the evidence from al-Hidayah, the disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, and the critical distinction between the permanent weakness of a child's prayer and the temporary weakness of a 'maznun' (presumed valid) prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the relied-upon ruling (mufta bihi) from the passage: an adult man cannot follow a child in any prayer, whether absolute nafl or time-bound nafl.
This is the view of Imam al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah and the scholars of Transoxiana.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Note that Imam Abu Yusuf held it impermissible even in absolute nafl, while Imam Muhammad permitted it in absolute nafl. The passage presents the dispute and then settles on the stricter view.
The disagreement is confined to absolute nafl; both agree on fard and other prayers?
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Understand the key evidence: a child's nafl prayer is weaker because if invalidated, no qada (make-up) is required, whereas an adult must make up an invalidated nafl. The principle 'strength cannot be built on weakness' applies.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on the ruling of qada.
4
Analyze the counter-argument and response
The scholars of Balkh analogized to an adult following a person praying a maznun prayer, which is valid. The response distinguishes: a child's weakness is permanent (childhood persists), while maznun's weakness is temporary (presumed valid until proven otherwise). Hence, the analogy is invalid (qiyas ma' al-fariq).
This shows the importance of examining the illa (effective cause) carefully.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage concludes that the preferred view (al-mukhtar) is impermissibility in all prayers, following Abu Yusuf's position, and this is the operative ruling for fatwa.
This is a fatawa mutakhkhirin authority weight, not from the six core books.

جواب يہ ہے اس [؟] اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد [؟] اشرف البدایہ [؟] جب نفل پڑھنے والا مظنونہ نماز ادا کرنے والے کی اقتداء کر سکتا ہے تو ایسے ہی نفل ادا کرنے والا بچہ کی اقتداء کر سکتا ہے۔ ہو گا کہ تم میں سے اور ہمارے مشائخ میں سے بعض نے نفل مطلق کی صورت میں امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے درمیان اختلاف بیان کیا ہے چنانچہ راہ لیکن اگر کو ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ نفل مطلق میں بھی بالغ مرد کا بچہ کی اقتداء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور امام محمد نے اس کو جائز قرار دیا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ بالغ مرد کا بچہ کی اقتداء کرنا کسی بھی نماز میں جائز نہیں ہے خواہ نفل مطلق ہو یا موقت ہو۔ یہی ماوراءالنہر کے عورتوں سے معتقد مشائخ کا مذہب ہے اس مذہب مختار کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بچہ کی نفل نماز بالغ کی نفل نماز سے کمتر اور ادائی ہے کیونکہ بالا تفاق اگر بچے نفل نماز ایک بارہ شروع کر کے فاسد کر دے تو اس پر اس کی قضاء واجب نہیں ہوتی اور اگر بالغ نفل نماز فاسد کر دے تو اس کے ذمہ قضاء کرنا واجب ہے، [؟] میں ابو مالک اشتر قاعدہ ہے کہ قوۃ کی بنا ضعیف پر نہیں کی جاتی اس لئے بالغ کے نقل کی بنا بچے سے نفل پر نہیں کی جائے گی۔
ابناء كم حتى
بخلاف المظنون سے مشائخ بلخ کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بالغ کا بچہ کی اقتداء کرنے کو خان کی اقتداء تقدم [؟] فصف [؟] پیاس کرنا فاسد ہے کیونکہ نماز مظنون مختلف فیہ ہے، چنانچہ امام زفر کے نزدیک فاسد کرنے کی صورت میں خان پر قضاء کرنا واجب ہے کہا کہ اسے اشعہ بچہ کی نماز کہ اس کی قضاء بالا جماع واجب نہیں ہے۔ نیز طفولیت (بچنہ ) ایسا امر ہے جو بالغ ہونے تک بہر حال باقی رہے گا۔ پس بانی نماز دکھلاؤں پر کی نماز اس کی نماز سے متحد نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ فاسد کر دینے کی صورت میں بالغ پر قضاء واجب ہوتی ہے اور نا بالغ پر قضاء واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ پھر ابو مالک آگے اس کے برخلاف مظنون کہ فن ایک عارضی چیز ہے۔ لہذا اس کو معدوم معتبر کیا گیا پس اب اگر نفل پڑھنے والے نے مظنون نماز پڑھنے عقلی دلیل والے امام کے پیچھے اقتداء کی تو دونوں کی نماز متحد ہوسکتی ہے بالخصوص امام زفر کے نزدیک کیونکہ فساد کی صورت میں دونوں پر قضاء واجب ہو جاتی ہے۔
حاصل یہ کہ بالغ اور نا بالغ کی نماز غیر متحد ہے اور بالغ اور خان کی نماز متحد ہے بالخصوص امام زفر کے نزدیک پس اس فرق کے ہونے ہوئے اقتداء بالغ بالصحی کو اقتداء بالظان پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ اس کے بر خلاف نابالغ کا نا بالغ کی اقتداء کرنا جائز ہے کیونکہ دونوں کی نماز متحد ہے اس لئے کہ دونوں میں سے کسی پر قضاء واجب نہیں ہے پس یہ ضعیف کی بنا ضعیف پر ہوگی۔
Chapter of Imamate. The answer is this: Just as one praying nafl can follow one performing maznun prayer, similarly one praying nafl can follow a child. It will be that among you and some of our scholars have mentioned a difference between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad in the case of absolute nafl. Abu Yusuf said that even in absolute nafl, an adult man following a child is not permissible, and Imam Muhammad declared it permissible. The author of Hidayah said that an adult man following a child is not permissible in any prayer, whether absolute nafl or time-bound. This is the school of the respected scholars of beyond the river. The proof of this preferred school is that a child's nafl prayer is lower and inferior to an adult's nafl prayer because by consensus if a child starts a nafl prayer once and invalidates it, making it up is not obligatory upon him, whereas if an adult invalidates a nafl prayer, making it up is obligatory upon him. [The rule] from Abu Malik Ash'ari is that strength is not built upon weakness, therefore an adult's nafl cannot be built upon a child's nafl. Contrary to maznun, this is the answer to the analogy of the scholars of Balkh. The gist of the answer is that an adult following a child is like following in the prayer of Khan? [garbled] prayer is invalid? because maznun prayer is disputed. Thus according to Imam Zufar, in case of invalidation, making up is obligatory upon Khan? He said about the child's prayer that its making up is not obligatory by consensus. Also, childhood is a matter that remains as long as one is a minor. So the child's prayer will not be unified with the adult's prayer because in case of invalidation, making up is obligatory upon the adult and not upon the minor. Then Abu Malik, contrary to maznun, [holds] that since maznun is a temporary thing, it is considered non-existent. So if the one praying nafl follows behind an imam praying maznun with rational proof, then both prayers can be unified, especially according to Imam Zufar because in case of invalidation, making up becomes obligatory upon both. The conclusion is that the prayers of adult and minor are not unified, while the prayers of adult and Khan are unified, especially according to Imam Zufar. Therefore, with this difference, analogizing the following of an adult to a minor to the following to a maznun is an analogy with a difference. On the contrary, a minor following another minor is permissible because both prayers are unified, since making up is not obligatory upon either. So this is strength built upon weakness.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the ruling of an adult (baligh) following a child (sabi) in prayer, specifically in nafl (supererogatory) prayers. The passage begins by stating the issue and then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. According to the text, Imam Abu Yusuf held that even in absolute nafl (nafl mutlaq), it is not permissible for an adult to follow a child, while Imam Muhammad permitted it. The author of al-Hidayah, Imam al-Marghinani, then states the relied-upon position (al-mukhtar) that it is not permissible in any type of prayer, whether absolute nafl or time-bound nafl. This is also the view of the scholars of Transoxiana (Ma wara' al-nahr). The proof given is that a child's nafl prayer is weaker (ad'af) than an adult's because if a child invalidates his nafl, he is not required to make it up (qada), whereas an adult must make up an invalidated nafl. The principle cited is that strength (quwwa) cannot be built upon weakness. Therefore, since the child's prayer is weak (no qada obligation), the adult's prayer, which requires qada upon invalidation, cannot validly follow the child's. The text then addresses a counter-analogy from the scholars of Balkh, who analogized this case to an adult following a person praying a maznun (presumed valid) prayer. In that case, the adult's following is valid despite the maznun's prayer being weaker in some aspects. The response is that the two cases are different: in the case of a child, the child's prayer is permanently weak (childhood is an ongoing state), while in the case of maznun, the weakness is temporary (the maznun's prayer is considered valid until proven otherwise). Therefore, the adult following a child is qiyas ma' al-fariq (analogy with a difference). Finally, the text notes that a child following another child is permissible because both prayers are equal in weakness (no qada obligation for either).

Key Terms
نفل مطلق (nafl mutlaq): Supererogatory prayer without a specific time or cause, as opposed to raghaib or sunan muakkada.
مظنونہ نماز (maznunah salat): A prayer that is presumed valid (zann al-sihhah) but may have a latent defect.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or invalidated prayer after its time.
متحد (mutahid): Unified, meaning that both prayers are of the same legal status in terms of qada obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, why can an adult not follow a child in nafl prayer?
A) Because a child cannot be an imam under any circumstances.
B) Because the child's prayer is weaker (no qada obligation) and strength cannot be built on weakness.
C) Because the child's prayer is invalid by consensus.
D) Because the adult must always pray alone when a child is present.

Key Takeaway
An adult cannot validly follow a child in prayer because the child's prayer is permanently weak (no qada obligation), and the Hanafi school rules that strength cannot be built on weakness.
