Order of Rows in Congregational Prayer
Specifies the order of rows: men, then children, then women, with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of rows in congregational prayer and explain the textual and rational proofs for placing men, then boys, then women.

Core Idea
Prayer rows are ordered men, then boys, then women to avoid invalidation by alignment.

In congregational prayer, the arrangement of rows is not arbitrary; it is guided by prophetic practice and legal reasoning. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the preferred sequence: men closest to the imam, then boys, then women at the back. Understanding this order helps maintain the validity and discipline of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories and their order
List the three groups (men, boys, women) in the order they should stand behind the imam as stated in the passage.
The order is men first, then boys, then women.
2
Examine the primary hadith proof
Find the hadith: 'Let those of you who are of understanding and intelligence be near me' (لَيَلِنِي مِنْكُمْ أُولُو الْأَحْلَامِ وَالنُّهَى). Understand that this prioritizes mature men, and by extension boys come after men.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim and Musnad Ahmad.
3
Analyze the rational proof
The passage states that alignment (muhadhat) of a woman with a man invalidates the man's prayer. Therefore, women are placed behind to avoid this. Boys are less likely to cause such concerns and are placed before women.
This is a rational (ʿaqlī) proof based on the legal effect of muhadhat.
4
Evaluate the objection and response
Someone might object that the hadith only prioritizes men over boys, not boys over women. The passage responds by noting that boys are subordinate to men due to masculinity, and the Prophet's practice further confirms the order. A stronger proof is the hadith of Abu Malik al-Ash'ari where he arranged rows accordingly.
This shows the comprehensive nature of the evidence.

ہو گا کہ تم میں سے مجھ سے قریب وہ لوگ رہیں جو عاقل بالغ ہوں۔
لیکن اگر کوئی یہ کہے کہ یہ حدیث مردوں کو بچوں پر مقدم کرتا تو ثابت کرتی ہے مگر عورتوں پر بچوں کی تقدیم ثابت نہیں کرتی ، تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے احتمال رجولیت کی وجہ سے بچے مردوں کے تابع ہیں اور تابع متبوع کے بعد ہوتا ہے لہذا بچے مردوں کے بعد ہوں گے اور عورتوں سے مقدم ہوں گے اور جواب میں یہ بھی کہا جاسکتا ہے کہ عورتوں پر بچوں کی تقدیم حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فعل سے ثابت ہے کیونکہ حضور نے ایک برڑھی عورت کو یتیم نامی بالغ کے پیچھے کھڑا کیا تھا۔ زیادہ بہتر استدلال اس حدیث سے ہو سکتا ہے جس کو امام احمد نے اپنی مسند میں ابو مالک اشعری سے تخریج کیا ہے روایت کے الفاظ یہ ہیں انه قال يا معشر الا شعر بين اجتمعوا و اجمعو انساء کم و ابناء كم حتى اريكم صلاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فاجتمعوا وجمعوا ابناء هم ونساء هم ثم تو ضاواراهم كيف يتوضأ ثم تقدم فصف الرجال فى ادنى الصف وصف الولدان خلفهم وصف النساء خلف الصبيان ، یعنی ابو مالک اشعری نے کہا کہ اے اشعری قبیلہ کے لوگو! تم خود بھی جمع ہو جاؤ اور اپنی عورتوں : اولا د کو بھی جمع کر لو یہاں تک کہ میں تم کو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی نماز دکھلاؤں پس وہ خود بھی جمع ہو گئے اور اپنے بیٹوں اور عورتوں کو بھی بیج کیا پھر وضو کیا اور ان کو دکھلایا کہ آپ کس طرح وضو کرتے تھے۔ پھر ابو مالک آگے بڑھے پھر مردوں کی صف باندھی ، اور لڑکوں کی ان کے پیچھے اور عورتوں کی صف بچوں کے پیچھے بنائی۔ عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت کی محاذات مرد سے مفسد نماز ہے۔ اس لئے عورتیں مؤخر کی جائیں گی۔
And rows are arranged: men, then boys, then women, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Let those of you who are of understanding and intelligence be near me,' and because alignment (muhadhat) of a man and woman invalidates prayer, so women are delayed. Translation: And rows are arranged: men, then boys, then women, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Those of you who are mature and intelligent should be near me,' and because the alignment of a man and woman invalidates the prayer, therefore women are delayed. Commentary: In this phrase, the order of standing behind the imam is explained. So it is said that behind the imam, first men, then behind them boys, and behind them women. The proof is the Prophet's statement: 'Let those of you who are of understanding and intelligence be near me.' 'Lil' is a command form derived from 'waliy' meaning nearness. 'Ahlam' is the plural of 'hilm' meaning intelligence, and 'nuhu' is plural of 'nuha' meaning intellect. Now the hadith's meaning is that those who are mature and intelligent should be near me. But if someone says: This hadith establishes the priority of men over boys, but it does not establish the priority of boys over women. The answer to that is that boys are subordinate to men due to masculinity, and the subordinate comes after the principal; therefore boys will come after men and before women. Another answer is that the priority of boys over women is established by the Prophet's action, because he placed a woman behind an adult named Yatim? A better proof is the hadith narrated by Imam Ahmad in his Musnad from Abu Malik al-Ash'ari. The words of the narration are: 'He said: O assembly of Ash'aris, gather and gather your women and children so that I may show you the prayer of the Messenger of Allah. So they gathered and gathered their children and women, then he performed wudu and showed them how he performed wudu, then he stepped forward and arranged the men in the front row, and the boys behind them, and the women behind the boys.' That is, Abu Malik al-Ash'ari said: O people of the Ash'ari tribe, gather yourselves and gather your women and children so that I may show you the prayer of the Messenger of Allah. So they gathered and gathered their sons and women, then he performed wudu and showed them how he performed wudu. Then Abu Malik went forward and arranged the men's row, and the boys behind them, and the women's row behind the boys. The rational proof is that alignment of a woman with a man invalidates the prayer, so women are delayed.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the preferred order of rows (sufuf) in congregational prayer. It states that the rows should be arranged with men first (closest to the imam), then boys (children), and then women at the back. Two proofs are given: a hadith and a rational argument. The hadith is: 'Let those of you who are of understanding and intelligence be near me' (لِيَلِنِي مِنْكُمْ أُولُو الْأَحْلَامِ وَالنُّهَى). This hadith from Sahih Muslim instructs that mature, intelligent men should occupy the first rows. Since boys are not fully mature, they come after men. A potential objection is raised: this hadith only prioritizes men over boys, but does not explicitly place boys before women. The commentator answers that boys are subordinate to men due to masculinity (rajuliyya), so they come after men but before women, as subordinates follow their principals. Additionally, the Prophet's practice (fi'l) is cited: he once placed a woman behind a man named Yatim, implying that men are before women. A stronger proof is the hadith of Abu Malik al-Ash'ari (narrated by Imam Ahmad) in which he arranged the rows exactly as described: men in front, then boys, then women. The rational proof ('aql) is that a woman aligning (muhadhat) with a man in the same prayer invalidates the man's prayer. Therefore, women are placed behind to avoid this, and since boys are less likely to cause fitna, they are placed before women. This order ensures that the prayer is valid and follows the sunna.

Key Terms
محاذات (muhadhat): The alignment of a man and a woman in the same row during prayer, which is considered mufsid (invalidating) for the man's prayer if the imam intended to lead the woman.
صف (saff): A row in congregational prayer. The order of rows is prescribed to maintain discipline and avoid invalidation.
اولو الاحلام والنهي (ulu al-ahlam wa al-nuha): Those who possess understanding and intellect, i.e., mature, intelligent men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main rational reason given for placing women behind boys in prayer rows?
A) Women are less capable of praying correctly.
B) Alignment (muhadhat) of a woman with a man invalidates the man's prayer.
C) Women must be as far back as possible to avoid distraction.
D) Boys are stronger than women in prayer.

Key Takeaway
The order of rows (men, then boys, then women) is a confirmed sunna based on both hadith and rational reasoning to prevent invalidation of prayer.

Ruling on Muhadhat (Alignment of a Woman with a Man in Prayer)
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on muhadhat, explain the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas, and distinguish the Hanafi view from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
A woman aligning with a man in the same prayer invalidates only the man's prayer, based on istihsan from a hadith.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in congregational prayer: when a woman stands exactly in line with a man (muhadhat). The Hanafi school rules that the man's prayer becomes invalid, while the woman's remains valid. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) overriding qiyas. Understanding this requires exploring the proof (hadith), the analogy with a muqtadi moving ahead of the imam, and the opposing Shafi'i view based on pure analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the alignment (muhadhat) of a woman with a man during the same prayer. The ruling: the man's prayer becomes invalid (fasid) if the imam intended to lead that woman.
Note the condition: the imam must have intended to lead the woman for the ruling to apply.
2
Locate the qiyas objection
What does qiyas (analogy) suggest? Since alignment is an act involving both parties, and the woman's prayer is not invalidated by consensus, the man's prayer should also not be invalidated. This is the Shafi'i position.
Imam al-Shafi'i uses qiyas on the woman's prayer.
3
Understand the istihsan basis
Why does Hanafi override qiyas? The text cites a famous hadith (مارويناه) as the basis for istihsan. The exact wording is not given, but it is relied upon as a stronger proof.
Istihsan is a source of law in Hanafi usul, used when a stronger dalil (here a hadith) indicates a different ruling.
4
Analyze the analogy with muqtadi
The Hanafi response further explains that the man is the addressee of the command to maintain position, not the woman. Therefore, when alignment occurs, the man is the one leaving the prescribed position, analogous to a muqtadi stepping ahead of the imam, which invalidates his prayer but not the imam's.
This analogy clarifies why only the man's prayer is affected.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
What is the practical difference? Under Hanafi, if alignment occurs with the imam's intention, the man must repeat his prayer. Under Shafi'i, both prayers are valid.
This difference has real implications in congregation settings.

وان حاذته امرأة وهما مشتركان فى صلوة واحدة، فسدت صلاته ان نوى الامام امامتها والقياس ان لا تفسد وهو قول الشافعى رحمة الله تعالى عليه اعتبارا بصلاتها حيث لاتفسد وجه الاستحسان مارويناه و انه من المشاهير وهو المخاطب به دونها فيكون هو التارك لفرض المقام فتفسد صلاته دون صلاتها كالمأموم اذا تقدم على الامام
ترجمہ اور اگر کوئی عورت مرد سے محاذی ہوگی اور حال یہ ہے کہ دونوں ایک نماز میں شریک ہیں تو مرد کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی بشرطیکہ امام نے اس عورت کی امامت کی نیت کی ہو اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ مرد کی نماز فاسد نہ ہو اور یہی امام شافعی کا قول ہے عورت کی نماز پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے کیونکہ عورت کی نماز فاسد نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور وجہ استحسان وہ حدیث ہے جو ہم روایت کر چکے ۔ اور حدیث احادیث مشہورہ میں سے ہے اور مرد ہی اس حکم کا مخاطب ہے نہ کہ عورت پس مرد ہی مقام مفروض کا ترک کرنے والا ہوگا لہذا اسی کی نماز فاسد ہوگی نہ کہ عورت کی نماز جیسے مقتدی جب وہ امام سے آگے ہو جائے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی عورت کسی مرد سے محاذی ہوگئی در انحالیکہ مرد اور عورت دونوں ایک نماز میں مشترک ہیں اور امام نے اس عورت کی امامت کی نیت بھی کی ہے تو ایسی صورت میں مرد کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ اور قیاس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ مرد کی نماز بھی فاسد نہ ہو۔ اور یہی امام شافعی کا قول ہے۔ امام شافعی نے مرد کی نماز کو عورت کی نماز پر قیاس کیا ہے یعنی محاذات کی وجہ سے عورت کی نماز بالاتفاق فاسد نہیں ہوئی لہذا مرد کی نماز بھی فاسد نہ ہوگی اور قیاس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ محاذات ایسا فعل ہے کہ جانبہین سے محقق ہوتا ہے پس
Issue of Alignment (Muhadhat): And if a woman aligns with a man while both are participating in one prayer, his prayer becomes invalid if the imam intended to lead her. The qiyas is that it should not become invalid, and this is the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), taking into consideration her prayer because it does not become invalid. The basis of istihsan is the hadith we have narrated, and it is among the famous hadiths. And he (the man) is the addressee of this ruling, not the woman, so he is the one leaving the prescribed position; therefore his prayer becomes invalid, not the woman's, like the muqtadi when he moves ahead of the imam. Translation: And if a woman aligns with a man and the situation is that both are sharing in one prayer, then the man's prayer becomes invalid provided that the imam intended to lead that woman. And the qiyas is that the man's prayer should not become invalid, and this is the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i, analogizing to the woman's prayer because her prayer does not become invalid. The basis of istihsan is the hadith we have narrated, and it is among the famous hadiths. And the man is the addressee of this ruling, not the woman. So the man is the one leaving the prescribed position, therefore his prayer becomes invalid, not the woman's, like the muqtadi when he moves ahead of the imam. Commentary: The scenario is that if a woman aligns with a man while both are sharing in one prayer and the imam has also intended to lead that woman, then in such a situation the man's prayer becomes invalid. And qiyas requires that the man's prayer also not become invalid. And this is the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i. Imam al-Shafi'i analogized the man's prayer to the woman's prayer, i.e., because the woman's prayer by consensus does not become invalid due to alignment, therefore the man's prayer should also not become invalid. And the basis of qiyas is that alignment is an act that is actualized from both sides.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of muhadhat, i.e., when a woman stands exactly in line with a man during the same prayer. The Hanafi ruling, based on istihsan, is that the man's prayer becomes invalid (fasid) if the imam intended to lead that woman (i.e., he had her in his intention when beginning the prayer or during it). The woman's prayer remains valid. The text then contrasts this with qiyas (analogy), which would suggest that the man's prayer should also remain valid, just as the woman's does, because the alignment is an action involving both parties. This qiyas view is held by Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi response is two-fold: (1) A famous hadith (likely referring to the hadith that a woman's alignment invalidates the man's prayer, though the exact hadith is not quoted here) supports the view of invalidation. (2) The man is the addressee of the command to maintain proper positioning (he is commanded to be aware of his surroundings and avoid alignment), not the woman. Therefore, if alignment occurs, the man is the one who has committed the violation by not maintaining his position, analogous to a muqtadi (follower) stepping ahead of the imam, which invalidates the muqtadi's prayer but not the imam's. Thus, the man's prayer is invalidated, while the woman's remains intact. This ruling is based on the principle of istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas.

Key Terms
محاذات (muhadhat): The alignment of a man and a woman in the same prayer row, leading to invalidation of the man's prayer under Hanafi.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas when a stronger proof (e.g., hadith) indicates a different ruling.
نوى الامام امامتها (nawa al-imam imamataha): The imam intended to lead that specific woman in prayer, making the ruling of muhadhat applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, why does only the man's prayer become invalid when a woman aligns with him?
A) Because the woman is not commanded to avoid alignment.
B) Because the man is the one commanded to maintain proper position and he neglected it.
C) Because the man's prayer is inherently weaker.
D) Because the hadith specifically mentions men only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on muhadhat is that the man's prayer becomes invalid due to his violation of the command, based on istihsan from a hadith, not on qiyas.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Ruling of Muhadhat: Asymmetry in Salah Validity
Establishes that muhadhat invalidates the man's prayer, not the woman's, with proof and objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on muhadhat, explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, and distinguish why the man's prayer is invalidated but not the woman's.

Core Idea
The man's prayer is invalidated by muhadhat because he alone is addressed by the command to keep women behind.

In congregational prayer, the positioning of women relative to men is a matter of legal consequence. This lesson examines the specific case where a woman stands exactly in line with a man (muhadhat). The Hanafi school holds that this invalidates the man's prayer but not the woman's, departing from a simple analogy. We will explore the textual proof and the juristic reasoning behind this asymmetry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the exact ruling: muhadhat invalidates the man's prayer, not the woman's.
Note that this is specific to the Hanafi school.
2
Examine the dalil
Locate the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and understand its command: 'Akhkhiruhunna' (put them behind). Determine whom the command addresses.
The command is directed at men, not women.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the imperative indicates obligation (wujub) per Hanafi usul, and why abandoning this obligation invalidates the man's prayer.
This is a fard obligation due to the mashhoor nature of the hadith.
4
Address the qiyas objection
Understand the apparent qiyas: if muhadhat doesn't affect the woman's prayer, why should it affect the man's? Then see how istihsan overrides this qiyas.
Also note the analogy with a follower moving ahead of the imam.
5
Defend the hadith's authority
Respond to the objection that the hadith is khabar wahid: it is actually mashhoor, capable of establishing a fard obligation.
Mashhoor hadiths are considered qati al-dalala in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الامامة
جب محاذات عورت کی نماز کے لئے مفسد نہیں ہے تو مرد کی نماز کے لئے بھی مفسد نہیں ہوگا۔ وجہ استحسان وہ حدیث ہے جو ہم سابق شرط نہیں ہے اس۔ روایت کر چکے۔ عبداللہ بن مسعود کی حدیث ان رسول الله قال اخر وهن من حيث اخر من الله، اس حدیث میں مردوں پھر واضح ہوکہ دیا گیا کہ وہ عورتوں کو نماز میں پیچھے رکھیں پس جب عورت اس کے محاذی ہوگئی تو گویا مرد نے اپنا فرض مقام ترک کر دیا کیونکہ ایسی نماز بھی مرد اس امام کی جس کے اندر دونوں شریک ہوں عورت کو مؤخر کرنا مرد پر فرض ہے۔ اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ جس نے فرض ترک کیا اس کی نماز کے لئے عورت کے ہو جائے گی نہ کہ دوسرے کی، اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ محاذات کی وجہ سے مرد کی نماز فاسد ہوگی نہ عورت کی۔ کہ حدیث اخر
اور اگر یہ اعتراض کیا جائے کہ یہ خبر واحد ہے اور خبر واحد سے فرضیت ثابت نہیں ہوتی تو اس کا جواب صاحب ہدایہ نے ان شخص پر کوئی چیز لالہ المشاهير کہ کر دیا ہے یعنی یہ حدیث احادیث مشہورہ میں ہے جو قطعی الدلالت ہوتی ہے اور حدیث مشہور سے فرضیت ثابت مقتدی کا اقتداء کر ہو جاتی ہے لہذا اب کوئی اعتراض نہیں ہوگا۔ نے نماز میں نقص و وهو المخاطب سے قیاس کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ عورت کی نماز فاسد نہ ہونے سے مرد کی نماز فاسد نہ ہونالازمی نیت کرنا شرط ہے۔ آتا۔ کیونکہ حضور ہے کے قول اخر و ھن کا مخاطب مرد ہے نہ کہ عورت پس تارک فرض مرد ہوا نہ کہ عورت اس لئے صرف مرد کی نماز بار شمس الائمہ الہ ہو گی عورت کی نماز فاسد نہیں ہو گی۔ جیسے مقتدی جب وہ امام سے آگے ہو جائے اور اپنا فرض مقام چھوڑ دے تو تو اس کی نماز فاسد ہوجہ اقتداء صحیح قرار دید گی۔ اسی طرح جب عورت کے ساتھ اپنا فرض مقام چھوڑے گا تو اس کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ فوائد محاذات مفسدہ یہ ہے کہ نماز کے اندر عورت کا قدم مرد کے کسی عضو کے محاذی اور مقابل ہو جائے۔
Chapter of Imamate. When a woman's muhadhat is not invalidating for her own prayer, then it is also not invalidating for the man's prayer. The basis of istihsan is the hadith we have narrated earlier from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'The Messenger of God said: Put them (women) where God has put them (behind).' In this hadith, men are commanded to place women behind in prayer. So when a woman becomes in line with him (the man), it is as if the man has abandoned his obligatory position, because the obligation upon the man is to keep the woman behind, especially in a prayer where both are sharing in following the same imam. And it is agreed that whoever abandons an obligation, his prayer is invalidated, not another's. Therefore we say: muhadhat invalidates the man's prayer but not the woman's. And if one objects: this is a khabar wahid, and a khabar wahid does not establish an obligation, then the answer given by the author of Hidayah is that this hadith is among the mashhoor hadiths which are definitive in meaning, and obligation can be established by a mashhoor hadith, so no objection remains. The answer to the qiyas (analogy) is that the command 'akhkhiruhunna' is addressed to men, not women, so the one abandoning the obligation is the man, not the woman. Therefore only the man's prayer becomes invalid, not the woman's. Just as when a follower moves ahead of the imam and leaves his obligatory position, his prayer becomes invalid even though his following remains valid. Similarly, when he leaves his position due to a woman, his prayer becomes invalid. The specifics of invalidating muhadhat: the woman's foot comes in line with any part of the man's body during prayer.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the effect of a woman standing alongside a man in congregational prayer. The author, commenting on the Hidayah, clarifies that muhadhat (the woman being exactly in line with the man) invalidates the man's prayer but not the woman's. The apparent qiyas might suggest that since it does not affect the woman's prayer, it should not affect the man's either. However, istihsan (juristic preference) departs from qiyas based on a hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, where the Prophet ﷺ commanded men to place women behind them. This establishes an obligation (fard) upon the man to not have a woman in line with him. If he neglects this obligation, his prayer becomes invalid. The woman is not addressed by this command, so her prayer remains valid. The author also addresses an objection that the hadith is khabar wahid, which typically does not establish an obligation in Hanafi usul. He responds that this particular hadith is mashhoor (well-known) and thus carries stronger authority, able to establish an obligation. An analogy is drawn to a follower who moves ahead of the imam—his prayer invalidates despite his following being valid. Thus, the man's prayer solely is affected by muhadhat.

Key Terms
محاذات (muhādhat): A woman standing exactly in line with a man (her foot alongside any part of his body) during prayer.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that departs from the strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a stronger evidence or public interest. Here, it overrides the qiyas that muhadhat does not affect either party.
خبر واحد (khabar wāḥid): A hadith narrated by one or few companions, considered zanni al-thubut. The objector claimed this hadith is khabar wahid and thus cannot establish a fard obligation.
حدیث مشہور (ḥadīth mashhūr): A hadith narrated by at least two companions or widely known among early scholars, considered qati al-dalala (definitive in meaning) and capable of establishing fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school rule that muhadhat invalidates the man's prayer but not the woman's?
A) Because the woman's prayer is always more valid.
B) Because the hadith command 'akhkhiruhunna' is addressed to men, making them the ones who abandon a fard.
C) Because qiyas dictates that only the man's prayer is affected.
D) Because the hadith is weak and cannot apply to women.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on muhadhat is asymmetric: the man's prayer is invalidated because he alone is commanded to keep women behind, while the woman's prayer remains valid.
